## User (2026-04-20 12:47:52)

We are trying to prove the Riemann Hypothesis. A paper draft is attached.

## Your Task: Source-level two-point theorem

Please work only on the **two-point/source-level theorem** in the attached paper draft. Do **not** spend time on the (3)-point or (4)-point branch unless it is strictly needed for this theorem.

### Objective

Try to close the remaining **source-level two-point theorem** that would force the quadratic interaction factorization
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2,
]
or an equivalent corrected quotient-germ / corrected interaction-remainder statement that gives the same consequence.

I want you to focus on the exact missing source-level structure, not on document cleanup.

### Current state to assume

From the draft, the broad situation is:

* the two-point branch is expected to be settled by a **source-level corrected interaction remainder** or equivalent corrected quotient-germ map;
* the target structure should encode:

  * the right **swap symmetry**,
  * **one-amplitude collapse**,
  * **diagonal collapse**,
  * and the resulting **quadratic ((h_1-h_2)^2)** factor;
* the theorem is expected to rule out the remaining two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches once the factorization is in hand.

### Your job

Please do all of the following:

1. **Locate the exact source-level theorem statement the draft is implicitly aiming at.**
   Rewrite it in the cleanest possible form, ideally as one theorem or proposition.

2. **Audit what is already proved versus missing.**
   Be precise:

   * which identities are already in the draft,
   * which reductions are already valid,
   * which one or two lemmas are actually still open.

3. **Try to prove the missing theorem.**
   If you cannot fully prove it, reduce it as far as possible to a minimal finite list of concrete source identities.

4. **Prefer exact structural formulas over heuristics.**
   I care most about:
   * corrected quotient-germ maps,
   * corrected interaction remainder,
   * symmetry identities,
   * vanishing/collapse identities,
   * factorization mechanisms.

### Routes to attack

Please prioritize these attack routes:

#### Route A: corrected interaction remainder theorem

Try to formulate the exact corrected two-point remainder (\mathcal I_2) or equivalent object whose properties imply
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2.
]
Then prove:

* swap symmetry,
* one-amplitude collapse,
* diagonal collapse,
* quadratic divisibility.

#### Route B: quotient-germ transport

If the draft is really using a corrected quotient-germ picture, identify the precise map and prove the needed functorial/symmetry/collapse properties there instead of at the scalar remainder level.

#### Route C: minimal finite reduction

If full closure is too hard, reduce the theorem to the smallest possible list of explicit source-level identities. I want exact missing identities, not broad commentary.

### Non-goals

Do **not** spend time on:
* the mixed (4)-point branch,
* the nonmixed (4)-point branch,
* the centered (v_5/u_5)-patch dichotomy,
(these will be worked on in other chats)

I’ve isolated the pressure point: the draft already proves the downstream consequence once a source-level object exists, but it never actually constructs the source-level map. So the real target is not another estimate; it is an existence-and-functoriality theorem for the two-atom corrected coefficients themselves.

_Thought for 14m 9s_

I worked only on the two-point/source-level issue.

The main conclusion is that the draft is already very close to the correct formal reduction, but the real missing theorem is slightly sharper than the current “conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder” proposition. In particular, the current proposition is under-assumed: its proof uses two source-level properties that are not actually stated.

What the draft is really aiming at

For the two-point branch alone, the cleanest target is not an abstract quotient-germ map first, but a source-level fixed-sector coefficient package through order \(7\):
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
=
\bigl(C[\mu],A_5[\mu],A_7[\mu]\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f,
\]
defined for small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
such that for a one-atom source,
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)
=
\bigl(a\,c(h),\,a\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\,a\,A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]

Then for two atoms define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1})
-\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]

The exact theorem the draft wants is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
}
\]
for an analytic
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})\to \mathbf C\oplus\mathfrak f\oplus\mathfrak f.
\]

This is enough. It is stronger and cleaner than the current architectural definition of a pair-interaction germ, and it is weaker than building a full abstract quotient-germ target \(\mathcal G\). For the two-point branch, the coefficient package \((C,A_5,A_7)\) already suffices.

An equivalent corrected-remainder formulation

There is an even cleaner formal statement which is the actual divisibility engine.

Let \(\mathcal G\) be any finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in\mathcal G
\]
be analytic near the diagonal. Assume:

\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)
\]
(swap symmetry),

\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0
\]
(one-amplitude collapse),

and
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0
\]
(diagonal collapse).

Then there exists an analytic \(\mathcal J_2\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
}
\]

Proof: by the amplitude-axis vanishing and analyticity,
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for analytic \(G\). Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
Set
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right).
\]
Then \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is even in \(s\). Diagonal collapse gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
So \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is divisible by \(s^2\), hence
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
with analytic \(H\). Returning to \((h_1,h_2)\) gives the factorization.

That part is done.

What is already proved in the draft

The downstream side is already in place.

The draft already proves the exact coincidence bridge through the strengthened data \(\widehat\Psi\) in Theorem \(\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}\). It already proves defect-scale closeness on good patches in Corollary \(\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}\). And it already proves that sublinear total defect is impossible on compact good patches in Proposition \(\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch}\).

So once you get
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
=
O\!\left((h_1-h_2)^2\right),
\]
the two-point branch is over.

The draft also already isolates the intended source-level mechanism in Proposition \(\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}\) and Corollary \(\ref{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}\).

What is missing or slightly wrong

The current conditional proposition is not quite correct as stated.

Its proof uses two extra source-level facts that are not assumed:

First, from
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0
\]
the proof is implicitly using
\[
\mathfrak Q(0)=0.
\]

Second, from
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0
\]
the proof is implicitly using same-support additivity:
\[
\mathfrak Q\bigl((a_1+a_2)\delta_h\bigr)
=
\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_h)+\mathfrak Q(a_2\delta_h).
\]
Equivalently, along a one-point source ray,
\[
\mathfrak Q(a\delta_h)
\]
must be linear in \(a\).

Without those two properties, the proof of diagonal collapse does not go through.

So the exact source-level theorem is not merely “there exists an analytic map on atomic sources.” It is:

there exists an analytic source-defined package, normalized at zero, and additive on coincident atoms.

That is the real missing source structure.

What the open part reduces to

After separating the formal divisibility lemma from the genuine source construction, the remaining source-level closure collapses to one substantive theorem and one almost-tautological projection step.

The substantive theorem is:

there exists a source-defined order-\(\le 7\) corrected fixed-sector package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(\mu)
=
\bigl(C[\mu],A_5[\mu],A_7[\mu]\bigr)
\]
for finite atomic sources, depending only on the source \(\mu\), with
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(0)=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{\le7}((a+b)\delta_h)=\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)+\mathfrak P_{\le7}(b\delta_h),
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)
=
\bigl(a\,c(h),\,a\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\,a\,A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]

Then the two-point interaction remainder automatically has:

\[
\text{swap symmetry,}
\qquad
\text{one-amplitude collapse,}
\qquad
\text{diagonal collapse.}
\]

And then the quadratic factor follows formally.

The second step is only to note that the present two-pair defects are linear projections of this remainder:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\Pi_3(\mathcal I_2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=\Pi_5(\mathcal I_2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=\bar\Pi_7(\mathcal I_2).
\]
If you build \(\mathfrak P_{\le7}\) directly in
\[
\mathbf C\oplus\mathfrak f\oplus\mathfrak f,
\]
these projections are immediate.

So in my judgment, only one genuinely nontrivial lemma remains:

the source-presentation / coincident-atom additivity theorem for the order-\(\le 7\) corrected fixed-sector package.

Minimal finite reduction

If you want the smallest concrete identity list, it is this.

For each of
\[
X\in\{C,\ A_5,\ A_7\},
\]
define the two-point source coefficient
\[
X_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=X[a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}],
\]
and the one-point coefficient
\[
X_1(a,h):=X[a\delta_h].
\]

It is enough to prove:

\[
X_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=X_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]

\[
X_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=X_1(a_2,h_2),
\qquad
X_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=X_1(a_1,h_1),
\]

\[
X_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=X_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]

and
\[
X_1(a_1+a_2,h)=X_1(a_1,h)+X_1(a_2,h).
\]

Then the remainder
\[
I_X:=X_2-X_1(a_1,h_1)-X_1(a_2,h_2)
\]
satisfies
\[
I_X=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_X.
\]

You do not need any extra first-derivative identity on the diagonal. Symmetry kills the linear separation term automatically.

My best attempt at an actual proof route from the current machinery

The most plausible way to close this from the existing draft is not to start at the quotient level. It is to source-ize the corrected block construction before whitening.

The draft already has the analytic whitening map
\[
(G_-,N,G_+)\longmapsto G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}
\]
and already extracts the relevant order-\(3,5,7\) fixed-sector data from the whitened block.

So the natural source theorem to prove is:

for each finite atomic source \(\mu\), there are corrected source blocks
\[
G^{\corr}_{\mu,-},\quad N^{\corr}_{\mu},\quad G^{\corr}_{\mu,+}
\]
such that:

they depend only on \(\mu\), not on a presentation of \(\mu\) as an ordered list of atoms;

they are analytic in the finite source parameters;

for a single atom \(a\delta_h\), they reproduce the current one-pair corrected blocks with amplitude \(a\);

and when two atoms collide,
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
the corrected source blocks collapse to the one-atom blocks with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\).

Once those pre-whitened source blocks exist, the rest is automatic:
apply whitening, then fixed-sector projection, then extract \((C,A_5,A_7)\).

So the theorem is not blocked by any new two-point asymptotic estimate. It is blocked by source-functoriality of the corrected block package.

Bottom line

The source-level two-point problem is now very sharp.

The formal divisibility theorem is done.

The draft’s current conditional proposition should be corrected, because it silently uses
\[
\mathfrak Q(0)=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathfrak Q((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_h)+\mathfrak Q(a_2\delta_h).
\]

The actual open theorem is:

construct the order-\(\le7\) corrected fixed-sector package as a genuine analytic function of the finite atomic source itself, with zero-source normalization and coincident-atom additivity.

Once that is in hand, the quadratic factor
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
follows formally, and the existing defect-scale-close machinery excludes the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

If you want, I can next turn this into a precise replacement theorem/proposition package for the paper, with exact hypotheses and proof text.

_Thought for 10m 5s_

Yes — here is the cleanest attack I can honestly justify from the current draft.

The first thing to sharpen is the target itself. For the two-point branch, you do **not** need a full source-level map on arbitrary finite atomic sources. That is overkill. What you actually need is only a **two-atom source theorem**.

The right theorem

Let \(F_h\) denote the corrected one-pair odd germ, and let
\[
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
denote the corrected two-atom odd germ through the finite-order package actually used downstream, namely cubic, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient class. Define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

Then the exact source-level theorem you want is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
}
\]
for an analytic \(\mathcal J_2\).

A sufficient hypothesis set is much smaller than the current conditional proposition:

\[
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak Q_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak Q_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\qquad
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
and the merger identity
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
}
\]

That is the real missing theorem. Nothing broader is needed for the two-point branch.

What is already done

The downstream geometry is already in place.

Definition \(\ref{def:two-pair-decomposition}\) already gives a two-pair object and already isolates the interaction germ \(\mathcal I_{12}\) as quadratic in the amplitudes.

Theorem \(\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}\) already shows that if the cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are \(O(\delta^2)\), with \(\delta=|h_1-h_2|\), then the strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi(h)\) is also \(O(\delta^2)\)-close.

Corollary \(\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}\) and Proposition \(\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch}\) already exclude the two-point bad-core branch once those defects are sublinear, and in particular once they are quadratic.

So the whole two-point branch is already reduced to forcing
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

What is not yet done

The current Proposition \(\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}\) is very close, but it is not quite the right theorem.

First, it assumes a full finite-source map \(\mathfrak Q\), which is stronger than necessary.

Second, its proof silently uses two facts not stated as hypotheses:

\[
\mathfrak Q(0)=0,
\]
and, more importantly,
\[
\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)=\mathfrak Q((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]

That second identity is the real issue. It is the source-level merger/collision property.

Once that is stated, the proof is easy.

The sharp reduction

For the two-point theorem, everything reduces to one open lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Q_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
}
\]

Swap symmetry and one-amplitude collapse are already built into the intended architecture. The merger identity is the only substantive missing source-level structure.

Why that one lemma is enough

Assume the three identities above. Then
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0,
\]
so analyticity gives
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(G\).

Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]

The merger identity gives
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Now set
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right).
\]
Then \(\widetilde G\) is even in \(s\), and \(\widetilde G(m,0)=0\). Hence
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Returning to \((h_1,h_2)\),
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

So the theorem is finished once merger is proved.

The finite-order version you actually need

Even that merger identity can be weakened. You do not need full germ equality. Since the downstream two-point branch only uses cubic, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient class, it is enough to prove merger through those three layers.

Write the two-atom corrected package as
\[
c_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),\qquad
A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),\qquad
[A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}](a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]

Then it is enough to prove:

\[
c_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)c(h),
\]
\[
A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]
\[
[A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}](a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h).
\]

Together with swap symmetry and one-amplitude collapse, those three identities already imply
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_3,
\quad
E_{12}^{(5)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_5,
\quad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_7,
\]
hence the desired \(O(\delta^2)\) bounds after normalization.

So the minimal finite reduction is now extremely small: three merger identities, one at each relevant order.

Where I pushed and where I got stuck

I tried to get the merger identity directly from the current text. I do not see a proof of it from the draft as written.

The reason is structural: the draft already has the one-pair object \(F_h\), and it already has the two-pair decomposition, but it does **not** yet define the corrected package as a function on the commutative source semigroup of atomic data. Without that, coincident-atom merger is not a theorem you can even state internally except as an extra axiom.

So the present bottleneck is not another transport estimate. It is not an order-7 computation. It is not anything on the three- or four-point side. It is exactly this:

can the corrected two-atom package be shown to depend only on the underlying two-atom source, modulo identification
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h?
\]

My best exact formulation of the open lemma

Here is the version I would try to prove next.

**Two-atom source well-definedness through order 7.**  
There exist analytic maps
\[
\mathfrak C_2,\ \mathfrak A_{5,2},\ \mathfrak A_{7,2}
\]
defined for small \((a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)\), taking values in
\[
\mathbf C,\qquad \mathfrak f,\qquad \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
such that:

\[
\mathfrak C_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak C_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
and similarly for \(\mathfrak A_{5,2},\mathfrak A_{7,2}\);

\[
\mathfrak C_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2c(h_2),

\mathfrak A_{5,2}(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_2),

\mathfrak C_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)c(h),

\]
\[
\mathfrak A_{7,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h).
\]

Then the remainder maps
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}:=\mathfrak C_2-a_1c(h_1)-a_2c(h_2),
\]
\[
\mathcal E^{(5)}:=\mathfrak A_{5,2}-a_1A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_1)-a_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_2),

\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}:=\mathfrak A_{7,2}-a_1[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h_1)-a_2[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h_2)
\]
all factor as
\[
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\times(\text{analytic}).
\]

That is the theorem I think the draft is really trying to reach.

Here is the theorem.

## The source-level two-point theorem

Fix the same corrected local formulas already used in the draft for the same-point and mixed blocks. For a finite atomic source
\[
\mu=\sum_{r=1}^N a_r\delta_{h_r},
\]
define the source-summed phase fields by
\[
q_\mu(t):=\sum_{r=1}^N a_r\,q_{h_r}(t),
\qquad
\Phi_\mu(t):=\sum_{r=1}^N a_r\,\Phi_{h_r}(t),
\]
and
\[
\Delta_{\mu,m}(s):=\Phi_\mu\!\left(m-\frac s2\right)-\Phi_\mu\!\left(m+\frac s2\right).
\]

Now substitute \(q_\mu,\Delta_{\mu,m}\) into the already-written corrected block formulas:
\[
G_{\mu,m,\pm}^{\corr}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2q_\mu(t_\pm) & \frac12 q_\mu'(t_\pm)\\[.6ex]
\frac12 q_\mu'(t_\pm) &
\frac1{12}\bigl(q_\mu''(t_\pm)+2q_\mu(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
t_\pm=m\pm \frac s2,
\]
and
\[
N_{\mu,m}^{\corr}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
-\dfrac{2\sin\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)}{s}
&
\dfrac{\sin\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)+q_\mu(t_+)s\cos\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
-\dfrac{\sin\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)+q_\mu(t_-)s\cos\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)}{s^2}
&
\dfrac{(q_\mu(t_-)+q_\mu(t_+))s\cos\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)+(2-q_\mu(t_-)q_\mu(t_+)s^2)\sin\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Whiten exactly as before:
\[
\widehat\Omega_{\mu,m}^{\corr}(s)
=
G_{\mu,m,-}^{\corr}(s)^{-1/2}
\,N_{\mu,m}^{\corr}(s)\,
G_{\mu,m,+}^{\corr}(s)^{-1/2}.
\]

Let its odd Taylor expansion be
\[
\widehat\Omega_{\mu,m}^{\corr}(s)\sim
B_{3,\mu}(m)s^3+B_{5,\mu}(m)s^5+B_{7,\mu}(m)s^7+\cdots.
\]
Project to the fixed sector:
\[
A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}:=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(B_{5,\mu}),
\qquad
A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}:=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(B_{7,\mu}),
\]
and let \(c_\mu\) be the cubic scalar/channel already denoted \(c(h)\) in the one-pair case. Define the source-level finite-order package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu):=
\bigl(c_\mu,\ A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},\ A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f.
\]

Then:

1. \(\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)\) is analytic in the atomic parameters and depends only on the source \(\mu\), not on an ordering/presentation of its atoms.

2. For every \(h\), the one-atom ray is linear:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h).
\]
Write
\[
F_h:=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]

3. For two atoms,
\[
\mu_{12}:=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu_{12})-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}
\]
satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
}
\]
for an analytic
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})\to
\mathbf C\oplus\mathfrak f\oplus\mathfrak f.
\]

4. Applying linear extraction/projection maps gives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_3,
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_5,
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_7,
\]
hence on compacta
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)} = O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

That is exactly the missing source-level two-point theorem.

## Proof

The proof has one genuinely structural step and then a short divisibility argument.

### 1. The corrected finite-order package is source-defined

The formulas for \(G^{\corr}\) and \(N^{\corr}\) depend only on:
\[
q_\mu(t_\pm),\ q_\mu'(t_\pm),\ q_\mu''(t_\pm),\ \Delta_{\mu,m}(s),
\]
and on the elementary analytic operations appearing in those explicit formulas.

But \(q_\mu\) and \(\Phi_\mu\) are linear in \(\mu\). So if two atomic presentations define the same source \(\mu\), they give exactly the same \(q_\mu\), \(\Phi_\mu\), \(\Delta_{\mu,m}\), hence the same corrected same-point blocks and corrected mixed block. Whitening is an analytic function of those blocks on the positive-definite region, so it too depends only on \(\mu\). Therefore every odd coefficient \(B_{2k+1,\mu}\), and hence
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)=\bigl(c_\mu,A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr),
\]
depends only on \(\mu\).

So the finite-order corrected package is genuinely source-level.

### 2. Swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, diagonal merger

For two atoms,
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}.
\]
Since this source is unchanged by swapping the two atoms,
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}).
\]
That is the exact source-level swap symmetry.

If one amplitude is zero,
\[
a_1=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mu_{12}=a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
so
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu_{12})=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}),
\]
and similarly with \(a_2=0\). That is one-amplitude collapse.

If \(h_1=h_2=h\), then as atomic sources
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]
Because \(\mathfrak P_{\le 7}\) is source-defined,
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]
That is the exact diagonal merger identity.

This is the source-level statement the draft was missing.

### 3. Linearity on one-atom rays

Fix \(h\), and write
\[
Q_h(a):=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h).
\]
By the diagonal merger identity,
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2).
\]
Also \(Q_h(0)=0\). Since \(Q_h\) is analytic in \(a\), the additive Cauchy equation forces linearity:
\[
Q_h(a)=a\,Q_h(1).
\]
Define
\[
F_h:=Q_h(1)=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h).
\]
Then
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h.
\]

So the draft’s intended decomposition
\[
\text{(two-atom object)} = a_1F_{h_1}+a_2F_{h_2}+(\text{interaction})
\]
is not an extra axiom. It follows from source-definedness plus diagonal merger.

### 4. Quadratic factorization of the interaction remainder

Now define
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

By one-amplitude collapse,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Since \(\mathcal I_2\) is analytic, it is divisible by \(a_1a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic \(G\).

By swap symmetry,
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]

By diagonal merger and one-atom linearity,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0.
\]
Hence
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right).
\]
Swap symmetry makes \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) even in \(s\), and diagonal vanishing gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
An even analytic function vanishing at \(s=0\) is divisible by \(s^2\). So
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Returning to \((h_1,h_2)\),
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]

That proves the source-level two-point factorization.

### 5. Passage to the draft’s defects

The cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector coefficient, and septic fixed-sector coefficient are linear coefficient-extraction maps from the order-\(\le7\) odd germ. Therefore each extracted interaction defect inherits the same factorization:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_3,
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_5,
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(7),\mathfrak f}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_7.
\]
Projecting the third line to the quotient
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}
\]
gives
\[
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\overline J_7.
\]

So on compact families,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

Then the draft’s existing quantitative two-pair bridge and the good-patch exclusion result finish the two-point bad-core branch.

## What this does and does not close

This closes the source-level two-point theorem at the level actually needed downstream:
\[
(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\quad\text{through order }7.
\]

It does **not** by itself construct a full abstract \(\Qabs\)-valued source map to all orders. But that is not needed for the current two-point branch. The order-\(\le7\) corrected source package already gives the exact quadratic interaction factorization the draft was trying to isolate.

So the real gap was smaller than it looked. The missing step was to source-define the corrected finite-order block using the already-written formulas, then use atomic-source merger. Once that is written down, the quadratic \((h_1-h_2)^2\) factor is forced.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Two-pair decomposition]
\label{def:two-pair-decomposition}
For a normalized two-pair core with amplitudes $a_1,a_2$ and offsets
$h_1,h_2$, write its quotient odd germ schematically as
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(z),
\]
where $\mathcal I_{12}(z)$ denotes the pair-interaction germ.

In the explicit finite-order corrected source-level model through order $7$
constructed below, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector projections of $\mathcal I_{12}$ are quadratic in the amplitudes
and divisible by $(h_1-h_2)^2$.
\end{definition}
```

Next, replace the current remark `\label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection}` with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Subsection guide]
\label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection}
This subsection is best read as a rigidity program built on the strengthened
one-pair local package
\[
c(h),\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\qquad \Delta_7(h),
\]
or equivalently the normalized planar curve
\[
h\longmapsto \left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]
The projective coincidence conditions remain the organizing principle for the
two-pair and minimal-core analysis. The two-point algebraic interaction

finite-order package, and the remaining steps are the genuine multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping and the extraction into the finite-core endgame.
```

Now replace the entire block from



with the following.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Source-level finite-order quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
For a small finite atomic source
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
let $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$ be defined by linear superposition of the corrected
one-pair phase derivative and primitive attached to each atom:
\[
q_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,q_{h_j},
\qquad
\Phi_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,\Phi_{h_j}.
\]
Insert $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas
of Propositions~\ref{prop:block-perturbation} and
\ref{prop:cross-block-perturbation}, and whiten as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening}. Let
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
:=
\bigl(c_\mu,\ A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},\ A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
denote the resulting cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector package of the odd germ through order $7$.

For a single atom set
\[
F_h:=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]
For two atoms define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

Then the finite-order source package is source-defined and satisfies
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Moreover there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})
\longrightarrow
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
In particular, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic fixed-sector
interaction defects all satisfy the same quadratic factorization.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By construction, the corrected same-point blocks, the corrected mixed block,
and the whitened block depend on the atomic data only through the source-summed
fields $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$. Since these are linear in $\mu$, the resulting
finite-order package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
=
\bigl(c_\mu,A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\]
depends only on the source $\mu$ itself, not on any ordering or presentation of
its atoms. Analyticity in the atomic parameters follows from the linear
superposition in $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ together with the analytic whitening map of
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening} after shrinking the source
neighborhood if necessary.

For two atoms, source-definedness immediately gives swap symmetry:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}).
\]
Likewise, on the diagonal
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
hence
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]

Fix $h$ and write
\[
Q_h(a):=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h).
\]
The diagonal merger identity gives
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2).
\]
Since $Q_h$ is analytic in $a$, the analytic Cauchy equation forces linearity:
\[
Q_h(a)=a\,Q_h(1).
\]
Defining
\[
F_h:=Q_h(1)=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
\]
yields
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]

Now define
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
If one amplitude is zero, then by the one-atom linearity just proved,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Therefore analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto \mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f.
\]

Swap symmetry of $\mathfrak P_{\le 7}$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal, using source-definedness and one-atom linearity,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0.
\]
Hence
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Because $G$ is symmetric in $(h_1,h_2)$, the function $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is
even in $s$. Since $G(h,h)=0$, we have
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]
This proves the proposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Let the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient defects in the
present two-pair section be extracted from the finite-order source package of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
by the same linear coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps used
throughout this subsection. Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by $a_1$ and use boundedness of $|a_2|$ on
normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero $\delta$. Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Source-level identities behind the quadratic factor]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The proof isolates the exact source-level mechanism behind the two-point
closure. First, coincident-atom merger gives analytic additivity on one-atom
rays:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Thus the two-point interaction remainder is not an extra ansatz: it is the
unique defect of additivity of the finite-order source package on the two-atom
source semigroup. Second, once swap symmetry and diagonal merger are known, the
first nonzero separation term is automatically quadratic:
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
So the two-point source-level theorem is fundamentally a finite-order
source-definedness statement rather than a separate asymptotic estimate.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant $\widehat\Psi$, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
together with
Corollary~\ref{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
now close the source-level two-point branch on compact good patches.

Thus the remaining work beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer the
two-point algebraic correction itself. What remains is the genuinely multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping through orders $3,5,7$, together with the local lifted
$3/4$-point analysis for close-point branches on the $v_5\neq 0$ and parallel
$u_5\neq 0$ patches, and the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}
```

Then update the live-routes remark. Inside `\label{rem:live-attack-routes}`, replace only the first item

```latex
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
...
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.
```

Yes — I found one important thing, and it changes the answer.

The main new “finding” is not another goodie. It is that the new source-level proposition is still too strong as written.

The gap is here:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)
\]
does **not** imply
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2).
\]
So the proof does not actually establish one-atom linearity
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h.
\]

And that matters, because the rest of the quadratic factorization proof uses that linearity.

There is a second related issue: the source-summed construction
\[
q_\mu=\sum_j a_j q_{h_j},\qquad \Phi_\mu=\sum_j a_j \Phi_{h_j}
\]
is a natural model, but the corrected block formulas are nonlinear in \(q\) and \(\Phi\) — for example they contain \(q^3\), \(\sin \Delta\), \(\cos \Delta\), and whitening — so one cannot just read off one-atom linearity from the formulas.

So I would **not** keep the draft in its current “two-point branch closed” form yet.

What I would do instead is:

1. replace the current unconditional source-level proposition by a **minimal finite-order criterion** lemma, which is true;
2. make the two-point source theorem conditional again, but now in a very sharp and useful way;
3. update the later “live routes / closed branches” remarks so they no longer claim the two-point branch is finished.

The best real “goodie” to add is this exact minimal criterion.

Replace the current proposition+proof beginning at `\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}` with this:

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Minimal finite-order source criterion for quadratic two-point factorization]
\label{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}
Let $V$ be a finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in V
\]
be analytic on a neighborhood of the small two-atom data. Assume that there is
a one-atom package
\[
F_h\in V
\]
such that the following three identities hold:
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
Define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
Then there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})\to V
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the one-amplitude collapse identities,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Hence analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto V.
\]
Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0,
\]
so
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]
Now set
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Since $G$ is symmetric, $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is even in $s$, and since
$G(h,h)=0$, one has
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}
```

Then replace the current corollary with the honest conditional version:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Assume that the actual corrected two-pair finite-order package through order $7$
admits a source-level realization

F_h=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h)\bigr).
\]
Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects are obtained by dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized
families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} to the cubic,
quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient outputs, then argue exactly as in the
present proof using
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}.
\end{proof}
```

## Assistant (2026-04-20 14:14:59)

Yes — that is the right thing to attack now. I’m checking whether the “diagonal merger” can be proved directly from the corrected block construction already in the paper, rather than assumed as a source-level axiom.

_Thought for 7m 54s_

Yes — and the attack immediately reveals something important.

The gap is real, but it is also more structured than it looked. The naive fix “prove
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h
\]
from the source-summed corrected block formulas” is almost certainly the wrong target.

Here is the decisive computation.

Take a one-atom source of weight \(a\) at height \(h\). In the attempted source-level construction, you set
\[
q_{a,h}=a\,q_h,\qquad \Phi_{a,h}=a\,\Phi_h,\qquad \Delta_{a,h}=a\,\Delta_h.
\]

From the explicit corrected same-point formula in Proposition \(\ref{prop:block-perturbation}\),
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2a\,q_h(t_\pm) & \frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm) &
\frac1{12}\bigl(a\,q_h''(t_\pm)+2a^3 q_h(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s)
}
\]
for some analytic matrix-valued \(\mathcal G_{h,\pm}\).

Likewise, from the explicit corrected mixed block formula in Proposition \(\ref{prop:cross-block-perturbation}\), every entry is odd in \(a\): \(\sin(a\Delta_h)\) is odd, \(a\,q_h\cos(a\Delta_h)\) is odd, and \((2-a^2q_-q_+s^2)\sin(a\Delta_h)\) is odd. Hence
\[
\boxed{
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)
}
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal N_h\).

Now whiten:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,-}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}
\,N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)\,
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,+}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}.
\]
Because
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s),
\]
we get
\[
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}
=
a^{-1/2}\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
Therefore the scalar \(a\) cancels:
\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}
\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)\,
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
}
\]

So the raw corrected whitened block depends on \(a\) only through \(a^2\).

That is the key attack result.

What it means

It means the naive source-summed corrected package is **even** in the source weight \(a\), not linear in \(a\). So the statement
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h
\]
does not follow from the current block construction, and in fact the construction strongly suggests it is false in that raw form.

So the current “unconditional source-level closure” is not salvageable just by pushing harder on the same proof.

But this also tells us the correct replacement target.

The right theorem to prove is not raw linearity in the source weight. It is a **projective one-atom rigidity statement**:

for a one-atom source \(a\delta_h\), the raw finite-order package through order \(7\) lies on the same line as the normalized one-pair package \(F_h\). In other words, one should try to prove
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P^{\raw}_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=\kappa(a,h)\,F_h
}
\]
for some scalar factor \(\kappa(a,h)\), with the shape \(F_h\) independent of \(a\).

Equivalently, the normalized ratios should be independent of the source weight:
\[
\frac{A_{5,\raw}^{\mathfrak f}(a,h)}{c_{\raw}(a,h)}
=
\frac{A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
\frac{\Delta_{7,\raw}(a,h)}{c_{\raw}(a,h)^2}
=
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}.
\]

That is much more plausible, because the draft already treats
\[
\widehat\Psi(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}\right)
\]
as the amplitude-invariant object.

So the real attack path is now:

1. Prove that the raw one-atom corrected package for \(a\delta_h\) is projectively constant in \(a\), not linearly scaling in \(a\).

2. Then for two atoms, work with the raw package in the form
\[
\mathfrak P^{\raw}_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
b_1F_{h_1}+b_2F_{h_2}+\mathcal I_2,
\]
where \(b_i=\kappa(a_i,h_i)\) are the effective amplitudes.

3. If one can prove swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger in that projective form, then the same quadratic factorization argument goes through with \(b_1,b_2\) in place of \(a_1,a_2\):
\[
\mathcal I_2=b_1b_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

That is enough for the two-point exclusion, because the downstream coincidence theorem only needs some nonzero scalar coefficients multiplying the normalized one-pair data. It never truly cares that those coefficients equal the raw source weights.

So: yes, we attacked the gap, and the outcome is:

- the naive source-summed proof route is structurally blocked;
- the correct replacement target is a projective/source-normalization theorem, not a raw linearity theorem.

The most concrete theorem to try next is:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_{\raw}(a,h)=\widehat\Psi(h)
\quad\text{for one-atom sources through order }7,
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\mathfrak P^{\raw}_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=\kappa(a,h)\,F_h.
\]

That is the sharpest way to attack the gap now.

If you want, I’ll turn this into exact LaTeX replacements: remove the current false unconditional proposition, insert the even-in-\(a\) obstruction lemma, and replace it by the projective one-atom rigidity theorem as the new live target.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 14:27:30)

I’m checking the actual formulas now, because this turns on the precise amplitude dependence of the corrected same-point block, mixed block, and whitening. The question is whether the normalized one-atom invariants are truly independent of source weight, or whether the amplitude sneaks back in at order \(5\) or \(7\).

_Thought for 7m 44s_

Yes. I attacked it, and there is a real payoff.

The attack splits the issue cleanly into two different levels:

1. the **raw/source-summed corrected block level**, where the naive one-atom linearity is false or at least not supported by the formulas;  
2. the **ambient quotient level \(\Qabs\)**, where the one-atom amplitude variation is actually invisible.

That distinction is the key.

First, the raw obstruction

Fix \(h\), and consider the one-atom source-weight path
\[
(q_{a,h},\Phi_{a,h})=(a\,q_h,\ a\,\Phi_h).
\]
Insert this into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas.

For the same-point block,
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2a\,q_h(t_\pm) & \frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm) &
\frac1{12}\bigl(a\,q_h''(t_\pm)+2a^3 q_h(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
So
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s)
\]
for an analytic matrix-valued \(\mathcal G_{h,\pm}\).

For the mixed block, every entry is odd in \(a\): \(\sin(a\Delta_h)\) is odd, \(a q_h s\cos(a\Delta_h)\) is odd, and the \(q_-q_+s^2\) correction contributes only even powers multiplying \(\sin(a\Delta_h)\). Thus
\[
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)
\]
for an analytic \(\mathcal N_h\).

After whitening,
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,-}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,+}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2},
\]
the overall factor of \(a\) cancels:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]

So the raw corrected whitened block depends on the source weight only through \(a^2\).

That gives a rigorous obstruction to the naive claim
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
The source-summed raw package is not naturally linear in \(a\); its dependence is even in \(a\).

Now the good news: quotient-level constancy

This same computation also shows the right way to attack the theorem.

Let \(R_{a,h}(z)\) be the corrected local odd germ obtained from the one-atom source-weight path \(a\mapsto(aq_h,a\Phi_h)\), after the same normalization procedure used in the one-pair construction.

Then varying \(a\) at fixed \(h\) is a pure-value deformation of the local input data. But the ambient quotient \(\Qabs\) is, by definition, the odd-germ quotient by the value/gauge family. So the class of \(R_{a,h}\) in \(\Qabs\) is constant along the amplitude path.

In other words, at the ambient quotient level,
\[
[R_{a,h}]_{\Qabs}=[R_{1,h}]_{\Qabs}=F_h.
\]

So the exact rigorous statement we do get is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the one-atom source-weight path is invisible in } \Qabs.
}
\]

That is a real theorem, and it is the correct replacement for the failed raw linearity statement.

What this means for the gap

This proves that the source-summed raw theorem and the quotient-germ theorem are not the same thing.

The raw/source-summed claim
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h
\]
is not justified, and the block formulas point against it.

But the quotient-level statement
\[
[R_{a,h}]_{\Qabs}=F_h
\]
is exactly what one should expect, and it follows from the definition of the quotient by the value family.

So the correct remaining gap is now much sharper:

the two-point/source-level theorem has to be proved either

1. directly at the **quotient-germ transport** level, where one-atom source-weight variation is invisible, or  
2. at the **raw finite-order fixed-sector** level, by proving that the raw amplitude dependence descends projectively to the same quotient-level package.

The exact raw theorem still missing

If you want the sharpest concrete raw statement still open, it is this:

for the weighted one-atom raw finite-order package
\[
(c_a(h),\ A_{5,a}^{\mathfrak f}(h),\ \Delta_{7,a}(h)),
\]
prove
\[
\frac{u_{5,a}(h)}{c_a(h)},
\qquad
\frac{v_{5,a}(h)}{c_a(h)},
\qquad
\frac{\Delta_{7,a}(h)}{c_a(h)^2}
\]
are independent of \(a\).

Equivalently,
\[
\partial_a\!\left(\frac{u_{5,a}(h)}{c_a(h)}\right)=0,\qquad
\partial_a\!\left(\frac{v_{5,a}(h)}{c_a(h)}\right)=0,\qquad
\partial_a\!\left(\frac{\Delta_{7,a}(h)}{c_a(h)^2}\right)=0.
\]

That is the exact projective one-atom rigidity theorem in raw fixed-sector form.

What I think is now the strongest honest conclusion

I do not think the raw/source-summed proof route currently closes.

But I do think we now have a real theorem and a much sharper fork:

- **Rigorous gain:** the one-atom source-weight path is constant in the ambient quotient \(\Qabs\).  
- **Rigorous obstruction:** the raw corrected block is even in the source weight \(a\), so naive raw linearity is the wrong target.  
- **Remaining raw task:** prove amplitude-independence of the strengthened ratios \(u_5/c\), \(v_5/c\), \(\Delta_7/c^2\), or equivalently prove that the raw amplitude path descends projectively to the same quotient germ.

So the gap is not “prove one-atom linearity.” The right target is either quotient-level transport, or raw projective descent.

{\Qabs}_h^{(\le 5)}/\ell_h.

Here is the clean statement.

## One-atom amplitude invariance in the ambient quotient

Fix \(h\) in the cubic-generic region, and let
\[
F_{a,h}(z)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
denote the corrected quotient odd germ of the weighted one-atom family at
source weight \(a\neq 0\).

Then, on each connected nonzero amplitude interval,
\[
\boxed{
F_{a,h}=F_{a_0,h}
\qquad\text{in }\Qabs[[z^2]]
}
\]
for every \(a,a_0\neq 0\).

Equivalently, the weighted one-atom amplitude path is constant in the ambient
odd-germ quotient by the value/gauge family.

### Proof

This is actually built into the setup.

The section introducing \(\Qabs\) says explicitly that \(\Qabs\) is the abstract
odd-germ quotient by the **value/gauge family**. The weighted one-atom path at
fixed \(h\) is obtained by replacing the one-pair local value data
\[
(q_h,\Phi_h)
\]
by
\[
(a\,q_h,\ a\,\Phi_h).
\]
This changes only the local value data at the fixed parameter \(h\); it does not
change the geometric parameter \(h\) itself. So
\[
a\longmapsto (a\,q_h,\ a\,\Phi_h)
\]
is a path entirely inside the value family at fixed \(h\).

But \(\Qabs\) is defined by quotienting out exactly that family (together with
normalization gauge). Therefore every point on this amplitude path determines
the same class in \(\Qabs\). Hence
\[
F_{a,h}=F_{a_0,h}
\qquad\text{in }\Qabs[[z^2]],
\]
as claimed.

That is the whole proof.

---

This immediately gives the order-\(\le 5\) result we already isolated explicitly, but now as a special case:

\[
[A_5(a,h)] = [A_5(a_0,h)]
\quad\text{in }{\Qabs}_h^{(\le 5)}/\ell_h,
\]
which matches the finite-order comparison theorem.

More importantly, it also kills the septic one-atom transport issue at the
ambient level:

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a,h)] = [A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a_0,h)]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and therefore
\[
\Delta_7(a,h)=\Delta_7(a_0,h),
\]
because \(\Delta_7\) is exactly the gauge-invariant scalar attached to the
canonical septic quotient class.

So the earlier direct target
\[
\partial_a[A_{7,a}^{\mathfrak f}]=0
\]
does hold conceptually, but it holds for a simpler reason: the whole one-atom
path is already quotient-trivial before one ever enters the explicit septic
\(K_1\)-formulas.

## Why the earlier raw obstruction does not contradict this

Earlier we found that the raw corrected whitened block along the weighted
one-atom path is even in \(a\):
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
That is still true.

But that only says the **raw representative** varies nontrivially with \(a\).
It does **not** say the class in \(\Qabs\) varies. In fact, the point of
\(\Qabs\) is precisely to mod out such pure-value variation.

So there is no contradiction:

- at the raw block level, the representative can vary with \(a\);
- at the quotient level, that entire variation is invisible.

That is the correct reconciliation.

This is the key consequence:

the remaining source-level/two-point gap is **not** a one-atom septic transport
problem.

So I would no longer treat
\[

\]
as the live target. That is a false fork.

The genuinely remaining issue is now purely **two-atom**:

you need a source-level or quotient-level theorem for the actual two-atom
package itself, with the right

- swap symmetry,
- one-amplitude collapse,
- diagonal collision/merger,

in a form that yields quadratic divisibility in \(h_1-h_2\).

The one-atom path is no longer the blocker.

\text{the one-atom source-weight path is already trivial in }\Qabs
\text{ to all orders.}
}

That means the two-point/source-level theorem has been sharpened again:

it is no longer about transporting one-atom amplitude data through order \(7\);
it is about constructing the **two-atom interaction class** itself.

That is a genuine reduction.

The next attack should therefore go back to the two-atom object and ask:

can we define the corrected two-atom quotient germ directly, and prove its
axis-collapse and diagonal-collapse identities without trying to linearize the
one-atom amplitude dependence?

That is now the right place to push.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 14:55:01)

I’m back on the genuinely live target now: the two-atom quotient object itself. I’m reading the exact definitions around the two-pair decomposition and the quotient model to see whether the diagonal and axis collapse can be proved directly from how the corrected germ is built, rather than from a one-atom scaling story.

_Thought for 4m 9s_

Yes. I attacked it, and the result is sharp:

**the direct ambient-quotient two-atom route can be made precise, but it is too collapsed to yield the needed analytic amplitude-weighted interaction factorization.**

So this attack gives both a real theorem and a real obstruction.

## 1. What the ambient two-atom quotient object actually gives

Let
\[
R_{a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2}(z)
\]
be the raw corrected odd germ obtained by inserting the two-atom source
\[
\mu=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}
\]
into the corrected local construction, and let
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=[R_{a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2}(z)]\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
be its class in the ambient odd-germ quotient.

Then three things are true.

First, **swap symmetry**:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
because the source \(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}\) is unchanged by swapping the two atoms.

Second, **axis collapse**:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=F_{h_1},
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=F_{h_2}.
\]
Reason: on an axis the source becomes a single weighted atom, and the weighted one-atom amplitude path is quotient-trivial in \(\Qabs\).

Third, **diagonal collapse**:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h.
\]
Reason: on the diagonal the source is
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
again a single weighted atom, hence quotient-equivalent to the normalized one-pair class \(F_h\).

So the direct quotient object exists and satisfies the exact collapse identities one would want at the level of classes.

That part is good.

## 2. But this is not enough for the theorem you need

The problem is that the quotient has erased the one-atom amplitude information.

You ultimately want something of the form
\[
\mathcal F_2
=
\lambda_1(a_1,a_2,\dots)\,F_{h_1}
+
\lambda_2(a_1,a_2,\dots)\,F_{h_2}
+
\mathcal I_2,
\]
with \(\mathcal I_2\) vanishing on the axes and on the diagonal, and with \(\lambda_i\) analytic near the small-amplitude origin so that one can force quadratic divisibility.

That is exactly what the direct quotient route cannot supply.

## 3. Obstruction theorem

Here is the clean obstruction.

Assume there exist analytic coefficient functions
\[
\lambda_1,\lambda_2
\]
defined near \((a_1,a_2)=(0,0)\), and an analytic remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]],
\]
such that
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\lambda_1(a_1,a_2,h_1,h_2)F_{h_1}
+
\lambda_2(a_1,a_2,h_1,h_2)F_{h_2}
+
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
and such that \(\mathcal I_2\) vanishes on both axes:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0.
\]

Then along the \(a_2=0\) axis,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=F_{h_1},
\]
so
\[
F_{h_1}
=
\lambda_1(a_1,0,h_1,h_2)F_{h_1}
+
\lambda_2(a_1,0,h_1,h_2)F_{h_2}.
\]
Since this must hold for varying \(h_2\), one gets
\[
\lambda_1(a_1,0,h_1,h_2)=1,
\qquad
\lambda_2(a_1,0,h_1,h_2)=0.
\]

Similarly, along the \(a_1=0\) axis,
\[
\mathcal F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=F_{h_2},
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_1(0,a_2,h_1,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\lambda_2(0,a_2,h_1,h_2)=1.
\]

But now \(\lambda_1\) would have to satisfy
\[
\lambda_1(a_1,0,\dots)=1
\quad\text{for all small }a_1,
\qquad
\lambda_1(0,a_2,\dots)=0
\quad\text{for all small }a_2,
\]
which is impossible for a function analytic at \((0,0)\). The same contradiction appears for \(\lambda_2\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{there is no analytic ambient-quotient decomposition with axis-vanishing remainder near }(a_1,a_2)=(0,0).
}
\]

That is the key result of this attack.

## 4. What this means

This shows that the direct quotient-germ route is **too quotientized**.

It correctly captures:

- swap symmetry,
- axis collapse,
- diagonal collapse,

but it cannot retain enough amplitude data to produce the desired analytic interaction remainder relative to the one-pair classes \(F_{h_1},F_{h_2}\).

So the remaining source-level theorem is not going to come from a pure \(\Qabs\)-valued two-atom object alone.

## 5. The correct conclusion

The two-point theorem must live in a **lift** of the ambient quotient, not in \(\Qabs\) itself.

More concretely, you need a finite-order object that still remembers the external source coefficients at the cubic/quintic/septic levels. That is exactly why the draft’s finite-order corrected package
\[
(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ [A_7^{\mathfrak f}])
\]
is the right place to work, even though the current source-summed proposition there is too strong as written.

So this attack does **not** close the theorem, but it does settle the fork:

- **Not enough:** a direct analytic two-atom object in \(\Qabs\).
- **Still plausible and necessary:** a lifted finite-order source-sensitive package through orders \(3,5,7\).

## 6. The new minimal live target

After this attack, the sharp remaining theorem is:

construct a lifted two-atom finite-order package
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus
\bigl(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\]
such that:

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1}^{\mathrm{fin}},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2}^{\mathrm{fin}},
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h^{\mathrm{fin}},
\]
where
\[
F_h^{\mathrm{fin}}=(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h)).
\]

Once that lifted theorem exists, the quadratic factorization is formal.

So this attack tells us something quite valuable:

**the ambient quotient route is not the missing proof. The missing proof really is a lifted finite-order source theorem.**

If you want, I can now push on that exact lifted theorem and try to isolate whether the true remaining obstruction is already visible at cubic, quintic, or only septic level.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 15:02:12)

I’m pushing on the lifted finite-order theorem now. The immediate question is whether the obstruction already appears at cubic or quintic level, or whether those levels can actually be made source-linear and only the septic layer remains problematic.

_Thought for 3m 32s_

Yes. I attacked it, and I think the decisive result is a **no-go theorem**.

The source-summed corrected finite-order package currently written in the draft cannot possibly satisfy the one-atom linearity / diagonal additivity needed for the two-point theorem.

That is now a rigorous obstruction, not just a missing proof.

## The no-go theorem

Fix \(h\), and define the one-atom source-summed corrected package exactly as in the current proposition:
\[
q_{a,h}:=a\,q_h,\qquad \Phi_{a,h}:=a\,\Phi_h,
\]
insert this into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas, whiten, and extract the order-\(\le 7\) package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)
=
\bigl(c_a(h),\,A_{5,a}^{\mathfrak f}(h),\,A_{7,a}^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]

Then each component is an **even analytic function of \(a\)**.

In particular,
\[
c_a(h),\qquad A_{5,a}^{\mathfrak f}(h),\qquad A_{7,a}^{\mathfrak f}(h)
\]
all depend on \(a\) through \(a^2\).

### Proof

From Proposition \(\ref{prop:block-perturbation}\), the corrected same-point block is
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
2a\,q_h(t_\pm) & \frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm)\\[1ex]
\frac12 a\,q_h'(t_\pm) &
\frac1{12}\bigl(a\,q_h''(t_\pm)+2a^3 q_h(t_\pm)^3\bigr)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
So one can factor
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s)
\]
for an analytic matrix-valued \(\mathcal G_{h,\pm}\).

From Proposition \(\ref{prop:cross-block-perturbation}\), every entry of the corrected mixed block is odd in \(a\):
\[
\sin(a\Delta_h),\qquad a\,q_h s\cos(a\Delta_h),\qquad
(2-a^2q_-q_+s^2)\sin(a\Delta_h),
\]
so
\[
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)
\]
for an analytic \(\mathcal N_h\).

Now whiten:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,-}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,+}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}.
\]
Because
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s),
\]
we have
\[
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)\bigr)^{-1/2}
=
a^{-1/2}\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
Hence the scalar \(a\) cancels:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}\,
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)\,
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
So the whitened block depends only on \(a^2\), and therefore every odd Taylor coefficient in \(s\), and every linear projection/extraction from those coefficients, is an even analytic function of \(a\).

That proves the claim.

## Immediate consequence

This kills the current proposition in its present form.

Indeed, if the draft claims
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h,
\]
then the left side is even in \(a\), while the right side is odd unless \(F_h=0\).

So on any patch where
\[
c(h)\neq 0
\]
or
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\neq 0,
\]
this is impossible.

Likewise, the diagonal additivity used in the proof,
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2),
\qquad
Q_h(a):=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h),
\]
cannot hold for a nonzero even analytic function. The only analytic function that is both even and additive is the zero function.

So the obstruction is already present at the **one-atom cubic level**. It is not a septic-only issue.

## What this means for the theorem

This settles the fork.

The currently written “source-summed corrected finite-order package” route is dead in the strong form
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1F_{h_1}+a_2F_{h_2}+\mathcal I_2.
\]

It is not merely unproved. It is incompatible with the actual amplitude dependence of the corrected blocks.

So the live target is now sharper:

### Not viable
Using the raw source-summed corrected blocks, whitening, and direct coefficient extraction to obtain a package that is linear in the source amplitudes \(a_i\).

### Still potentially viable
Constructing a **different lifted package** through orders \(3,5,7\) that remembers the source amplitudes linearly before the whitening nonlinearity destroys that structure.

## Why this matters downstream

The exact strengthened coincidence theorem in the draft uses the actual coefficients
\[
a_1,\ a_2
\]
in
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2),\qquad
a_1A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_1)+a_2A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_2),\qquad
a_1[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h_1)+a_2[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h_2).
\]

So any replacement theorem must still produce a lift with those external source coefficients, or something demonstrably equivalent.

The current source-summed package does not do that.

## Strongest honest conclusion

The attack did not close the theorem. But it did prove something important:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the present source-summed corrected finite-order model cannot prove the desired two-point source theorem.}
}
\]

And more sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the obstruction appears already at one-atom cubic/quintic level, because the extracted package is even in the source weight.}
}
\]

So the next viable route is no longer “push harder on the same proposition.”

It has to be one of these:

1. build a **different lift** that is linear in source amplitudes before whitening, or  
2. reformulate the two-point theorem in terms of a different finite-order source-sensitive object, not the current source-summed corrected block package.

That is the cleanest mathematical outcome of the attack so far.

That is very consistent with the obstruction I found to naive source-linearity, and it suggests the right two-point theorem should probably be formulated only strongly enough to feed defect-corrected coincidence into the strengthened/projective data, not as a literal amplitude-linear decomposition of the raw corrected package. The note’s own summary still says the current two-point bottleneck is the missing source-level reduction/factorization in that subsection, but the surrounding structure now makes clear that this bottleneck sits inside a more amplitude-invariant endgame than before. 

So my updated view is:

The new ammo does **not** rescue the source-summed theorem I attacked and broke. That obstruction still stands.

But it **does** change what a successful replacement theorem needs to do. It likely only has to deliver the right quadratic control into the strengthened two-pair coincidence machinery, not a globally “linear in source amplitudes” corrected block theorem.

The three-point and four-point updates are mostly indirect for the present attack. They matter because they greatly stabilize the rest of the proof once the two-point branch is under control: the three-point branch is now organized by the lifted curvature/osculating package, and the nonmixed four-point branch is now governed by the scalar invariant \(\mathcal R\), with interval-persistent degeneracy collapsing to affine planarity rather than leaving a large uncontrolled branch. The explicit Mellin symbol, gamma-ratio kernel, and sign-definite surviving odd tail are strong infrastructure for the corrected odd channel and for the zeta-side cancellation story, but they do not seem to touch the specific local/source-level two-atom problem of proving swap symmetry plus axis/diagonal collapse in a lifted finite-order package. Yes, the new structural updates are relevant.

They do **not** directly fill the two-point gap.

But they **do** sharpen the correct target for the current attack:

instead of trying to prove a too-strong raw source-linear theorem, I should aim for the weakest lifted/projective two-atom theorem that is sufficient to feed the existing strengthened two-pair coincidence theorem and hence the defect-scale-close/exclusion pipeline. The updated architecture makes that a much more plausible and better-scoped target than the one I was initially chasing. 

My honest ranking of relevance is:

Most relevant: the finite-core / amplitude-invariant reformulation around the two-pair-to-minimal-core bridge.

Somewhat relevant: the three-point curvature package and four-point \(\mathcal R\)-planarity package, because they reduce downstream uncertainty.

Least relevant to this exact gap: the \(N\)-point odd-tail Mellin/sign package.

The next attack I would run is to reformulate the two-point theorem directly as a **lifted projective coincidence theorem for the strengthened data**, rather than as a raw source-linear corrected-block decomposition.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 15:27:52)

I’m pushing on the weaker, more plausible target now: not raw source-linearity, but a projective/lifted two-atom theorem just strong enough to drive the strengthened coincidence machinery. _Thought for 5m 55s_

I think there is a real bypass.

It does **not** give the quadratic defect factorization. But it does look strong enough to kill the **exact close two-point bad-core branch**, which may be all you actually need on the finite-core side.

The core idea is much weaker than the source-level finite-order theorem:

you do not need an amplitude-linear decomposition.  
You only need the actual two-atom corrected quotient germ to be continuous in the atomic data and to collapse on the diagonal to the one-pair quotient class.

Here is the clean statement.

---

### Proposition (exact close two-point exclusion from quotient diagonal collapse)

Let
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
denote the actual corrected quotient odd germ attached to the normalized two-atom data \((a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\).

Assume:

1. \(\mathcal F_2\) is continuous in the normalized two-atom parameters;

2. on the diagonal,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h,
\]
where \(F_h\) is the normalized one-pair quotient germ;

3. on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), one has \(F_h\neq 0\).

Then there exists \(\varepsilon_J>0\) such that no normalized bad two-pair core with
\[
h_1,h_2\in J,\qquad 0<|h_1-h_2|<\varepsilon_J
\]
can exist.

---

### Proof

Assume the contrary. Then there is a sequence of normalized bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_1^{(n)},h_1^{(n)};a_2^{(n)},h_2^{(n)})
\]
with
\[
h_1^{(n)},h_2^{(n)}\in J,\qquad h_1^{(n)}-h_2^{(n)}\to 0,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1^{(n)},h_1^{(n)};a_2^{(n)},h_2^{(n)})=0
\]
because they are bad cores.

By compactness of \(J\) and the normalization on amplitudes, after passing to a subsequence we may assume
\[
h_1^{(n)}\to m,\qquad h_2^{(n)}\to m,
\qquad
a_1^{(n)}\to a_1^*,\qquad a_2^{(n)}\to a_2^*.
\]
Continuity of \(\mathcal F_2\) gives
\[
0
=
\lim_{n\to\infty}
\mathcal F_2(a_1^{(n)},h_1^{(n)};a_2^{(n)},h_2^{(n)})
=
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Now apply diagonal collapse:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=F_m.
\]
Hence
\[
F_m=0.
\]
But \(m\in J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), so the one-pair quotient germ is nonzero there. Contradiction.

So such a sequence cannot exist.

\(\square\)

---

This is the first attack that I think really lands.

It avoids the false source-summed linearity theorem completely. It also avoids the over-quotientized decomposition problem. It only uses:

- exact bad-core vanishing,
- continuity of the true two-atom quotient object,
- diagonal collapse to the one-pair quotient class.

And that diagonal collapse is exactly where our earlier “one-atom amplitude path is invisible in \(\Qabs\)” result becomes useful.

## Why this matters

This does **not** prove the current conditional lemma
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

It also does **not** give the draft’s quantitative defect statement.

But it **does** appear to give the same consequence for the exact close two-point branch:

there are no exact normalized bad two-pair cores accumulating to the diagonal on compact good patches.

That is a real substitute if the finite-core endgame only needs to rule out exact 2-point minimal bad cores.

## Why I think this is compatible with the new structural updates

The recent structural updates push the global endgame toward exact finite-core configurations of size \(\le 4\), with the real geometry then living in the 3-point and 4-point branches. In that architecture, an exact close-point exclusion theorem is already quite valuable: it removes the 2-point branch from the finite-core list without needing the heavier quantitative factorization theorem.

So my updated view is:

- the **quadratic defect-factorization route** is still open;
- the **exact close two-point branch** may now be killable by this much weaker quotient-diagonal continuity theorem.

## What still needs to be checked

The remaining rigorous checks are much smaller than the old source theorem:

1. Define the actual corrected two-atom quotient map
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
cleanly enough that continuity is explicit.

2. State and prove diagonal collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h.
\]
This should come from:
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h
\]
plus the fact that the weighted one-atom path is quotient-trivial in \(\Qabs\).

3. Make explicit that \(F_h\neq 0\) on \(\{c\neq 0\}\).

That is a much smaller and more believable package than the full lifted finite-order source-linear theorem.

My honest assessment: this is the strongest progress so far on the two-point attack. It does not close the quantitative source-level factorization, but it may close the exact local two-point bad-core branch anyway.

If you want, I’ll turn this into exact LaTeX to insert as an alternative proposition/remark replacing the current “two-point source bottleneck” wording.
