_Thought for 3m 35s_

I checked it against the current draft.

Verdict: **the argument is mathematically sound as a conditional bypass, but it does not yet check out as an unconditional theorem of the draft.**

What does check out is the internal logic of the contradiction:

If you had a genuine corrected two-atom quotient map
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
defined on normalized two-atom data, continuous in those parameters, and satisfying exact diagonal collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h,
\]
then the close exact two-point bad-core exclusion argument is fine. Combined with “bad core means quotient odd germ vanishes identically,” it would rule out exact bad two-point cores accumulating to the diagonal on compact patches where \(F_h\neq 0\).

The parts that already match the draft are these.

The one-pair quotient germ \(F_h\) is a real object in the draft. “Bad normalized finite core” is defined by vanishing of its quotient odd germ. And on the good one-pair region the cubic leading coefficient is nonzero, so on a patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the one-pair germ is certainly not the zero germ. So the contradiction endpoint
\[
0=\mathcal F_2(\cdots)\to F_m\neq 0
\]
is the right shape.

What does **not** currently check out is the input package needed to run that proof.

First, the draft does **not** presently define the actual two-atom quotient object \(\mathcal F_2\) in a theorem-strength way. The current `def:two-pair-decomposition` is explicitly schematic, and it is phrased in exactly the amplitude-linear way that we have already found reason to distrust.

Second, the draft does **not** yet prove continuity of the quotient germ for a normalized two-atom family in the atomic parameters. That continuity is plausible, but right now it is not a proved lemma.

Third, the diagonal collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h
\]
is also not a proved theorem in the current text. It would need a genuine source-to-quotient functoriality statement for coincident atoms, plus the claim that the weighted one-atom path is quotient-trivial in the relevant sense. Architecturally that is plausible, but it is not yet established in the draft.

Fourth, your compactness step on amplitudes also needs one more explicit input. I do not see a standalone theorem in the current draft stating that the normalized two-point amplitude space is compact or precompact. If normalization really fixes the amplitudes up to a compact projective parameter, then the subsequence extraction is fine. But that assumption still needs to be made explicit.

So the cleanest summary is:

Your bypass is a **good conditional proposition**, not yet a proved replacement theorem.

More specifically, it proves the following conditional statement:

If the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ exists as a continuous function of normalized two-atom data and collapses on the diagonal to the one-pair quotient germ, then exact close bad two-point cores cannot occur on compact patches \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\).

That is worth keeping. It is substantially weaker than the current source-level quadratic factorization target, but also much more believable.

Two caveats matter.

It only kills the **exact** close two-point bad-core branch. It does not recover the current quantitative defect machinery.

And it does not yet integrate automatically with the present two-pair subsection, because that subsection is still organized around defect identities and the conditional finite-order source criterion.

So my honest recommendation is: do **not** replace the current two-point bottleneck by this as if it were done. But it is definitely worth recording as a sharper alternative route, conditional on a much smaller input package than the false source-linear theorem.

The next step would be to state it in the draft explicitly as a conditional exact two-point exclusion proposition, rather than as a claimed closure.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 15:53:09)

_Thought for 1m 12s_

Yes. I would add this as a **separate conditional bypass**, not as a replacement for the current source-level criterion.

Insert the following block **immediately after** the proof of

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
```

and **before** `\begin{remark}[Exact remaining source-level input on the two-point branch]`.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Conditional exact two-point exclusion from quotient diagonal collapse]
\label{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}
Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}
\]
be a compact interval. Assume there exists an actual corrected two-atom quotient
map
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
defined on normalized two-pair data, with the following properties:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Continuity.}
The map $\mathcal F_2$ is continuous in the normalized two-pair parameters.

\item \textbf{Diagonal collapse.}
For every $h\in J$ and every normalized amplitude pair $(a_1,a_2)$,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h,
\]
where $F_h$ is the normalized one-pair quotient odd germ.

\item \textbf{Precompactness of normalized amplitudes.}
Every sequence of normalized two-pair data with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0
\]
admits a subsequence along which the full normalized parameter tuple converges.
\end{enumerate}

Then there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Equivalently, under the three assumptions above, the exact close two-point
bad-core branch is excluded on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume for contradiction that there exists a sequence of nontrivial normalized
bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Since each core is bad, its quotient odd germ vanishes identically, so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})=0
\qquad
\text{for all }n.
\]

By the precompactness assumption, after passing to a subsequence we may assume
that the full normalized parameter tuple converges:
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,
\qquad
a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,
\qquad
h_{1,n}\to m,
\qquad
h_{2,n}\to m
\]
for some $m\in J$. By continuity of $\mathcal F_2$,
\[
0
=
\lim_{n\to\infty}
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
=
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Applying diagonal collapse gives
\[
0=\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=F_m.
\]

But $m\in J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}$, so the normalized one-pair quotient germ
$F_m$ is nonzero: its cubic leading coefficient is nonzero on $\{c\neq 0\}$.
This contradiction proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[A weaker exact two-point route]
\label{rem:weaker-exact-two-point-route}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs} is strictly
weaker than the quadratic defect-factorization route of
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}. It does not produce
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
and does not yield the quantitative defect estimates used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}.
Instead, it isolates a smaller alternative input: a genuine corrected two-atom
quotient map, continuity in normalized parameters, and exact diagonal collapse
to the one-pair quotient class.

Thus there are now two distinct two-point routes in the draft:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the stronger finite-order source-level route, which would force quadratic
defect bounds and hence quantitative defect-scale closeness;

\item the weaker quotient-diagonal route, which would already exclude exact
close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{enumerate}

At present, the draft does not prove either route outright. The first remains a
finite-order source-level merger problem; the second remains a continuity and
diagonal-collapse problem for the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ.
\end{remark}
```

I would also make one small update to the later “what remains” remark so the draft acknowledges this new weaker branch.

Inside `\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}`, replace the sentence

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic.
```

with:

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a

two-point side: the stronger finite-order source-level merger route, which
would force quadratic defect estimates, and the weaker quotient-diagonal route,

And replace the next sentence

with:

```

I would **not** remove the existing minimal-source-level lemma/corollary. This new proposition belongs alongside them as a weaker alternative route, not as a replacement.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 16:02:52)

I’m going to pin this down to the smallest live target in the current draft, so the next attack is on the most promising route rather than another broad pass.

_Thought for 36s_

Yes. The best next attack is **not** the raw source-linear theorem anymore.

The highest-probability route is:

## Attack the weaker exact two-point route first

Try to prove the conditional bypass outright:

1. define the **actual corrected two-atom quotient germ**
   \[
   \mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
   \]
   on normalized two-pair data;

2. prove it is **continuous** in those normalized parameters;

3. prove **diagonal collapse**
   \[
   \mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h;
   \]

4. combine that with \(F_h\neq 0\) on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\) to exclude exact close bad two-point cores.

That is the smallest live package, and it is much more believable than the quadratic source-factorization theorem. It also matches the current state of the draft, where the two-point bottleneck is still identified as a source-level reduction problem, but the surrounding architecture has become more amplitude-invariant and finite-core oriented. turn10file3

Why this is the best way:

- The raw source-summed finite-order route is blocked by the even-in-amplitude obstruction we found.
- The direct ambient-quotient route is strong enough to kill the **exact** close two-point branch if continuity and diagonal collapse are available.
- The newer three-point and four-point structure means that removing exact two-point cores is already quite valuable, because the remaining live branches are now organized much more cleanly than before. turn10file2

## What to prove, in order

The right order is:

### 1. Prove quotient triviality for weighted one-atom collapse
You already have the conceptual statement:
\[
(a_1+a_2)\delta_h
\quad\text{and}\quad
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h
\]
represent the same coincident source, and weighted one-atom amplitude variation should be invisible in \(\Qabs\).

So the first clean lemma to isolate is:

\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h)=F_h
\quad\text{in }\Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
for every normalized one-atom weight \(a\neq 0\).

That is the engine behind diagonal collapse.

### 2. Build the actual two-atom quotient object
Not schematic decomposition. Just the object itself:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]

You do not need to decompose it as
\[
a_1F_{h_1}+a_2F_{h_2}+\mathcal I_2.
\]
That decomposition is exactly where the bad obstruction showed up.

You only need the existence of the quotient germ of the corrected two-atom construction as a function of normalized data.

### 3. Prove continuity
This is the narrow technical point.

You want:
if
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})\to (a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
then
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})\to \mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
in the finite-order or germ topology being used.

This is likely the most attackable missing piece, because it should come from continuity of the local corrected block formulas and the normalization/quotient construction.

### 4. Prove diagonal collapse
Once continuity and the one-atom quotient-triviality are explicit, diagonal collapse should be short:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h)
=
F_h.
\]

### 5. Use exact bad-core vanishing
Then the contradiction argument excludes exact close two-point bad cores on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}.
\]

## Why I would do this before anything else

Because the stronger route still asks for a theorem of the form
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
or a lifted finite-order analogue, and every attempt so far has run into a genuine structural problem.

By contrast, the exact route asks only for:

- existence of the true corrected two-atom quotient object,
- continuity,
- diagonal collapse.

That is a much smaller target.

## If that works, what next

If exact close two-point exclusion is enough for the finite-core reduction, you may not need the quadratic defect theorem at all for the two-point branch.

If it turns out not to be enough, then the next-best attack is **not** to go back to raw source-linearity, but to prove a weaker **projective/lifted finite-order statement** only for the strengthened coincidence data, not for the full corrected package. That would mean targeting just enough structure to feed
\[
\widehat\Psi
\]
rather than all raw coefficients. But that is the second-choice route, not the first. 

So my ranking is:

First choice: prove the exact quotient-diagonal route.

Second choice: prove a weaker lifted/projective finite-order theorem tailored only to the strengthened two-pair coincidence machinery.

Last choice: keep pushing the raw source-summed amplitude-linear theorem. That one now looks like the wrong object.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 16:06:29)

I’m going after the exact route directly now: trying to turn “actual corrected two-atom quotient germ” into a minimal, provable statement from the current local construction, rather than another schematic ansatz.

_Thought for 1m 51s_

Yes. I think the best live attack now is this, and it actually gets somewhere:

## Try to prove the exact two-point branch directly from the actual two-atom quotient germ

Not from a source-linear finite-order package. Not from quadratic defect factorization.

The key theorem to aim for is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no sequence of exact normalized bad two-pair cores with }h_1-h_2\to 0
\text{ on }J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}.
}
\]

And I think the right proof package is now small enough to be believable.

---

## The right object

For a finite atomic source
\[
\mu=\sum_{r=1}^N a_r\delta_{h_r},
\]
define the source fields
\[
q_\mu:=\sum_r a_r q_{h_r},
\qquad
\Phi_\mu:=\sum_r a_r \Phi_{h_r}.
\]

Then feed \((q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)\) into the **same corrected local construction** already used for the one-pair family:

- corrected same-point blocks,
- corrected mixed block,
- whitening,
- corrected odd germ,
- then pass to the quotient by the value/gauge family.

For two atoms,
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
call the resulting quotient germ
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]].
\]

This avoids the bad ansatz
\[
a_1F_{h_1}+a_2F_{h_2}+\mathcal I_2.
\]
You never decompose it.

---

## What I think can actually be proved

### 1. Permutation invariance
This is immediate:
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal F_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
because the underlying source is the same.

### 2. Axis collapse
If \(a_2=0\), then
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_{h_1}.
\]
So
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1),
\]
where \(\mathcal F_1(a,h)\) is the one-atom quotient germ.

Now the weighted one-atom amplitude path
\[
a\mapsto (a q_h,a\Phi_h)
\]
is a pure-value deformation at fixed \(h\), so in the ambient quotient by the value/gauge family it has constant class. Therefore
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h)=F_h.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=F_{h_1},
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=F_{h_2}.
}
\]

### 3. Diagonal collapse
If \(h_1=h_2=h\), then as a source
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]
So
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h)=F_h.
\]
Thus
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h.
}
\]

### 4. Continuity
This is the only real technical step, but it looks very attackable.

Why I think it should go through:

- \((a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)\mapsto q_\mu,\Phi_\mu\) is continuous in the local source topology;
- the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas are explicit analytic expressions in \(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu\);
- whitening is analytic on the positive-definite region;
- the quotient map is defined by modding out a fixed ambiguity family, so passing to class should preserve continuity.

So on a compact good patch, after shrinking neighborhoods if needed, the two-atom quotient germ should vary continuously in normalized parameters.

That gives the following theorem.

---

## Conditional theorem, now very sharp

If the actual two-atom corrected quotient germ
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
is continuous in normalized two-atom parameters, then exact close bad two-point cores are excluded on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\).

### Proof
Suppose
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
is a sequence of normalized bad two-pair cores with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,\qquad 0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Because the cores are bad,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})=0.
\]
Pass to a convergent subsequence of normalized parameters:
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,
\qquad
a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,
\qquad
h_{1,n}\to m,
\qquad
h_{2,n}\to m.
\]
By continuity,
\[
0=\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
By diagonal collapse,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=F_m.
\]
Hence
\[
F_m=0.
\]
But on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the one-pair quotient germ is nonzero because its cubic coefficient is nonzero. Contradiction.

So exact close bad two-point cores cannot occur.

---

## What this attack achieves

This does **not** prove the stronger theorem
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

It also does **not** recover the current quantitative defect route.

But it **does** look like a plausible way to remove the exact close two-point branch from the finite-core list.

And given the new structural updates elsewhere, that might be enough to hand the endgame off to the 3-point and 4-point branches.

---

## The actual best next sub-attack

The single best next thing to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
(a_1,h_1,a_2,h_2)\longmapsto \mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\text{ is continuous on normalized two-atom data.}
}
\]

That is now the smallest live technical target.

Not source-linearity.  
Not septic \(K_1\)-transport.  
Not quadratic factorization.

Just continuity of the true quotient object.

If that continuity proof lands, the exact close two-point branch is basically dead.

My honest view: this is now the strongest route on the table.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 16:20:03)

I’m pushing directly on the continuity target now. If that can be proved from the existing local construction, the exact close two-point branch may fall without needing the stronger quadratic interaction theorem.

_Thought for 4m 7s_

Yes. I think I can sharpen the attack one more time.

The best route is **smaller than full quotient-germ continuity** and **much smaller than quadratic factorization**:

## Only prove continuity of the cubic channel

You do not need continuity of the whole two-atom quotient germ to kill the exact close two-point branch.

A bad core has quotient odd germ identically zero, so in particular its **cubic quotient coefficient** vanishes. If that cubic coefficient is continuous in the normalized two-atom parameters and collapses on the diagonal to the one-pair cubic coefficient \(c(h)\), then exact close two-point bad cores are already excluded on any compact patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\).

That is the smallest live target I see.

Here is the precise statement.

---

### Lemma (cubic continuity criterion for exact two-point exclusion)

Let
\[
C_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
denote the cubic coefficient of the actual corrected two-atom quotient odd germ on normalized two-pair data.

Assume:

1. \(C_2\) is continuous in the normalized two-pair parameters;

2. for every \(h\) and normalized amplitude pair \((a_1,a_2)\),
\[
C_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=c(h);
\]

3. the normalized amplitude parameter space is precompact on sequences with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,\qquad |h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]

Then there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair cores with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,\qquad 0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]

### Proof

If the two-pair core is bad, its quotient odd germ vanishes identically, hence
\[
C_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})=0.
\]
Pass to a convergent subsequence of normalized parameters:
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,\qquad a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,\qquad
h_{1,n}\to m,\qquad h_{2,n}\to m
\]
with \(m\in J\). By continuity,
\[
0=\lim_{n\to\infty} C_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
= C_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
By diagonal collapse,
\[
C_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=c(m).
\]
But \(m\in J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), so \(c(m)\neq 0\). Contradiction.

So exact close bad two-point cores cannot accumulate to the diagonal.

---

That is a real improvement over the full-germ route. It removes the need to topologize all of \(\Qabs[[z^2]]\).

## Why this is the best attack

Because continuity of the cubic channel is much more believable from the actual formulas than continuity of the whole quotient germ.

If the actual two-atom corrected object is built by feeding the combined source
\[
\mu=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}
\]
into the same corrected local construction, then
\[
q_\mu=a_1 q_{h_1}+a_2 q_{h_2},\qquad
\Phi_\mu=a_1 \Phi_{h_1}+a_2 \Phi_{h_2}.
\]

The corrected same-point and mixed blocks are explicit analytic expressions in

- \(q_\mu(t_\pm)\),
- \(q_\mu'(t_\pm)\),
- \(q_\mu''(t_\pm)\),
- \(\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)=\Phi_\mu(m-\tfrac s2)-\Phi_\mu(m+\tfrac s2)\),

and the whitening map is analytic on the positive-definite region. So the cubic coefficient extracted from the whitened odd expansion should be continuous, in fact analytic, in the two-atom parameters as long as you stay on a compact good patch and within the normalization regime.

So the continuity piece is now down to a very concrete local analytic-dependence lemma, not a global source theorem.

## Diagonal collapse at cubic level is also easier than full diagonal collapse

On the diagonal,
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]
So the two-atom construction reduces to a weighted one-atom construction. But the weighted one-atom amplitude path is quotient-trivial in the ambient value/gauge quotient, so its cubic quotient coefficient is the same normalized one-pair cubic coefficient:
\[
C_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=c(h).
\]

So the diagonal statement you need is only the cubic version, and that is much lighter than proving full equality of quotient germs.

## What this means strategically

This is now my ranking of the two-point routes:

First choice:
prove the **cubic continuity criterion** and use it to kill exact close two-point bad cores.

Second choice:
prove the full quotient-diagonal continuity route.

Third choice:
prove the stronger finite-order source-level merger theorem giving
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

The first route is now clearly the best one.

It is also well aligned with the updated architecture: the draft’s real two-point bottleneck is still in the two-pair subsection, while the three-point branch is now more derivative-geometric and the four-point nonmixed branch is more controlled, so removing exact close two-point cores would already simplify the finite-core endgame substantially. turn12file1

## What is still actually open

I do not think the current draft yet proves the cubic continuity lemma outright.

The remaining items are:

- define the **actual** cubic coefficient \(C_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\) of the corrected two-atom quotient object in a theorem-strength way;
- prove it depends continuously on normalized two-atom parameters;
- make the normalization/precompactness of the amplitude parameters explicit if it is not already fixed by convention.

That is a much smaller list than before.

## My honest bottom line

Yes, there is a better attack.

The best target is no longer “prove source-linear two-point factorization.”

It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove continuity of the cubic quotient coefficient and its diagonal collapse.}
}
\]

If that lands, the exact close two-point bad-core branch is dead.

Yes. I think the cubic route can be sharpened one more step, and this is now the best attack I see.

The right object is **not** a scalar \(C_2\) at first. It is the **cubic quotient class**, or even better, a canonical cubic witness for that class.

The clean version is:

\[

Here is the strongest form I think is actually attackable.

---

## 1. Replace the scalar cubic criterion by a class-valued one

For the actual corrected two-atom local construction, let
\[
J_{3,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \mathcal J_3
\]
denote the cubic raw odd-jet coefficient of the corrected local block, and let
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
[J_{3,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)]
\in
\mathcal J_3/V_{\val}^{(3)}.
\]

Then the exact close two-point branch is excluded if we can prove just these two facts:

1. \(v_{0,2}\) is continuous in normalized two-atom parameters;

2. on the diagonal,
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=v_0(h),
\]
where
\[
v_0(h)=[J_3^{\pair}(h)]\neq 0
\]
on the cubic-generic region.

This is already enough, because a bad two-pair core has quotient odd germ \(0\), hence in particular cubic quotient class
\[
v_{0,2}=0.
\]
Then continuity plus diagonal collapse gives a contradiction exactly as before.

So the exact close two-point route does **not** need continuity of the whole quotient germ. It only needs continuity of the cubic quotient class.

That is a major simplification.

---

## 2. There is an even cleaner witness: the diagonal-traceless cubic part

The draft’s cubic-leading proposition does something stronger than just say
\[
[J_3^{\pair}(h)]\neq 0.
\]
It identifies a concrete nonzero witness: the **diagonal-traceless part** of the cubic jet. In fact the cubic quotient is detected by the diagonal-traceless component
\[
v(h)B(h)(x_1-x_2)
\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\]
under the hypothesis
\[
V_{\val}^{(3)}\subset
\left\{
\begin{pmatrix}0&*\\ *&0\end{pmatrix}
\right\}.
\]

So the best cubic two-point object is actually
\[
\Xi_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\pi_{\mathrm{dt}}\bigl(J_{3,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C
\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(\pi_{\mathrm{dt}}\) means diagonal-traceless projection.

If the cubic value-family for the actual two-atom corrected family is still off-diagonal, then \(\Xi_2\) is already a quotient-invariant cubic witness. In that case the exact close two-point exclusion reduces to:

- \(\Xi_2\) is continuous;
- \(\Xi_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\Xi(h)\neq 0\) on the cubic-generic patch.

That is even better than class-valued continuity.

So the real attack target is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show that the two-atom cubic quotient is detected by the diagonal-traceless cubic part, and that this part is continuous.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Why continuity of the cubic witness is believable

This is the part I think we can nearly prove from the existing formulas.

For a two-atom source
\[
\mu=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
the source fields are
\[
q_\mu=a_1q_{h_1}+a_2q_{h_2},
\qquad
\Phi_\mu=a_1\Phi_{h_1}+a_2\Phi_{h_2}.
\]

The corrected same-point and mixed blocks are explicit analytic expressions in:

\[
q_\mu(t_\pm),\quad q_\mu'(t_\pm),\quad q_\mu''(t_\pm),\quad
\Delta_{\mu,m}(s)=\Phi_\mu(m-\tfrac s2)-\Phi_\mu(m+\tfrac s2),
\]
and the whitening map is analytic on the positive-definite region.

So the raw corrected local block varies analytically in the two-atom parameters as long as we stay on a compact patch where the baseline blocks remain uniformly positive-definite. Therefore its cubic coefficient
\[
J_{3,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
is continuous, indeed analytic, in those parameters.

And then:

- either pass to the fixed finite-dimensional quotient \(\mathcal J_3/V_{\val}^{(3)}\), or
- project to diagonal-traceless part if that is already quotient-invariant.

So continuity is no longer the scary part. It reduces to a local analytic-dependence lemma for the cubic jet.

---

## 4. Diagonal collapse is also easier at cubic level

On the diagonal,
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]
So the two-atom corrected local construction becomes a weighted one-atom construction at the same \(h\).

Now the weighted one-atom amplitude path is quotient-trivial in the ambient value/gauge quotient. Therefore the cubic quotient class along that path is constant. So
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=v_0(h).
\]

If you work with the diagonal-traceless witness instead, this becomes
\[
\Xi_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\Xi(h),
\]
where \(\Xi(h)\neq 0\) on the cubic-generic region.

So the diagonal-collapse input also collapses to a small one-atom quotient-triviality statement, not to the full two-point source theorem.

---

## 5. The exact exclusion theorem you can now target

This is the best theorem to aim for next:

### Proposition
Let
\[
J\Subset \mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}.
\]
Assume the actual corrected two-atom cubic jet
\[
J_{3,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
is defined on normalized two-pair data, depends continuously on those parameters, and has the property that its quotient class satisfies
\[
[J_{3,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)]=[J_3^{\pair}(h)]
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathcal J_3/V_{\val}^{(3)}.
\]
Then there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair cores with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]

### Proof
If the core is bad, its quotient odd germ is zero, so in particular
\[
[J_{3,2}(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})]=0.
\]
After passing to a convergent normalized subsequence,
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,\quad a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,\quad
h_{1,n}\to m,\quad h_{2,n}\to m.
\]
By continuity of the cubic quotient class,
\[
0=[J_{3,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)].
\]
By diagonal collapse,
\[
[J_{3,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)]=[J_3^{\pair}(m)]=v_0(m).
\]
But \(m\in \mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}\), so \(v_0(m)\neq 0\). Contradiction.

That would kill the exact close two-point branch.

---

## 6. What remains genuinely open

This attack isolates one real remaining lemma.

It is **not** continuity of the whole quotient germ.

It is **not** quadratic defect factorization.

It is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show that the actual corrected two-atom cubic jet defines a continuous cubic quotient class, with diagonal collapse to }v_0(h).
}
\]

And if you want the strongest concrete version, replace “cubic quotient class” by “diagonal-traceless cubic witness” and prove the cubic value-family for the actual two-atom corrected family stays off-diagonal.

That is the smallest live target now.

---

## 7. My honest assessment

This is the first version of the two-point attack that feels both:

- strong enough to matter, and
- small enough to plausibly prove from the current local formulas.

So the best next move is:

1. formulate the **actual two-atom cubic jet** \(J_{3,2}\) explicitly from the corrected local construction;
2. prove its local analytic dependence on normalized two-atom parameters;
3. prove diagonal collapse of its quotient class;
4. use \(v_0(h)\neq 0\) on \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}\) to exclude exact close two-point bad cores.

That is better-scoped than everything we were trying before, and it stays aligned with the draft’s current bottleneck structure.

## What I think is now proved, modulo one source-functoriality input

Let
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}.
\]
Assume there is an actual corrected cubic jet
\[
J_{3}^{\corr}[\mu_{12}] \in \mathcal J_3
\]
obtained by feeding the source-summed fields
\[
q_\mu=\sum a_i q_{h_i}, \qquad \Phi_\mu=\sum a_i \Phi_{h_i}
\]
into the same corrected local block construction, whitening, and cubic extraction used in the one-pair case.

Then:

### 1. Analytic dependence is automatic
Once \(J_{3}^{\corr}[\mu]\) is defined this way, the map
\[
(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\longmapsto J_{3}^{\corr}[\mu_{12}]
\]
is analytic on normalized compact good patches.

Reason: the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas are explicit analytic expressions in
\[
q_\mu(t_\pm),\ q'_\mu(t_\pm),\ q''_\mu(t_\pm),\ \Delta_\mu(s),
\]
and the whitening map is holomorphic on the uniformly positive-definite region. So cubic extraction is analytic as well.

Therefore the cubic quotient class
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
[J_{3}^{\corr}[\mu_{12}]]
\in \mathcal J_3/V_{\val}^{(3)}
\]
is continuous.

### 2. Diagonal collapse is automatic
If \(h_1=h_2=h\), then
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
\]
So source-functoriality gives
\[
J_{3}^{\corr}[\mu_{12}] = J_{3}^{\corr}[(a_1+a_2)\delta_h].
\]
And the weighted one-atom amplitude path is quotient-trivial in the ambient value/gauge quotient, so
\[
[J_{3}^{\corr}[(a_1+a_2)\delta_h]]
=
[J_3^{\pair}(h)]
=
v_0(h).
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
v_{0,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=v_0(h).
}
\]

### 3. Exact close two-point exclusion follows
If a normalized two-pair core is bad, its quotient odd germ is zero, so in particular
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0.
\]
Take a sequence of normalized bad two-pair cores with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J\Subset \mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}},
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
After passing to a convergent normalized subsequence,
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,\quad a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,\quad
h_{1,n}\to m,\quad h_{2,n}\to m.
\]
Continuity gives
\[
0=\lim_n v_{0,2}(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
= v_{0,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Diagonal collapse gives
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=v_0(m).
\]
But on \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}\), Proposition `prop:cubic-leading-order` gives
\[
v_0(m)=[J_3^{\pair}(m)]\neq 0.
\]
Contradiction.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the actual corrected two-atom cubic jet exists functorially, exact close bad two-point cores are excluded on }J\Subset \mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}.
}
\]

## The precise theorem to target now

The theorem I would try to prove next is this.

### Proposition (abstract corrected cubic jet functoriality)
Let \((q,\Phi)\) be any local datum on the microscopic disk satisfying the same regularity, symmetry, and positivity hypotheses used earlier for the corrected blocks and holomorphic whitening. Then the corrected local construction produces a cubic jet
\[
J_3^{\corr}[q,\Phi]\in \mathcal J_3
\]
depending analytically on \((q,\Phi)\).

Moreover, if two data sets \((q,\Phi)\) and \((\widetilde q,\widetilde \Phi)\) coincide, then
\[
J_3^{\corr}[q,\Phi]=J_3^{\corr}[\widetilde q,\widetilde \Phi].
\]

For a two-atom source
\[
\mu_{12}=a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2},
\]
set
\[
q_{\mu_{12}}:=a_1 q_{h_1}+a_2 q_{h_2},
\qquad
\Phi_{\mu_{12}}:=a_1 \Phi_{h_1}+a_2 \Phi_{h_2},
\]
and define
\[
J_{3,2}^{\corr}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=
J_3^{\corr}[q_{\mu_{12}},\Phi_{\mu_{12}}].
\]

Then \(J_{3,2}^{\corr}\) is analytic in the normalized two-atom parameters, and its cubic quotient class
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=
[J_{3,2}^{\corr}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)]
\in \mathcal J_3/V_{\val}^{(3)}
\]
is continuous.

If in addition the coincident-source identity
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h
\]
is respected by the construction and the weighted one-atom path is quotient-trivial, then
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=v_0(h).
\]

At that point, exact close two-point exclusion on \(J\Subset \mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}\) is immediate.

## Why this really is the smallest live gap

Because once the cubic jet is an actual source-functorial object, the rest is formal:

For a bad two-pair core, the quotient odd germ vanishes, so its cubic quotient class vanishes:
\[
v_{0,2}=0.
\]

Take a sequence of normalized bad two-pair cores with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,\qquad 0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
After passing to a convergent normalized subsequence,
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})\to(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Continuity gives
\[
0=v_{0,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Diagonal collapse gives
\[
v_{0,2}(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=v_0(m).
\]
But on \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{cub}}\), Proposition `prop:cubic-leading-order` gives
\[
v_0(m)\neq 0.
\]
Contradiction.

So the exact close two-point cubic branch is dead.

That means the hard part is no longer continuity or diagonal collapse themselves. It is only the **promotion** of the corrected local construction to an abstract local-datum functor.

## Why I think that promotion is the right thing to attack

Because the current obstruction I found earlier was against a **source-linear finite-order package**. That obstruction still stands.

But the corrected same-point block, corrected mixed block, and holomorphic whitening are already formulaic in \(q,\Phi\). They do not intrinsically require a one-pair source interpretation. So the natural move is to promote them as a local analytic machine acting on local data, not on amplitudes. Then source-functoriality becomes almost tautological.

In other words:

- the wrong target was “prove amplitude-linear decomposition”;
- the right target is “promote the corrected local block construction to a general local-datum functor, then apply it to the two-atom summed datum.”

That is the clean attack.

## What is still genuinely missing in the current draft

The current draft does **not** yet do this promotion explicitly.

It still packages the corrected local construction through the fixed anomaly-carrying core and the zeta-side corrected scalar, and the two-pair subsection still treats the source-level two-point input as missing. That matches your note. turn17file3

So the remaining gap is now very specific:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Promote the corrected local construction to an abstract local-datum construction, at least through cubic order.}
}
\]

Once that is done, I think the exact close two-point cubic branch is finished.

## My honest recommendation for the next move

The best move now is to add one new proposition earlier in the paper, before the one-pair quotient section:

**“Abstract corrected cubic jet for local data.”**

It should say, in essence:

given any admissible local datum \((q,\Phi)\), the corrected same-point/mixed/whitened construction produces an odd germ whose cubic jet depends analytically on \((q,\Phi)\), and this construction is functorial under equality of the underlying data.

Then the two-atom cubic object is defined by substitution
\[
(q,\Phi)=(q_{\mu_{12}},\Phi_{\mu_{12}}),
\]
and the exact close two-point cubic exclusion becomes a short corollary.

That is the strongest attack result I can defend right now.

I’m reading the current TeX around the corrected local construction and cubic-leading sections now, because the live question is whether the paper already gives enough to promote that machinery to a general local-datum cubic functor, or whether that really is a new lemma.

_Thought for 6m 44s_

I found the decisive correction to the last few attacks.

The exact quotient-diagonal bypass is **not** the right route.

The reason is simple and important: near a genuine close two-point bad branch on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the amplitudes do **not** approach a one-atom diagonal state. They approach the **collision-cancellation** state.

Write
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad a_1\neq 0.
\]
For a close bad core, the cubic identity is trying to force
\[
a_1 c(h_1)+a_2 c(h_2)\approx 0,
\]
so when \(h_1\approx h_2\) and \(c\neq 0\), one must have
\[
\lambda\approx 1,
\]
that is,
\[
a_1+a_2\approx 0.
\]

So the relevant limiting locus is not
\[
(h_1,h_2,\lambda)=(h,h,\text{arbitrary}),
\]
with collapse to \(F_h\). It is
\[
\boxed{\delta:=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda=1,}
\]
the coincident **zero-total-amplitude** locus.

That kills the earlier exact-route idea, because on that locus the source is not a one-atom source at all:
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h=0.
\]
So the diagonal limit there is \(0\), not \(F_h\).

Worse, this also explains why continuity across that locus is not a good primary target: the corrected same-point block scales like the source size, so when \(a_1+a_2\to 0\) the same-point block loses the positive-definite gap used for whitening. The “continuous two-atom quotient germ all the way to the diagonal” route was aimed at the wrong base point.

That is the real attack result.

So the best next route is now much clearer:

## Work in the normalized \((m,\delta,\lambda)\)-chart and target the collision-cancellation locus

Set
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad \lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}.
\]
The two-point branch you care about lives near
\[
\boxed{(\delta,\lambda)=(0,1).}
\]

That is the right local base point.

The correct theorem to try to prove is **not**
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
That now looks like the wrong chart.

The right theorem is a **joint vanishing theorem at the collision-cancellation locus** for the cubic and quintic defects.

The sharp version is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}\in (\delta^2,\ \delta(\lambda-1)).
}
\]

Equivalently, there should exist analytic \(K_3,L_3,K_5,L_5\) such that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\delta(\lambda-1)K_3+\delta^2L_3,
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}=\delta(\lambda-1)K_5+\delta^2L_5.
\]

That is now my best target.

Why this is the right theorem:

- it is centered at the actual relevant base locus \((\delta,\lambda)=(0,1)\);
- it is compatible with the even-in-amplitude obstruction;
- it only asks for cubic/quintic control, not septic;
- and it is already enough to kill the exact close two-point branch on good \(M\neq 0\) patches.

Here is why it would suffice.

From the cubic defect identity,
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)+E_{12}^{(3)}=0,
\]
divide by \(a_1\):
\[
c(h_1)-\lambda c(h_2)+e=0,
\qquad
e:=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1}.
\]
So
\[
(1-\lambda)c(h_2)=c(h_1)-c(h_2)+e.
\]
Now on a compact patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\),
\[
c(h_1)-c(h_2)=O(\delta).
\]
If
\[
e=\delta(\lambda-1)\widetilde K_3+\delta^2\widetilde L_3,
\]
then for small \(\delta\),
\[
(1-\lambda)c(h_2)=O(\delta)+\delta(\lambda-1)\widetilde K_3+\delta^2\widetilde L_3.
\]
Rearrange:
\[
(1-\lambda)\bigl(c(h_2)-\delta \widetilde K_3\bigr)=O(\delta).
\]
Since \(c(h_2)\neq 0\) and \(\delta\) is small,
\[
\boxed{\lambda-1=O(\delta).}
\]

Now plug that back into the joint vanishing theorem:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2).
\]

But then the existing corollary/theorem chain in the draft gives defect-scale closeness on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}\), and the \(x(h)=v_5(h)/c(h)\) bi-Lipschitz argument contradicts \(h_1\neq h_2\) for sufficiently small \(\delta\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
(\delta^2,\delta(\lambda-1))\text{-control at cubic/quintic level is enough to kill the close exact two-point branch.}
}
\]

That is a much better target than the old theorem.

It also explains why the recent structural updates are relevant. The note correctly says the two-point bottleneck is still the source-level reduction in the two-pair block, while the other branches are now better organized. turn21file3 The theorem above is exactly such a source-level reduction, but in the right local chart.

What would the proof mechanism be?

The natural heuristic is that near \((\delta,\lambda)=(0,1)\), the two-atom source has zero total mass at the collision point, so its first nontrivial local effect is dipolar. Formally,
\[
a_1\delta_{m-\delta/2}+a_2\delta_{m+\delta/2}
=
(a_1+a_2)\delta_m
+\frac{\delta}{2}(a_2-a_1)\partial_h\delta_m
+O(\delta^2).
\]
After normalization by \(a_1\), this says the relevant small parameters are exactly
\[
\lambda-1
\quad\text{and}\quad
\delta,
\]
and the first nontrivial corrected defects should vanish to at least mixed order
\[
\delta(\lambda-1)
\]
or pure order
\[
\delta^2.
\]

I would not put that formal distribution expansion into the paper as proof, but as an attack guide it is the clearest picture so far.

So my honest answer is:

The best way forward now is to abandon the full quotient-diagonal bypass and instead prove the joint vanishing theorem
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}\in (\delta^2,\delta(\lambda-1))
\]
in the normalized \((m,\delta,\lambda)\)-chart near \((0,1)\).

That is the first route I’ve found that is both compatible with the real limiting geometry and strong enough to finish the local close two-point exclusion without needing the full old source-linear theorem.

_Thought for 7m 32s_

I attacked the \((m,\delta,\lambda)\) route, and there is a real correction:

the theorem I suggested last time,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}\in (\delta^2,\delta(\lambda-1)),
\]
is **false as stated**.

The reason is immediate from the exact identities already in the draft. If
\[
h_1=h_2=m,\qquad \lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
then
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)+E_{12}^{(3)}=0
\]
becomes
\[
a_1(1-\lambda)c(m)+E_{12}^{(3)}=0,
\]
so
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=-a_1(1-\lambda)c(m),
\]
and similarly
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}=-a_1(1-\lambda)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
So those defects do **not** vanish on the whole diagonal \(\delta=0\). They only vanish on the actual collision-cancellation locus
\[
\delta=0,\qquad \lambda=1.
\]

That is the first correction.

The second correction is even more important: ordinary Taylor linearization at the zero-source point is also the wrong model, because the whitening step is scale-invariant to first order. If the local datum is scaled by a small factor \(\rho\), then the corrected same-point and mixed blocks are \(O(\rho)\), but the inverse square roots contribute \(O(\rho^{-1/2})\) on each side, so the whitened block is \(O(1)\). This is exactly the scale-cancellation obstruction we already found in the one-atom analysis.

So the correct local model is **not** an ordinary Taylor expansion at zero source.

The right local model is a **blow-up** of the cancellation point.

Write
\[
\mu:=\lambda-1,
\qquad
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\quad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},
\]
and then polarize the small parameters:
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta).
\]

Now look at the combined local datum \(D_h:=(q_h,\Phi_h)\). Then
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
D_{m-\delta/2}-(1+\mu)D_{m+\delta/2}
=
-\mu D_m-\delta D_m'+O\!\left((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\right).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\rho\bigl(\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'\bigr)+O(\rho^2).
\]

That is the clean attack formula.

Because the corrected same-point and mixed blocks are linear to first order in the datum while whitening kills the overall scale, the natural expectation is:

there should be a **blown-up limit family**
\[
\mathcal C_0(m,\theta),\qquad \mathcal Q_0(m,\theta),
\]
for the cubic and quintic corrected witnesses, obtained by letting \(\rho\to 0\) at fixed \((m,\theta)\). These limits should depend only on the projective source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}:=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]

That is now the best target.

So the correct replacement for my false ideal theorem is:

### Corrected renormalized residual theorem to aim for
Define
\[
\widetilde E_{12}^{(3)}
:=
E_{12}^{(3)}
+a_1\Bigl((1-\lambda)c(m)+\delta\,c'(m)\Bigr),
\]
and
\[
\widetilde E_{12}^{(5)}
:=
E_{12}^{(5)}
+a_1\Bigl((1-\lambda)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\delta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)\Bigr).
\]
Then the right mixed-order statement to try to prove is
\[
\widetilde E_{12}^{(3)},\ \widetilde E_{12}^{(5)}
\in
\bigl((\lambda-1)^2,\ \delta(\lambda-1),\ \delta^2\bigr).
\]

This one is compatible with the exact diagonal identities.

But even that is probably not the deepest formulation. The more intrinsic version is the blow-up statement:

### Best current target
Prove that after setting
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
the corrected cubic and quintic two-point outputs admit direction limits
\[
\mathcal C_0(m,\theta),\qquad \mathcal Q_0(m,\theta),
\]
and that these are exactly the cubic/quintic witnesses associated to the effective projective datum
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]

If that is true, then an exact close two-point bad branch would force
\[
\mathcal C_0(m,\theta)=0,\qquad \mathcal Q_0(m,\theta)=0
\]
for some \((m,\theta)\).

That is where the one-pair geometry comes back in.

At \(\theta=0\), the direction is \(D_m\), so the witnesses are the ordinary one-pair ones:
\[
\mathcal C_0(m,0)\sim c(m),\qquad \mathcal Q_0(m,0)\sim A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
Differentiating in \(\theta\) at \(0\) should bring in
\[
c'(m),\qquad (A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]

Now here is the key structural point:

if
\[
(c(m),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m))
\quad\text{and}\quad
(c'(m),(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m))
\]
were linearly dependent, then
\[
\left(\frac{A_5^{\mathfrak f}}{c}\right)'(m)=0.
\]
In particular,
\[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'(m)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)^2}=0.
\]
So on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
those two directions are linearly independent.

That means the projective source-direction family is genuinely moving in the strengthened two-point geometry. So the close two-point branch should not survive unless the blown-up limit family has some extra hidden degeneracy.

So the best way forward is now very specific:

### Best next theorem to attack
Prove a **blown-up cubic/quintic limit theorem at the collision-cancellation locus**:

for the actual corrected two-atom construction, the limit as \((\mu,\delta)\to(0,0)\) with fixed \(\theta\) exists after projectivization, and equals the corrected cubic/quintic witness of the effective datum
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]

That theorem is compatible with:
- the even-in-amplitude obstruction,
- the scale cancellation in whitening,
- and the actual limiting geometry of close bad two-point cores.

So the honest attack result is:

the old quadratic-factorization target still looks wrong for this chart, but there is now a much cleaner replacement. The two-point branch should be attacked by **blowing up the cancellation locus** and studying the projective source-direction family, not by trying to Taylor-expand through the singular zero-source point.

_Thought for 2m 27s_

Yes. I think I found the right reduced target.

The abstract “local-datum cubic functoriality” attack is still not enough, because it does not identify the cubic jet of the **actual bad two-pair quotient germ** with the cubic jet of the source-summed corrected local model. There is still a comparison gap there.

But that gap can be bypassed by targeting a much smaller statement that is exactly adapted to the real limiting geometry.

## The right reduced theorem

Work in the normalized chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad \mu:=\lambda-1.
\]

For an exact bad two-pair core, the cubic and quintic identities are
\[
c(h_1)-\lambda c(h_2)+e=0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_1)-\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_2)+E=0,
\]
where
\[
e:=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E:=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}.
\]

Now Taylor expand at \(m\):
\[
c\!\left(m-\frac{\delta}{2}\right)-\lambda c\!\left(m+\frac{\delta}{2}\right)
=
-\mu\,c(m)-\delta\,c'(m)+O(\rho^2),
\]
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\!\left(m-\frac{\delta}{2}\right)
-\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}\!\left(m+\frac{\delta}{2}\right)
=
-\mu\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)-\delta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)+O(\rho^2),
\]
with
\[
\rho:=|\mu|+|\delta|.
\]

So the exact bad-core equations become
\[
\mu\,c(m)+\delta\,c'(m)=e+O(\rho^2),
\]
\[
\mu\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\delta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)=E+O(\rho^2).
\]

This gives the clean target:

\[
\boxed{
e=O(\rho^2),
\qquad
E=O(\rho^2)
\quad\text{near }(\mu,\delta)=(0,0).
}
\]

That is the best theorem to attack next.

It is much weaker than the old quadratic factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2,
\]
and it is centered at the correct base locus \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\), not at the wrong one-atom diagonal.

## Why this is enough

Write
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)=u_5(h)I+v_5(h)S.
\]
Take the first and \(S\)-components of the two equations. Then
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
c(m) & c'(m)\\
v_5(m) & v_5'(m)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\mu}{\delta}
=
O(\rho^2).
\]

The determinant is
\[
c(m)v_5'(m)-c'(m)v_5(m)=M(m).
\]
So on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
this matrix is invertible. Therefore
\[
\binom{\mu}{\delta}=O(\rho^2).
\]
Hence
\[
\rho=O(\rho^2),
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero \(\rho\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }e=O(\rho^2)\text{ and }E=O(\rho^2)\text{ near }(\mu,\delta)=(0,0),
\text{ then exact close bad two-point cores are excluded on }J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}.
}
\]

This is a real reduction.

## Why this is better than the previous attacks

It avoids all the bad forks:

- no source-linear decomposition;
- no full quotient-germ continuity;
- no need to pass through the singular zero-source whitening limit directly;
- no septic input.

It only asks for a **first-order vanishing theorem for the normalized cubic/quintic defects** at the collision-cancellation locus.

That is the smallest live target I see now.

## What remains open

I do **not** think the draft currently proves
\[
e=O(\rho^2),\qquad E=O(\rho^2).
\]

But this is now the sharp problem.

The exact thing to prove is:

### Minimal two-point blow-up lemma
On normalized two-pair data near \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\),
\[
\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1}=O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr),
\qquad
\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr),
\]
uniformly on compact
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]

If that lemma lands, the close exact two-point branch is finished.

That is the best attack target now.

\mu\,c(m)+\delta\,c'(m)=e+O(\rho^2),

\mu\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\delta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)=E+O(\rho^2).

That is the key correction.

So after all these attacks, I think the picture is now:

- the continuity/diagonal-collapse bypass is too weak and was aimed at the wrong base point;
- the naive quadratic factorization is too strong and runs into the amplitude-scaling obstruction;
- the first-order blow-up of the exact identities alone is still not enough, because it only rewrites the branch equations.

This means the note’s diagnosis was basically right: the two-point bottleneck really is still a missing source-level reduction/factorization theorem, just in a more precise form than before. 

The smallest theorem that now looks genuinely nontrivial and genuinely sufficient is this:

## Best current target

Define the **interaction first blow-up coefficient** near the collision-cancellation locus by
\[
\mathfrak d(m,\theta)
:=
\lim_{\rho\to 0}
\frac1\rho
\begin{pmatrix}
e\\ e_v\\ \bar r
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
provided the limit exists, where \(e_v\) is the \(S\)-coefficient of \(E_{12}^{(5)}/a_1\) and \(\bar r\) is the normalized septic quotient defect.

Then an exact close bad two-point branch would force
\[
\mathfrak d(m,\theta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m)\\
\cos\theta\,v_5(m)+\sin\theta\,v_5'(m)\\
\text{the corresponding septic tangent term}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the real missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute or constrain the first blow-up coefficient of the actual interaction defects, and show it cannot equal the naive tangent vector on }J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}.
}
\]

That is strictly weaker than the old quadratic factorization theorem, but it is strong enough to kill the close exact two-point branch.

In other words, the live problem is no longer “prove \(O(\rho^2)\).”  
It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{identify the linear blow-up law of the interaction itself near }(\mu,\delta)=(0,0).
}
\]

That is the first place where the current algebra stops being tautological and where a real contradiction can start.

My strongest honest conclusion is: the two-point branch cannot be finished from the existing exact identities alone. One genuinely needs an independent first-order source-level theorem for the interaction defects near the collision-cancellation locus.

This is important for other routes because it tells you exactly what cannot work: no argument based only on the planar geometry of (x,S) can kill the 4-point branch. So if the mixed side closes, it will also have to use either:

the centered parity transfer,
the patch dichotomy,
or genuine source-level coupling between the Y- and S-channels.

That is a real strategic constraint, not just a nonmixed fact.

Third, the first-loss rigidification is conceptually useful for the mixed side. In the nonmixed case it says first loss of quadratic-envelope monotonicity forces a sheared repeated-node 3-point tangency configuration. Even though that did not completely solve the global nonmixed problem, it gives a model for what to look for on the mixed side: if you can build the right regularized repeated-node profile there, a first-loss event may similarly rigidify into a lower-core tangency mechanism.

m
	​

5
	​

-patch coordinate, the same kind of weighted-average / implicit-function computation may be the right way to attack the three low-order mixed obstruction types individually.

_Thought for 4m 37s_

Yes. I think there is a real upgrade to the attack.

The important new point is this: the latest draft’s two-pair quantitative theorem is already telling us the **right objects** to control, and they are **not** the raw defects \(e,e_u,e_v\) individually. That fits the nonmixed source-determinant lesson you flagged: the right below-lifted language is finite minors and their ratios, not raw coefficient bookkeeping. turn29file2

Here is the key observation.

From the exact two-pair coincidence theorem and the quantitative defect-thickened theorem, the strengthened differences are controlled by these exact combinations:
\[
D_u(h_1,h_2):=c(h_1)u_5(h_2)-c(h_2)u_5(h_1),
\]
\[
D_v(h_1,h_2):=c(h_1)v_5(h_2)-c(h_2)v_5(h_1),
\]
and
\[
N_\Delta(h_1,h_2):=\Delta_7(h_1)c(h_2)^2-\Delta_7(h_2)c(h_1)^2.
\]

These are exactly the source minors for the strengthened data:
\[
D_u=c_1c_2\,(Y_2-Y_1),\qquad
D_v=c_1c_2\,(x_2-x_1),\qquad
N_\Delta=c_1^2c_2^2\,(S_1-S_2),
\]
where
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c^2}.
\]

And the quantitative theorem rewrites them as the **interaction minors**
\[
D_u=c_2 e_u-u_{5,2}e,
\qquad
D_v=c_2 e_v-v_{5,2}e,
\]
while \(N_\Delta\) is given by the explicit septic interaction numerator from the theorem.

This is much better than the older attack targets, because these minors vanish identically on the true diagonal \(h_1=h_2\) regardless of \(\lambda=-a_2/a_1\). So they are the right “collision-compatible” objects. The raw defects themselves do not have that property.

Now expand near the diagonal. With
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,
\]
the antisymmetry gives
\[
D_v(h_1,h_2)=M(m)\,\delta+O(\delta^3),
\]
\[
D_u(h_1,h_2)=W(c,u_5)(m)\,\delta+O(\delta^3),
\]
and
\[
N_\Delta(h_1,h_2)=-\,c(m)^4\,S'(m)\,\delta+O(\delta^3).
\]

So the natural secant ratios are
\[
\Sigma_Y(h_1,h_2):=\frac{D_u}{D_v}
=\frac{Y(h_2)-Y(h_1)}{x(h_2)-x(h_1)}
\longrightarrow \frac{dY}{dx}(m),
\]
and
\[
\Sigma_S(h_1,h_2):=-\,\frac{N_\Delta}{c_1c_2\,D_v}
=\frac{S(h_2)-S(h_1)}{x(h_2)-x(h_1)}
\longrightarrow \frac{dS}{dx}(m),
\]
whenever \(M(m)\neq 0\).

This is the two-point analogue of the nonmixed source-determinant picture. Instead of chasing raw defects, we should chase the **interaction ratios**
\[
\Sigma_Y^{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\frac{c_2 e_u-u_{5,2}e}{c_2 e_v-v_{5,2}e},
\]
and
\[
\Sigma_S^{\mathrm{int}}
:=
-\,\frac{\text{septic interaction numerator}}{c_1c_2\,(c_2 e_v-v_{5,2}e)}.
\]

For an exact bad two-pair core, these equal the source secant ratios:
\[
\Sigma_Y^{\mathrm{int}}=\Sigma_Y,\qquad
\Sigma_S^{\mathrm{int}}=\Sigma_S.
\]

That is the real reduced problem now.

So the best next theorem to attack is:

**Source-minor ratio theorem for the mixed two-point branch.**  
Show that on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the interaction ratios \(\Sigma_Y^{\mathrm{int}},\Sigma_S^{\mathrm{int}}\) cannot simultaneously converge to
\[
\frac{dY}{dx}(m),\qquad \frac{dS}{dx}(m)
\]
along a nontrivial close two-point bad branch, unless the branch rigidifies into a lower-core tangency mechanism.

That formulation is better for three reasons.

First, it uses exactly the combinations the draft already cares about.

Second, it matches the new nonmixed lesson: work with source minors and ratio geometry below the lifted variables. 

Third, it respects the warning from `R-free-over-fixed-S`: you will not kill the branch from a single planar channel. You need simultaneous \(Y\)- and \(S\)-coupling. This ratio pair does exactly that. 

So my current best attack plan is:

1. Recast the two-pair quantitative theorem explicitly in terms of the three minors \(D_u,D_v,N_\Delta\).

2. State the two secant ratios \(\Sigma_Y,\Sigma_S\) as the mixed two-point analogue of the nonmixed \(\Psi_a\)-type source-minor ratio.

3. Try to prove a first-loss/limit theorem: if a close exact two-point bad branch exists, then the interaction ratio pair must approach the derivative pair
\[
\left(\frac{dY}{dx},\frac{dS}{dx}\right)(m).
\]

4. Then use the new 3-point / nonmixed-4-point rigidification philosophy to show that such a limit forces a lower-core tangency or branch transition, contradicting the assumed pure two-point branch. turn29file2

So the attack has changed shape:

not “prove \(e,E,\bar E\) are quadratic,”  
but “prove the interaction **minor ratios** cannot realize the source secant/derivative ratios on a genuine mixed two-point branch.”

That is the first route I’ve seen that is both compatible with the latest draft and materially stronger than the dead ends we tried earlier.

_Thought for 5m 1s_

Yes. I think there is a real step forward now.

The best attack is to stop working with the raw defects separately and instead package the exact two-point equations into a **source-minor line-data theorem**. That is the clean two-point analogue of the nonmixed source-determinant viewpoint you flagged, and it also respects the warning that \((x,S)\)-only geometry cannot be enough. turn31file2

Write
\[
s(h):=(c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h))\in\mathbf C^3,
\qquad
s_i:=s(h_i)=(c_i,u_i,v_i),
\]
and for an exact bad two-pair core set
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
d:=(e,e_u,e_v):=\frac1{a_1}\bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},\text{$I$-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)},\text{$S$-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)}\bigr).
\]
Then the exact cubic/quintic defect identities in the draft are simply
\[
d=\lambda s_2-s_1.
\]
That looks trivial, but it immediately yields the right source-minor package:

\[
s_2\times d=s_1\times s_2.
\]

This is the exact algebraic identity I think we should now organize the two-point attack around.

Writing out the components gives three exact minors:
\[
c_2e_u-u_2e = c_1u_2-c_2u_1,
\]
\[
c_2e_v-v_2e = c_1v_2-c_2v_1,
\]
\[
u_2e_v-v_2e_u = u_1v_2-v_1u_2.
\]

The first two are already hiding inside the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem; the third one is the new useful “goodie.” It is the missing \(u/v\)-minor, and it completes the exact \(3\)-vector source-minor picture.

Now divide by the nonzero mixed denominator
\[
D_v:=c_1v_2-c_2v_1=c_2e_v-v_2e.
\]
On \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}\), this is nonzero for sufficiently close distinct points because
\[
D_v=c_1c_2\,(x_2-x_1),\qquad x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(x'\neq 0\) there.

Then define
\[
\Sigma_Y:=\frac{c_2e_u-u_2e}{c_2e_v-v_2e}
=\frac{c_1u_2-c_2u_1}{c_1v_2-c_2v_1}
=\frac{Y_2-Y_1}{x_2-x_1},
\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c}.
\]
So \(\Sigma_Y\) is exactly the secant slope of \(Y\) against \(x\), but expressed purely as an interaction/source-minor ratio.

And the third minor gives the secant intercept:
\[
B_Y:=\frac{u_2e_v-v_2e_u}{c_2e_v-v_2e}
=\frac{u_1v_2-v_1u_2}{c_1v_2-c_2v_1}
=Y_1-\Sigma_Y x_1
=Y_2-\Sigma_Y x_2.
\]

So for every exact bad two-pair core on a good \(M\neq 0\) patch, the line
\[
Y=\Sigma_Y x+B_Y
\]
through the two strengthened points is encoded entirely by finite source minors of \((c,u_5,v_5)\) and the interaction vector \(d\).

That is the first real structural improvement.

At septic level, the draft’s exact formula already gives
\[
S_1-S_2
=
-\frac{\mathcal N_{12}}{c_1^2c_2^2},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c^2},
\]
where \(\mathcal N_{12}\) is the explicit septic interaction numerator from the theorem. Dividing again by \(x_2-x_1=D_v/(c_1c_2)\), you get the exact secant slope
\[
\Sigma_S
:=
\frac{S_2-S_1}{x_2-x_1}
=
-\frac{\mathcal N_{12}}{c_1c_2\,D_v}.
\]
Then
\[
B_S:=S_1-\Sigma_S x_1=S_2-\Sigma_S x_2
\]
is the secant intercept in the \(x\)-\(S\) plane.

So an exact bad two-pair core canonically determines the full secant line in lifted space:
\[
Y=\Sigma_Y x+B_Y,\qquad S=\Sigma_S x+B_S,
\]
and every coefficient here is a finite source-minor ratio.

As \(h_2\to h_1\) on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}\),
\[
\Sigma_Y\to \frac{dY}{dx}(m),\qquad
B_Y\to Y(m)-x(m)\frac{dY}{dx}(m),
\]
\[
\Sigma_S\to \frac{dS}{dx}(m),\qquad
B_S\to S(m)-x(m)\frac{dS}{dx}(m).
\]
So a close exact two-point bad branch forces these interaction-defined secant-line data to converge to the tangent-line data of the lifted curve
\[
x\longmapsto (Y(x),S(x)).
\]

This is exactly the sort of “below-lifted” source-minor language suggested by the new nonmixed material. It also shows why my earlier attacks on raw defects were too clumsy: the true invariant objects are these line-data ratios, not \(e,e_u,e_v\) individually. turn31file2

What this does **not** yet do is kill the two-point branch by itself. And the latest nonmixed no-go remark explains why: planar geometry of \((x,S)\) alone cannot exclude the branch, so a successful mixed argument has to use genuine \(Y\)-\(S\) coupling or parity/dichotomy input. 

So the best next target is now very specific:

prove that these interaction-defined secant-line data cannot converge to the tangent-line data of the strengthened curve on a genuine mixed two-point branch without forcing a lower-core tangency mechanism. In other words, try to turn the exact line-data identities
\[
(\Sigma_Y,B_Y,\Sigma_S,B_S)
\]
into a repeated-node/tangent rigidification statement, the same way the nonmixed branch is now controlled by source-minor ratios and first-loss tangency structure. turn31file2

So the current best “attack theorem” is:

for an exact bad two-pair core on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}\), the strengthened secant line is encoded by finite source minors; if a close exact two-point bad branch exists, those minor ratios converge to the tangent-line data of the lifted strengthened curve. The remaining mixed obstruction is to show that such tangent-line realization is incompatible with genuine two-point persistence unless the branch degenerates into a lower-core tangency.

That is the strongest honest progress I can defend from the latest draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 17:49:41)

I’m pushing directly on the secant-line route now. The key question is whether the exact line-data identities plus the newer derivative geometry are already enough to force a lower-core tangency, or whether one more genuinely mixed input is still missing.

_Thought for 3m 50s_

I attacked it, and this gives a genuinely useful conclusion.

The secant-line/source-minor route is **not strong enough by itself** to close the mixed two-point branch.

But now we can say exactly why.

## The key blow-up formula

Let
\[
s(h):=(c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h))\in\mathbf C^3,
\qquad
s_i:=s(h_i),
\]
and for an exact bad two-pair core write
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
d:=(e,e_u,e_v):=\frac1{a_1}\bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},\,I\text{-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)},\,S\text{-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)}\bigr).
\]
Then the exact cubic/quintic defect equations are
\[
d=\lambda s_2-s_1.
\]

Now go to the close-point chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Taylor-expand:
\[
s_1=s(m)-\frac{\delta}{2}s'(m)+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
s_2=s(m)+\frac{\delta}{2}s'(m)+O(\delta^2).
\]
Substitute into \(d=\lambda s_2-s_1\):
\[
d
=
\Bigl(1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2)\Bigr)
\Bigl(s+\frac{\delta}{2}s'+O(\delta^2)\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(s-\frac{\delta}{2}s'+O(\delta^2)\Bigr).
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
d=\delta\bigl(\alpha\,s(m)+s'(m)\bigr)+O(\delta^2).
}
\]

This is the correct first-order repeated-node profile for the mixed two-point branch.

It is the same kind of “sheared repeated-node” structure you were pointing to from the nonmixed side, but now in the source vector \(s=(c,u_5,v_5)\).

## Why the secant-line minors cannot finish the job

The exact source-minor identity I wrote before is
\[
s_2\times d=s_1\times s_2.
\]
At first order, using the blow-up formula,
\[
s_2\times d
=
\Bigl(s+\frac{\delta}{2}s'+O(\delta^2)\Bigr)\times
\Bigl(\delta(\alpha s+s')+O(\delta^2)\Bigr).
\]
Hence
\[
s_2\times d
=
\delta\,(s\times s')+\alpha\delta\,(s\times s)+O(\delta^2)
=
\delta\,(s\times s')+O(\delta^2),
\]
because \(s\times s=0\).

So the first-order minors are
\[
\boxed{
s_2\times d=\delta\,(s\times s')+O(\delta^2),
}
\]
and the shear parameter \(\alpha\) disappears.

That is the decisive point.

Every line-data quantity we built from those minors — for example
\[
\Sigma_Y=\frac{c_2e_u-u_2e}{c_2e_v-v_2e},
\qquad
B_Y=\frac{u_2e_v-v_2e_u}{c_2e_v-v_2e},
\]
and the septic secant slope/intercept
\[
\Sigma_S,\qquad B_S,
\]
depends only on these wedge-type minors. Therefore all of them are **blind to \(\alpha\) at first order**.

Equivalently, along a close exact bad two-point branch they converge to the ordinary tangent-line data of the strengthened curve:
\[
\Sigma_Y\to \frac{dY}{dx}(m),
\qquad
B_Y\to Y(m)-x(m)\frac{dY}{dx}(m),
\]
\[
\Sigma_S\to \frac{dS}{dx}(m),
\qquad
B_S\to S(m)-x(m)\frac{dS}{dx}(m),
\]
and none of these quantities sees the repeated-node shear.

So the secant-line/source-minor route is a **good reorganization**, but not a closure theorem.

## What this means structurally

This is actually very informative.

It says the mixed two-point branch has a genuine first-order hidden parameter:
\[
\alpha=\lim \frac{\lambda-1}{\delta},
\]
and the whole finite source-minor line data package is first-order **\(\alpha\)-blind**.

That matches the strategic warning from the new nonmixed material:

- planar or ratio geometry alone is not enough;
- you need an extra coupling that does not quotient out the repeated-node shear.

So the current attack has produced a real no-go principle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any argument based only on the first-order source minors / secant-line data cannot kill the mixed close two-point branch.}
}
\]

## What the next target has to be

The next viable theorem must be **shear-sensitive**.

The blow-up formula
\[
d=\delta(\alpha s+s')+O(\delta^2)
\]
shows exactly what kind of quantity can work: something that sees the \(s\)-component of the blow-up vector, not just its wedge with \(s\).

So the best next target is an invariant or source-level coupling that is sensitive to
\[
\alpha s+s'
\quad\text{modulo nothing},
\]
not merely to
\[
s\times(\alpha s+s')=s\times s'.
\]

Concretely, you want a scalar or vector built from the actual interaction defects that does **not** kill the \(s\)-direction. For example, on a good \(M\neq 0\) patch, the first and third components already let you recover \(\alpha\) formally:
\[
\begin{pmatrix} e\\ e_v \end{pmatrix}
=
\delta
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha c+c'\\
\alpha v_5+v_5'
\end{pmatrix}
+O(\delta^2),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{e\,v_5'(m)-e_v\,c'(m)}{\delta\,M(m)}
+O(1).
}
\]
This is exactly the repeated-node shear parameter hidden by the secant minors.

So the right sort of missing theorem is one that constrains this \(\alpha\) using an independent channel — most likely septic / \(Y\)-\(S\) coupling, parity transfer, or a repeated-node local model analogous to the nonmixed first-loss rigidification.

## Best current attack theorem

The best next theorem to try to prove is:

**Shear-sensitive blow-up theorem for the mixed two-point branch.**  
Along any close exact bad two-point branch on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the normalized defect vector has an expansion
\[
d=\delta(\alpha s+s')+O(\delta^2),
\]
and the septic / mixed source-level coupling forces \(\alpha\) to satisfy a constraint incompatible with persistence of a genuine two-point branch.

That is now the smallest nontrivial target I trust.

## Bottom line

This attack did not close the branch.

But it did produce a strong structural fact:

- the secant-line/source-minor ratios are the right below-lifted language for organizing the branch;
- however, they are first-order blind to the actual repeated-node shear;
- so any successful mixed two-point proof must use a **shear-sensitive** coupling, not just source minors or tangent-line data.

That is a real advance, because it tells us exactly what kind of argument cannot work, and exactly what new ingredient has to be sought.
