## Assistant (2026-04-20 17:55:14)

I’m going straight at the shear-sensitive route now. The goal is to see whether the current cubic/quintic/septic identities already pin down the repeated-node shear \(\alpha\), or whether one genuinely new mixed coupling is still needed.

_Thought for 4m 39s_

I attacked it, and this produces a clean no-go theorem.

The new source-minor / secant-line language is genuinely useful, but it cannot by itself close the mixed two-point branch.

The reason is stronger than the first-order calculation I gave before:

## Exact \(\lambda\)-blindness of the source-minor package

Let
\[
s(h):=(c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h))\in \mathbf C^3,
\qquad
s_i:=s(h_i),
\]
and for an exact bad two-pair core define
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
d:=(e,e_u,e_v):=\frac1{a_1}
\Bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},\ I\text{-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)},\ S\text{-coeff of }E_{12}^{(5)}\Bigr).
\]
Then the exact cubic/quintic defect equations in the draft are
\[
\boxed{
d=\lambda s_2-s_1.
}
\]

Now take any wedge-type source minor involving \(d\) and \(s_2\). Since
\[
s_2\wedge d=s_2\wedge(\lambda s_2-s_1)=-\,s_2\wedge s_1=s_1\wedge s_2,
\]
every such minor is **exactly independent of \(\lambda\)**.

So this is not just a first-order blindness to the repeated-node shear. It is an **all-orders exact blindness**.

That means:

- the cubic/quintic minors
  \[
  c_2e_u-u_2e,\qquad c_2e_v-v_2e,\qquad u_2e_v-v_2e_u
  \]
  are exactly source secants, hence exactly \(\lambda\)-blind;

- any ratios built from them, such as
  \[
  \Sigma_Y,\ B_Y,
  \]
  are exactly \(\lambda\)-blind;

- the analogous secant-line packaging for \((x,S)\) is also \(\lambda\)-blind, because it is built from source secants and the septic numerator only after quotienting in the same secant-compatible way.

So the secant-line/source-minor route is a very good **organization** of the branch, but not a closure theorem.

This matches the strategic warning in the updated draft and your note: ratio language is the right below-lifted language, but planar or quotientized source-minor geometry alone cannot kill the mixed branch; one needs extra coupling that does not throw away the repeated-node shear. turn26file1

## The concrete consequence

Any argument that only sees
\[
s_1\wedge s_2
\quad\text{or}\quad
s_2\wedge d
\]
and ratios of those minors can never determine \(\lambda\), hence can never kill the mixed two-point branch.

So the current attack has identified an exact no-go principle:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No proof based only on cubic/quintic source minors and their secant-line ratios can exclude the mixed close two-point branch.}
}
\]

That is a real result.

## What a successful argument must now use

It has to be **shear-sensitive**.

Since the minor package kills the \(s_2\)-direction in
\[
d=\lambda s_2-s_1,
\]
the next invariant must depend on \(d\) itself, not only on its wedge with \(s_2\).

There are really only two plausible places this can come from.

### 1. A gauge-fixed septic representative

The septic equation in the draft is not just a scalar secant identity; it involves a representative
\[
R\in \mathfrak f
\]
of the quotient defect. The quotientized scalar
\[
\frac{\Delta_1}{c_1^2}-\frac{\Delta_2}{c_2^2}
\]
is secant-like and hence \(\lambda\)-blind in the same way, but the representative \(R\) itself is not obviously \(\lambda\)-blind.

So the best next attack is:

choose a **canonical gauge** for \(R\) relative to \(A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}\), turning the septic quotient defect into an actual vector-valued invariant
\[
R^\sharp
\]
rather than just a class or determinant scalar. Then study the first blow-up law of \(R^\sharp\) near the repeated-node limit.

That is the most promising shear-sensitive object currently visible in the draft.

### 2. A parity-transferred local model on the actual mixed coordinate

Your note also points to the odd/even local classification via \(J_m(\lambda)\) as a reusable template once parity is transferred to the actual mixed coordinate. That route could produce a local repeated-node profile whose first nontrivial coefficient is shear-sensitive, unlike the secant minors. turn26file1

So the realistic fork is now:

- either build a **canonical septic representative** and use it to read the shear;
- or import the parity/local-model machinery to the mixed coordinate and get a shear-sensitive repeated-node expansion there.

## Best next theorem to attack

The cleanest next target is this.

### Candidate theorem
Fix a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
For an exact bad two-pair core, choose the unique representative
\[
R^\sharp\in \mathfrak f
\]
of the septic quotient defect satisfying a normalization such as
\[
\det(R^\sharp,A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f})=0
\]
or an equivalent canonical gauge condition.

Then along any close mixed two-point bad branch,
\[
R^\sharp
\]
has a first-order blow-up law that depends on the repeated-node shear
\[
\alpha=\lim\frac{\lambda-1}{h_2-h_1},
\]
and the exact septic identity forces \(\alpha\) to satisfy a constraint incompatible with persistence of a genuine two-point branch.

That is now the smallest theorem I actually believe could work.

## Bottom line

So the attack result is:

- the new source-minor / ratio language is correct and useful;
- but it is **exactly** blind to the shear parameter, not just approximately;
- therefore it cannot close the mixed two-point branch by itself;
- the next viable route has to use a shear-sensitive invariant, most naturally a gauge-fixed septic representative or parity-transferred repeated-node local model.

That is the strongest honest advance I can defend from the latest draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:03:09)

I’m checking the latest draft against the shear-sensitive idea rather than free-associating. The question now is whether the current septic quotient machinery already contains a canonical representative or normalization that can see the repeated-node shear, or whether that really is still missing.

_Thought for 5m 11s_

I pushed this as far as the current draft lets me, and I think the right conclusion is now very sharp:

## New no-go result

A **canonical representative of the septic quotient defect cannot save the two-point branch** if it is built only from the quotient class and \(A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\).

Why:

The fixed sector \(\mathfrak f\) is 2-dimensional, while the septic quotient lives in
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f},
\]
which is 1-dimensional. So once you know the line \( \mathbf C A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\), every quotient class has only **one scalar degree of freedom**.

Concretely, write
\[
A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}=u_1 I+v_1 S,
\qquad
J(u,v):=(-v,u).
\]
Then for any representative \(R\in\mathfrak f\), the quotient class \([R]\) is completely determined by the scalar
\[
\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}).
\]
Indeed the unique Euclidean-orthogonal representative of \([R]\) is
\[
\boxed{
R^\perp
=
\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{\|A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\|^2}\,
J A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

So any “canonical gauge-fixed representative” built only from \([R]\) and \(A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\) carries **no more information** than the scalar determinant already appearing in the quantitative two-pair theorem.

That means it is still stuck in the same secant/quotient package, and therefore it is still blind to the repeated-node shear.

## Why this matters for the current theorem chain

From the current two-pair formulas, the cubic/quintic defect vector
\[
d=(e,e_u,e_v)
\]
satisfies
\[
d=\lambda s_2-s_1,
\qquad
s_i=(c_i,u_i,v_i),
\]
so every cubic/quintic source minor built from \(s_2\) and \(d\) is exactly
\[
s_2\wedge d=s_1\wedge s_2,
\]
hence exactly \(\lambda\)-blind.

The septic part that survives into the theorem is only
\[
\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}),
\]
and by the observation above, any canonical representative extracted from \([R]\) and \(A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\) still depends only on that same scalar.

So the whole current “below-lifted” two-point package

- cubic/quintic source minors,
- their secant-line ratios,
- and any canonical representative derived only from the septic quotient class,

is **exactly shear-blind**.

That is stronger than what I said before. It is not merely first-order blindness. It is an exact structural no-go.

This fits the strategic warning from the nonmixed side: planar or quotientized source-minor geometry alone cannot close the branch; one needs an additional source-level coupling that is not lost under the current quotientization. turn33file3

## The hidden variable is now explicit

There is a clean way to name what the quotient is throwing away.

Because \(\mathfrak f\) is 2D, every septic fixed-sector vector decomposes uniquely as
\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\eta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}
+
\frac{\Delta_7}{\|A_5^{\mathfrak f}\|^2}\,J A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

The second term is the quotient-visible part: it is exactly what \(\Delta_7\) records.

The first term is the **longitudinal coefficient**
\[
\eta.
\]

And \(\eta\) is precisely what the quotient kills.

Under the projected septic gauge law,
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+c_2A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
so
\[
\eta\mapsto \eta+c_2,
\]
while \(\Delta_7\) stays invariant.

So the two-point mixed obstruction is now extremely concrete:

- everything we currently control in the draft sees only the transverse quotient part;
- the repeated-node shear lives in the longitudinal direction;
- therefore a successful proof has to control the longitudinal coefficient \(\eta\), or some canonical comparison of it, by an extra source-level or parity-transferred mechanism.

## Best next attack

The next viable theorem is no longer about \(R^\perp\) or any quotient-derived representative.

It is:

### Shear-sensitive longitudinal theorem
Define the pre-quotient septic difference
\[
\Xi:=A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}-\lambda A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Decompose it relative to \(A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\):
\[
\Xi = L\,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f} + T\,J A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The current draft controls \(T\) through the quotient/septic determinant data.  
What is missing is a theorem controlling the **longitudinal coefficient**
\[
L.
\]

That is the first shear-sensitive scalar.

Near a close mixed two-point branch,
\[
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2),
\]
and one gets
\[
\Xi=-\delta\bigl(\alpha A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)+(A_7^{\mathfrak f})'(m)\bigr)+O(\delta^2),
\]
so \(L\) is exactly where the repeated-node shear \(\alpha\) survives.

If you can constrain \(L\) by parity transfer, source-level coupling, or a repeated-node local model, then the branch becomes attackable. If you stay only in the quotient/septic determinant language, it does not.

## Bottom line

The current attack produced a real theorem-strength structural fact:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any argument using only the present cubic/quintic source minors and the septic quotient class is exactly shear-blind.}
}
\]

So the next move is no longer to refine those same invariants.

The next move is to introduce a **longitudinal septic variable** — explicitly or implicitly — and prove a constraint on it.

That is now the cleanest and smallest live target I can see.

_Thought for 2m 46s_

I checked the latest draft, and I think this attack now reaches a clean conclusion:

the **longitudinal septic coefficient is not an intrinsic object** in the current setup, so the route “control the longitudinal coefficient \(L\)” is dead unless you add a genuinely new cross-point gauge choice.

Here is the exact reason.

Let
\[
A_{5,i}:=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_i),\qquad A_{7,i}:=A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h_i),
\]
and on an exact bad two-pair core write
\[
A_{5,1}=\lambda A_{5,2}.
\]
The draft’s projected septic gauge law is
\[
A_{7,i}\mapsto A_{7,i}+\beta_i A_{5,i},
\]
and the raw representative is explicitly described as noncanonical, with only local auxiliary gauge-fixes like \(v_7=0\) or \(u_7=0\) on a patch. The handoff note is also still consistent with the two-point bottleneck being source-level rather than already closed. 

Now define the pre-quotient two-point septic difference
\[
\Xi:=A_{7,1}-\lambda A_{7,2}.
\]
Under independent gauges at the two points,
\[
\Xi\mapsto \Xi+\beta_1 A_{5,1}-\lambda \beta_2 A_{5,2}
      = \Xi+(\beta_1-\beta_2)A_{5,1}.
\]

So if you decompose \(\Xi\) relative to \(A_{5,1}\) as
\[
\Xi=L\,A_{5,1}+T\,J A_{5,1},
\]
then

\[
T \text{ is invariant,}
\qquad
L\mapsto L+(\beta_1-\beta_2).
\]

That is the decisive obstruction.

The transverse coefficient \(T\) is exactly the quotient-visible part, equivalently the determinant part already encoded by \(\Delta_7\) or the septic quotient class. But the longitudinal coefficient \(L\) is completely gauge-dependent: by choosing \(\beta_1-\beta_2\) arbitrarily, you can shift \(L\) arbitrarily.

So there is **no intrinsic theorem about \(L\)** available from the present quotient package alone.

That also explains why the local gauge-fixing remark in the draft does not rescue this route. On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, setting \(v_7=0\) gives
\[
u_7^{\new}=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
and on a \(u_5\neq 0\) patch, setting \(u_7=0\) gives
\[
v_7^{\new}=-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5}.
\]
But those are just pointwise gauge sections for the already quotient-visible septic data. They do not canonically compare two different points, and they do not produce a shear-sensitive invariant beyond what \(\Delta_7\) already sees.

So the current attack yields a stronger no-go statement than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The present cubic/quintic source minors plus the septic quotient class see only the transverse part of } \Xi,
\text{ never the longitudinal part.}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any proof that only uses the existing quotient-level septic machinery is exactly blind to the repeated-node shear.}
}
\]

That is now the clean structural fact.

What this means for the next attack is also clearer.

A successful mixed two-point argument must add one extra ingredient that couples the gauges at \(h_1\) and \(h_2\). There are only two realistic ways I can see:

First, a **pre-quotient transport law**.  
You would need a canonically chosen smooth gauge section along a patch, not just pointwise gauge-fixing. Then the difference
\[
\Xi^{\sharp}=A_{7,1}^{\sharp}-\lambda A_{7,2}^{\sharp}
\]
would become meaningful, and its longitudinal component could carry the shear.

Second, a **parity-transferred mixed local model**.  
Instead of comparing raw septic representatives directly, you build a repeated-node normal form in the actual mixed coordinate, where the shear appears as a genuine coefficient before quotienting ever happens.

Of those two, the first now looks like the sharpest theorem to target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Construct a canonical smooth septic gauge section on a }v_5\neq 0\text{ or }u_5\neq 0\text{ patch, and compute the two-point transport defect in that gauge.}
}
\]

That would be genuinely new. Without it, the longitudinal variable is not well-defined enough to attack.

So the honest outcome of this attack is:

- the longitudinal idea was the right thing to probe;
- after checking the latest draft, it is **not** currently a viable invariant;
- the next viable target is not “prove something about \(L\)” but “create a cross-point gauge transport that makes \(L\) meaningful.”

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:17:17)

I’m going after the only route that still looks live: can the draft’s existing patchwise septic gauge choices be upgraded into a cross-point transport law strong enough to make the hidden shear meaningful, without inventing an entirely new object.

_Thought for 4m 17s_

Yes. I pushed the attack one level further, and this gives a clean new no-go result.

The natural “cross-point gauge transport” you would try first is the one the draft already uses on good patches:

- on a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, choose the local septic gauge \(v_7=0\);
- on a \(u_5\neq 0\) patch, choose the local septic gauge \(u_7=0\).

That looks like it might make the hidden longitudinal direction meaningful across two points.

But it does not.

On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch, the gauge \(v_7=0\) gives the canonical pointwise representative
\[
A_7^\sharp(h)=u_7^\sharp(h)\,I,
\qquad
u_7^\sharp(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}=c(h)\,\sigma_v(h).
\]

Now take an exact bad two-pair core and write, as in the quantitative two-pair theorem,
\[
A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}+R+\eta A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{5,1}I+v_{5,1}S,
\qquad
R=r_u I+r_v S.
\]

Use the **same** \(v_7=0\) gauge at both points. Then
\[
A_{7,1}^\sharp=\frac{\Delta_1}{v_{5,1}}\,I,
\qquad
A_{7,2}^\sharp=\frac{\Delta_2}{v_{5,2}}\,I,
\]
so
\[
A_{7,1}^\sharp-\lambda A_{7,2}^\sharp
=
\left(\frac{\Delta_1}{v_{5,1}}-\lambda\frac{\Delta_2}{v_{5,2}}\right)I.
\]

But the same two-point equation still has to hold in this gauge:
\[
A_{7,1}^\sharp=\lambda A_{7,2}^\sharp+R+\eta A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Comparing \(S\)-components gives
\[
0=r_v+\eta v_{5,1},
\qquad
\eta=-\frac{r_v}{v_{5,1}}.
\]
Then comparing \(I\)-components gives
\[
\frac{\Delta_1}{v_{5,1}}-\lambda\frac{\Delta_2}{v_{5,2}}
=
r_u-\frac{u_{5,1}}{v_{5,1}}\,r_v
=
\frac{r_u v_{5,1}-u_{5,1}r_v}{v_{5,1}}
=
\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{v_{5,1}}.
\]

So the transported septic difference in the \(v_7=0\) gauge is **exactly**
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\Delta_1}{v_{5,1}}-\lambda\frac{\Delta_2}{v_{5,2}}
=
\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{v_{5,1}}.
}
\]

And that is the crucial point: the right-hand side is the **same scalar quotient datum already present in the theorem**. So this “canonical” cross-point transport carries no extra information at all.

The parallel \(u_7=0\) gauge does the same thing. There
\[
A_7^\flat(h)=v_7^\flat(h)\,S,
\qquad
v_7^\flat(h)=-\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{u_5(h)}.
\]
Running the same comparison gives
\[
\boxed{
-\frac{\Delta_1}{u_{5,1}}+\lambda\frac{\Delta_2}{u_{5,2}}
=
-\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{u_{5,1}}.
}
\]

So both obvious patchwise gauge sections collapse the two-point septic transport to the **same quotient determinant scalar**. They do not recover the hidden repeated-node shear.

That gives a real theorem-strength structural conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any two-point argument based only on the patchwise gauges }v_7=0\text{ or }u_7=0
\text{ is still exactly quotient-blind.}
}
\]

This is stronger than what we had before. It means the first natural attempt to make the longitudinal direction meaningful across points has already failed.

So the next viable attack is narrower now.

It cannot be:

- quotient class only;
- cubic/quintic source minors only;
- or patchwise \(v_7=0\)/\(u_7=0\) transport only.

The next viable attack has to introduce something genuinely **cross-point**, not pointwise. There are only two realistic options I see:

First, a **transport gauge along the patch**, not just a pointwise section.  
That would mean choosing \(A_7^\sharp(h)\) by an ODE or derivative normalization along \(h\), so the comparison between \(h_1\) and \(h_2\) is not allowed to absorb arbitrary multiples of \(A_5\) independently at each point.

Second, a **parity-transferred repeated-node local model** on the actual mixed coordinate, where the shear appears before quotienting ever enters. That fits your note’s strategic constraint that mixed closure will need parity transfer, patch dichotomy, or genuine \(Y\)-\(S\) source coupling, not just planar or quotientized geometry. turn40file1

So the best current conclusion is:

- the longitudinal idea was the right thing to probe;
- the obvious implementation via local \(v_7=0\) or \(u_7=0\) gauges does **not** work;
- the next attack has to use a **nonlocal transport gauge** or a **parity-transferred mixed local model**.

That is real progress, because it removes another whole class of tempting but dead routes and narrows the live target further.

_Thought for 5m 27s_

Yes. I think I finally have a genuinely better reduction.

It still does not close the two-point theorem, but it converts it into a **repeated-node tangency problem in the lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry**, which is much closer to the now-mature 3-point machinery. That is exactly the sort of below-lifted source-minor viewpoint your note was pointing toward. turn41file2

Here is the clean statement.

On a connected patch \(U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}\), use the draft’s local septic gauge \(v_7=0\), so
\[
Q_v(h):=\left(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\right)
=
\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right).
\]

Now take an exact bad two-pair core and write
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
e:=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S.
\]
Choose a representative \(R=r_u I+r_v S\) of the septic quotient defect, exactly as in the quantitative two-pair theorem.

Then set
\[
e_\sigma:=-\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{v_{5,1}}.
\]

If \(e\neq 0\), define the **interaction point**
\[
P^{(v)}_{12}:=\left(\frac{e_u}{e},\frac{e_v}{e},\frac{e_\sigma}{e}\right)\in \mathbf C^3.
\]

The exact bad-core identities then become
\[
c_1-\lambda c_2+e=0,
\]
\[
c_1 y_1-\lambda c_2 y_2+e_u=0,
\]
\[
c_1 x_1-\lambda c_2 x_2+e_v=0,
\]
and, in the same \(v_7=0\) gauge,
\[
c_1 \sigma_{v,1}-\lambda c_2 \sigma_{v,2}+e_\sigma=0.
\]

So you get the exact affine relation
\[
\boxed{
c_1\,(1,Q_v(h_1))-\lambda c_2\,(1,Q_v(h_2))+e\,(1,P^{(v)}_{12})=0.
}
\]

That means:

\[
\boxed{
P^{(v)}_{12}\ \text{lies exactly on the secant line through}\ Q_v(h_1)\ \text{and}\ Q_v(h_2).
}
\]

This is the two-point mixed analogue of the source-determinant line picture. It is much better than the earlier source-minor ratios, because it is **shear-sensitive**: it uses \(e,e_u,e_v,e_\sigma\) themselves, not only wedge minors that kill the repeated-node shear.

Now take a close branch:
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad \lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Then the exact equations give
\[
e=\delta(\alpha c+c')(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
\[
e_u=\delta(\alpha u_5+u_5')(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
\[
e_v=\delta(\alpha v_5+v_5')(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
and similarly
\[
e_\sigma=\delta\bigl(\alpha(c\sigma_v)+(c\sigma_v)'\bigr)(m)+O(\delta^2).
\]

So projectively,
\[
[e:e_u:e_v:e_\sigma]
\longrightarrow
[\alpha c+c':\alpha u_5+u_5':\alpha v_5+v_5':\alpha(c\sigma_v)+(c\sigma_v)']_m.
\]

If \(\alpha c(m)+c'(m)\neq 0\), this gives a finite limit point
\[
\boxed{
P^{(v)}_\alpha(m)
=
Q_v(m)+\frac{1}{\alpha+\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}}\,Q_v'(m).
}
\]

If \(\alpha c(m)+c'(m)=0\), then \(P^{(v)}_{12}\) goes to infinity in the tangent direction of \(Q_v\) at \(m\).

So a close exact bad two-pair branch forces a very specific repeated-node profile:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the interaction point on the secant line converges to a tangent-point or tangent-direction of }Q_v.
}
\]

That is the strongest reduction I can defend right now.

Why this matters:

Earlier attacks using only secant minors or quotient determinants were exactly blind to the shear parameter. This one is not. The hidden shear \(\alpha\) is now visible as the parameter of the tangent-point
\[
Q_v(m)+t\,Q_v'(m),\qquad t=\frac{1}{\alpha+c'/c}.
\]

So the two-point branch has been reduced to this:

A genuine close bad two-pair branch would produce a family of secant-supported interaction points converging to the tangent line of the lifted curve \(Q_v\).

That is now close enough to the 3-point/lifted-tangency apparatus that the branches are starting to touch conceptually. turn41file2

What is still missing is one more lemma, and now it is very concrete:

you need a theorem saying that such a tangent-point realization by interaction points is impossible on a good \(v_5\)-patch unless it degenerates into a lower-core tangency mechanism already covered by the lifted 3-point branch or one of the mixed 4-point obstruction types.

So the best next target is no longer “prove quadratic factorization.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{interaction-point tangent rigidification on }Q_v.
}
\]

This is the first route that both uses the actual exact two-pair identities and lands in the derivative geometry that has recently become much stronger.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:35:23)

I’m checking the latest draft’s exact formulas around the \(v_7=0\) patch, the two-pair theorem, and the 3-point lifted tangency results, because the live question is whether the new interaction-point picture can actually be rigidified with machinery the paper already has.

_Thought for 2m 30s_

I attacked it, and I think this gives the cleanest no-go result so far.

The interaction-point reduction is real, but **tangent rigidification alone still cannot kill the mixed two-point branch**.

Here is the exact reason.

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, write
\[
Q_v(h):=\left(Y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\right)
=
\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)v_5(h)}\right).
\]

For an exact bad two-pair core, the exact identities give
\[
c_1-\lambda c_2+e=0,
\qquad
c_1Q_v(h_1)-\lambda c_2 Q_v(h_2)+e\,P^{(v)}_{12}=0,
\]
where
\[
P^{(v)}_{12}:=\left(\frac{e_u}{e},\frac{e_v}{e},\frac{e_\sigma}{e}\right).
\]

So as long as \(e\neq 0\),
\[
\boxed{
P^{(v)}_{12}
=
Q_v(h_1)+\frac{\lambda c_2}{e}\,\bigl(Q_v(h_2)-Q_v(h_1)\bigr).
}
\]
That is, \(P^{(v)}_{12}\) lies exactly on the secant line through \(Q_v(h_1)\) and \(Q_v(h_2)\).

Now pass to a close branch:
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Then
\[
e=\delta(\alpha c+c')(m)+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
Q_v(h_2)-Q_v(h_1)=\delta\,Q_v'(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
and \(\lambda c_2=c(m)+O(\delta)\). Therefore
\[
P^{(v)}_{12}
=
Q_v(m)+
\frac{1}{\alpha+\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}}\,Q_v'(m)+O(\delta).
\]

So in the limit,
\[
\boxed{
P^{(v)}_{12}\longrightarrow
Q_v(m)+t\,Q_v'(m),
\qquad
t=\frac{1}{\alpha+c'(m)/c(m)}.
}
\]

This is the key point: as \(\alpha\) varies, \(t\) varies freely.

So the repeated-node shear parameter does not force \(P^{(v)}_{12}\) to any special point of the tangent line. It can converge to **any finite point on the tangent line**, and when
\[
\alpha=-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}
\]
it goes to the point at infinity in the tangent direction.

That means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the interaction-point limit fills the whole tangent line.}
}
\]

This kills the hoped-for rigidification.

Why this matters for the 3-point machinery:

the lifted 3-point results in the draft classify when the tangent line at one source point meets the lifted curve again, via the repeated-node tangent-contact equation \(H_3(a,u)=0\), and then organize the local/global branch behavior from there. The note is right that this branch is now quite mature. turn42file1

But our point \(P^{(v)}_{12}\) is **not** an actual point \(Q_v(u)\) on the lifted curve. It is just an external affine combination built from the interaction defects.

So from the current identities, all we know is:

- \(P^{(v)}_{12}\) lies on the secant line;
- in the close limit it lies on the tangent line.

That is not enough to invoke \(H_3(a,u)=0\), because \(H_3\) needs a second **source point on the curve**, not an arbitrary external point on the line.

The same obstruction hits the 4-point tangent-plane picture: an external point converging into the tangent line or tangent plane does not by itself produce a repeated-node 4-point circuit.

So the strongest honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any argument based only on the fact that }P^{(v)}_{12}\text{ converges to the tangent line of }Q_v
\text{ cannot close the mixed two-point branch.}
}
\]

That is a real no-go theorem.

What would be enough now is one extra ingredient of one of these two types:

First, a **point-on-curve identification**:
prove that the interaction point is not just on the secant line, but actually equals
\[
P^{(v)}_{12}=Q_v(u_{12})
\]
for some source parameter \(u_{12}\), at least asymptotically. Then the repeated-node 3-point machinery becomes available immediately.

Second, a **restriction on the tangent-line parameter \(t\)**:
prove from parity transfer, patch dichotomy, or a source-level mixed coupling that the allowed \(t\) values lie in a forbidden subset of the tangent line. Right now, without such a restriction, \(t\) is free and the tangent-line geometry alone has no bite.

So this attack did not close the branch, but it did clarify the target a lot:

the missing ingredient is **not** tangent geometry by itself; it is a theorem that turns the interaction point from an arbitrary point on the tangent line into something source-geometric enough to trigger the 3-point or 4-point rigidification machinery.

That is the cleanest reduction I can defend now.
## User (2026-04-20 18:39:01)

ok attack

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:39:08)

I’m checking whether the interaction point carries more hidden structure than “some point on the tangent line.” The two promising possibilities are: either its coefficient forces \(t\) to match a nearby source parameter, or the exact bad-core equations secretly make \((1,P^{(v)}_{12})\) part of a repeated-node affine circuit rather than an arbitrary external point.

_Thought for 8m 17s_

I found a better reduction.

The first genuinely **shear-sensitive** scalar comes from using the \(v_7=0\) and \(u_7=0\) patch gauges **together** on an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]

Write
\[
Q_v(h)=\bigl(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)
=
\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c},\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\right),
\]
and
\[
Q_u(h)=\bigl(x(h),y(h),\tau_u(h)\bigr)
=
\left(\frac{v_5}{c},\frac{u_5}{c},-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}\right).
\]
For actual source points these satisfy the exact mixed compatibility quadric
\[
x\,\sigma_v+y\,\tau_u=0.
\]

Now for an exact bad two-pair core, keep the usual notation
\[
\lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},\qquad
E=e_u I+e_v S,
\]
and let \(R\) be a representative of the septic quotient defect.

On the \(v_7=0\) patch define
\[
e_\sigma:=-\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{v_{5,1}},
\qquad
P^{(v)}_{12}:=\left(\frac{e_u}{e},\frac{e_v}{e},\frac{e_\sigma}{e}\right),
\]
and on the \(u_7=0\) patch define
\[
e_\tau:=\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{u_{5,1}},
\qquad
P^{(u)}_{12}:=\left(\frac{e_v}{e},\frac{e_u}{e},\frac{e_\tau}{e}\right).
\]

Then the exact two-pair identities give the paired secant formulas
\[
c_1(1,Q_v(h_1))-\lambda c_2(1,Q_v(h_2))+e(1,P^{(v)}_{12})=0,
\]
\[
c_1(1,Q_u(h_1))-\lambda c_2(1,Q_u(h_2))+e(1,P^{(u)}_{12})=0.
\]

So the interaction point is not just on one secant line: it is simultaneously encoded in both patch models.

That lets you define the exact mixed compatibility defect
\[
\Gamma_{12}
:=
\frac{e_v}{e}\frac{e_\sigma}{e}
+
\frac{e_u}{e}\frac{e_\tau}{e}.
\]

A short calculation gives the exact formula
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{12}
=
\frac{\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{e^2}
\left(\frac{e_u}{u_{5,1}}-\frac{e_v}{v_{5,1}}\right)
=
\frac{\lambda\,\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})}{u_{5,1}v_{5,1}e^2}
\bigl(u_{5,1}v_{5,2}-v_{5,1}u_{5,2}\bigr).
}
\]

This is the first scalar I’ve found that has all the properties we wanted:

- it uses genuine \(Y\)-\(S\) coupling,
- it is not quotient-blind in the old way,
- it is not just planar \((x,S)\) geometry,
- and it matches the strategic constraint in your note that mixed closure will need parity transfer, patch dichotomy, or real \(Y\)-\(S\) source coupling rather than planar arguments alone. turn43file1

Now take a close branch
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
From the exact equations,
\[
P^{(v)}_{12}\to Q_v(m)+t\,Q_v'(m),
\qquad
P^{(u)}_{12}\to Q_u(m)+t\,Q_u'(m),
\qquad
t=\frac{1}{\alpha+c'(m)/c(m)}.
\]

Since the curve itself satisfies
\[
x\,\sigma_v+y\,\tau_u=0
\]
and its first derivative also vanishes along the curve, the first nontrivial tangent-line escape from the compatibility quadric is quadratic. Explicitly,
\[
\Gamma_{12}\longrightarrow \Gamma_0(m,t)=t^2\,\mathcal G(m),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G(m):=x'(m)\sigma_v'(m)+y'(m)\tau_u'(m).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G(m)
=
\frac{1}{c(m)^2}\Bigl(v_5'(m)\Bigl(\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}\Bigr)'(m)
+
u_5'(m)\Bigl(-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5}\Bigr)'(m)\Bigr),
\]
and also
\[
\mathcal G(m)
=
\left(\frac{u_5 v_5'-v_5 u_5'}{c^2}\right)(m)
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'(m).
\]

So the mixed two-point branch has now been reduced to this very concrete statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A close exact bad two-point branch forces } \Gamma_{12}\sim t^2\,\mathcal G(m).
}
\]

That is the strongest attack result so far.

What it means is:

- the old secant-minor package was blind to the hidden shear,
- but the paired \(v/u\)-patch compatibility defect \(\Gamma_{12}\) does see it,
- and the obstruction is now concentrated in the source-geometric scalar
\[
\mathcal G=x'\sigma_v'+y'\tau_u'.
\]

I do **not** yet have a contradiction from this alone. But this is now the smallest live target I trust:

prove that on the relevant mixed patch, \(\mathcal G\) has a sign/nonvanishing or parity-controlled behavior that is incompatible with an exact bad two-point branch. That would be exactly the sort of extra \(Y\)-\(S\) coupling your note says is required. 

So the branch has been reduced from a vague source-level theorem to one explicit mixed compatibility scalar.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 18:54:25)

I’m checking whether that new scalar \(\mathcal G=x'\sigma_v'+y'\tau_u'\) is actually expressible in terms of quantities the draft already controls, or whether it hides one more gauge-dependent variable. If it collapses to an existing invariant, we may be able to decide quickly whether this route really has bite.

_Thought for 8m 4s_

I attacked it, and this gives the cleanest reduction so far.

The right scalar is **not** the ad hoc \(\Gamma_{12}\) formula I was using before. There is a much cleaner exact identity once you use the two patch models together on an overlap
\[
U\subset \{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]

Write
\[
Q_v(h)=\bigl(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr)
=
\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c},\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}\right),
\]
and
\[
Q_u(h)=\bigl(y(h),x(h),\tau_u(h)\bigr)
=
\left(\frac{u_5}{c},\frac{v_5}{c},-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}\right).
\]

These satisfy the exact compatibility quadric
\[
\boxed{
x\,\sigma_v+y\,\tau_u=0.
}
\]

Now take an exact bad two-pair core and set
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
e:=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1}.
\]
From the exact cubic/quintic identities,
\[
c_1-\lambda c_2+e=0,
\]
and after passing to the \(v_7=0\) and \(u_7=0\) local gauges, the exact two-point equations can be written as
\[
c_1(1,Q_v(h_1))-\lambda c_2(1,Q_v(h_2))+e(1,P_{12})=0,
\]
\[
c_1(1,Q_u(h_1))-\lambda c_2(1,Q_u(h_2))+e(1,\widetilde P_{12})=0,
\]
where the first two coordinates of \(P_{12}\) and \(\widetilde P_{12}\) are the same:
\[
P_{12}=(p_y,p_x,p_\sigma),\qquad
\widetilde P_{12}=(p_y,p_x,p_\tau).
\]

So there is a single secant parameter
\[
\boxed{
T:=\frac{\lambda c_2}{e},
}
\]
such that
\[
(p_y,p_x,p_\sigma)=Q_v(h_1)+T\bigl(Q_v(h_2)-Q_v(h_1)\bigr),
\]
and
\[
(p_y,p_x,p_\tau)=Q_u(h_1)+T\bigl(Q_u(h_2)-Q_u(h_1)\bigr).
\]

That is the exact interaction-point formula.

Now define the exact compatibility defect of the interaction point by
\[
\Gamma_{12}:=p_xp_\sigma+p_yp_\tau.
\]

Because the source points satisfy
\[
x_i\sigma_i+y_i\tau_i=0,
\]
a direct calculation gives the exact identity
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{12}
=
T(T-1)\,B_{12},
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
B_{12}:=
(x_2-x_1)(\sigma_2-\sigma_1)
+
(y_2-y_1)(\tau_2-\tau_1).
}
\]

This is much better than the previous formulas. It is exact, and it shows precisely how the interaction point fails to lie on the compatibility quadric.

Now take a close branch
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Then
\[
e=\delta\bigl(\alpha c+c'\bigr)(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
so
\[
T=\frac{\lambda c_2}{e}
=
\frac{1}{\delta\bigl(\alpha+c'/c\bigr)(m)}+O(1).
\]
Also
\[
x_2-x_1=\delta x'(m)+O(\delta^3),\quad
y_2-y_1=\delta y'(m)+O(\delta^3),
\]
\[
\sigma_2-\sigma_1=\delta \sigma_v'(m)+O(\delta^3),\quad
\tau_2-\tau_1=\delta \tau_u'(m)+O(\delta^3).
\]
Hence
\[
B_{12}
=
\delta^2\,\mathcal G(m)+O(\delta^3),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G(m):=x'(m)\sigma_v'(m)+y'(m)\tau_u'(m).
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{12}
\longrightarrow
\frac{\mathcal G(m)}{\bigl(\alpha+c'(m)/c(m)\bigr)^2}
}
\]
whenever \(\alpha+c'/c\neq 0\). If \(\alpha+c'/c=0\), then \(T\) is of higher order and the interaction point goes to infinity along the tangent direction.

So the mixed two-point branch has now been reduced to one explicit scalar:
\[
\mathcal G=x'\sigma_v'+y'\tau_u'.
\]

Even better, \(\mathcal G\) factors in a very clean way. Since
\[
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\]
one computes
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G
=
(xy'-yx')\left(\frac{\tau_u}{x}\right)'
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}\left(-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
}
\]

This is the strongest “goodie” so far, because each factor is now tied to existing draft structure.

First factor:
\[
xy'-yx'=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\frac{y}{x}\ \text{is constant}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
u_5=\kappa v_5.
\]
But on a connected interval with
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,
\]
that would make
\[
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
linearly dependent, contradicting Proposition `prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c`.

Second factor:
\[
\left(\frac{\tau_u}{x}\right)'=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\tau_u=\kappa x
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\Delta_7=-\kappa\,u_5v_5.
\]
But the right-hand side is built entirely from cubic/quintic layers and carries no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice, contradicting the draft’s direct-\(q^{(7)}\)-nonvanishing result for \(\Delta_7\).

So on any connected overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
we get the honest theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G \not\equiv 0 \quad\text{on }U.
}
\]

That is real progress.

What it means:

- the overlap compatibility defect is not vacuous;
- it is governed by a concrete source-geometric scalar \(\mathcal G\);
- and \(\mathcal G\) is not identically zero by existing results in the draft.

What it does **not** yet give is a contradiction. A close exact bad two-point branch only forces
\[
\Gamma_{12}\sim \frac{\mathcal G(m)}{(\alpha+c'/c)^2},
\]
and the draft does not currently supply any reason that \(\Gamma_{12}\) must vanish, have a fixed sign, or stay in a forbidden range.

So the smallest live target is now very precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove one extra source-level or parity-transferred theorem that constrains }\Gamma_{12}.
}
\]

At this point the two-point branch is no longer a vague “source theorem” problem. It has been reduced to one explicit overlap scalar \(\mathcal G\) and one explicit interaction compatibility defect \(\Gamma_{12}\).

That is the strongest honest attack result I can defend from the current draft.

_Thought for 7m 0s_

I pushed it further, and there is a real new reduction.

The overlap-patch scalar is better written as
\[
\mathcal G
=
x'\sigma_v'+y'\tau_u',
\qquad
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\quad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},\quad
\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},\quad
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]

The key identity is that on an overlap patch
\[
U\subset \{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
this factors **exactly** into two source-level \(2\times 2\) Wronskians:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
}
\]
where
\[
W(f,g):=f g'-f' g.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'
=
-\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2u_5^2}\,\bigl(u_5\lambda'-u_5'\lambda\bigr).
\]

That is the cleanest “goodie” so far, because it turns the mixed overlap obstruction into a product of two source minors.

Why this matters:

The first factor
\[
W(u_5,v_5)=u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5
\]
vanishes identically only if \(u_5/v_5\) is constant, equivalently \(u_5=\kappa v_5\), which is ruled out on an interval by the draft’s linear-independence statement for
\[
1,\ \frac{u_5}{c},\ \frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

The second factor
\[
W(u_5,\lambda)=u_5\lambda'-u_5'\lambda,
\qquad \lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
vanishes identically only if \(\lambda/u_5\) is constant, equivalently
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5.
\]
But the right-hand side is built only from cubic/quintic layers and has no direct \(q^{(7)}\)-slice, while the draft’s direct-\(q^{(7)}\) theorem says \(\Delta_7\) has a generically nonzero direct septic slice. So this is also impossible on an interval.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{on every connected overlap patch }
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
}
\]

That is now rigorous modulo the already-written draft results.

There is another useful consequence on a centered good patch. When the centered parity package applies, \(u_5\) and \(\lambda=\Delta_7/v_5\) are odd in the centered variable \(s\), so both
\[
W(u_5,v_5),\qquad W(u_5,\lambda)
\]
are odd in \(s\). Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G(s)\ \text{is even in }s.
}
\]
So any isolated centered zero of \(\mathcal G\) has even order. That does not kill the branch, but it does say \(\mathcal G\) behaves more like the “sterile” parity-controlled scalars than like a branch-seeding odd scalar.

This fits the source-determinant viewpoint from the newer nonmixed material: the meaningful mixed overlap obstruction is now a product of two explicit source minors, not a vague quotient remainder. It is exactly the kind of below-lifted finite-minor language the updated draft is pushing toward. turn44file2

What this still does **not** give is a contradiction. A close exact bad two-point branch forces
\[
\Gamma_{12}\to \frac{\mathcal G(m)}{(\alpha+c'(m)/c(m))^2},
\]
so \(\mathcal G\not\equiv0\) only tells us the interaction compatibility defect is genuinely nontrivial; it does not yet tell us it is forbidden.

So the next best target is now very precise:

prove one extra theorem that constrains the second source minor
\[
W(u_5,\lambda)=u_5\lambda'-u_5'\lambda
\]
on the actual mixed branch — either by parity transfer into the \(u_5\)-patch local model, or by showing that if a close exact two-point branch persists then this Wronskian must vanish or have a forbidden parity/sign behavior. That is the smallest live target I trust now.

Yes. I checked the latest draft, and the new progress is genuinely relevant to the current attack.

My updated read is:

The two-point branch is **still not closed**, but the best target has shifted. The new differential-geometry and nonmixed 4-point work strongly suggests the right missing ingredient is now a **shear-transfer / source-coupling theorem**, not another attempt at raw two-point factorization. That matches your note and the draft’s own status language: the two-point bottleneck is still source-level, while the 3-point branch is now much more mature and the nonmixed 4-point branch has been pushed to a clean ceiling. turn48file0

What changed in a useful way

First, the draft now has a much sharper lifted-geometric “ambient” picture on a \(v_5\)-patch: defect-free bad cores reduce to affine dependence of the lifted points
\[
Q_v(h)=\bigl(y(h),x(h),\sigma_v(h)\bigr),
\]
with effective ceiling \(k\le 4\). So the geometry is no longer floating free: \(k=2\) means coincidence, \(k=3\) means collinearity, \(k=4\) means coplanarity. The draft itself says that once the lifted 3-point branch is globally rigid, the remaining burden shifts upward to the two-point source-level merger problem and the mixed/nonmixed 4-point mechanisms. That is directly relevant to us. It means any successful two-point argument should try to *feed into* this lifted finite-core geometry, not build a parallel theory. 

Second, the nonmixed 4-point side is now much clearer about both what works and what does not. On a nonmixed arc, interval-persistent exact 4-point degeneracy forces affine planarity via the scalar invariant
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right),
\]
so the nonmixed branch is no longer “raw coplanarity” but a derivative-geometric odd-zero problem for \(\mathcal R\). But the draft also proves a strong no-go statement: at the current source-level Wronskian / determinant package, the odd-zero pattern of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) and \(\mathcal R\) is formally unconstrained, so generic Wronskian algebra is not enough; the missing ingredient must be a genuine source-coupling theorem. That is highly relevant to the mixed two-point attack, because it tells us our repeated failures with generic source minors, secant ratios, quotient representatives, and similar algebra were not accidents. The paper now has an explicit theorem-strength version of “that whole style of argument reaches a ceiling.” turn48file1

Third, the draft’s “first-loss rigidification” on the nonmixed side is exactly the right conceptual template for the mixed two-point problem. It shows that any first loss of the repeated-source monotonicity scalar \(\Gamma_a\) rigidifies into a **sheared repeated-node tangent-contact** rooted at a curvature-zero point. Then the subsequent results show where that route still fails generically and where odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\) sterilize the sheared event. So the geometry is now very explicit: the relevant bad mechanism is not vague “4-point degeneracy” but a rooted sheared repeated-node event. That is precisely the sort of target our mixed two-point interaction-point analysis was starting to hint at. 

What this means for the current two-point attack

It makes several of the old targets clearly second-best.

I no longer think the best next move is to keep trying to prove a source-linear two-point factorization or a quotient-level continuity bypass. The new nonmixed results say, in effect, that generic determinant/ratio/Wronskian geometry hits a ceiling, and the real extra ingredient has to be source-coupling. That fits very well with what we already found on the mixed side: the secant-minor and quotient packages were exactly blind to the hidden repeated-node shear.

So the best current attack is:

### Prove a mixed-to-sheared transfer theorem

Something like:

On a good overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
any close exact mixed two-point bad branch canonically produces a **sheared repeated-node tangent-contact event** for an appropriate repeated-source scalar built from the same lifted data.

If you can prove that, then the new nonmixed machinery becomes relevant in a serious way. Not because the mixed branch becomes nonmixed, but because it would reduce the mixed obstruction to the same kind of rooted sheared event that the draft now understands much better.

Why I think this is the best target now

Because the current draft gives three useful facts all at once:

- the finite-core geometry on a \(v_5\)-patch already lives in the lifted points \(Q_v(h)\); 
- the nonmixed repeated-source scalar \(\Gamma_a\) has a full first-loss / sheared-event theory; 
- and the draft explicitly says the remaining burden is a genuine source-coupling theorem, not more generic determinant algebra. 

That is almost a direct instruction for the mixed two-point branch: stop looking for another determinant miracle, and instead build the source-coupling/shear-transfer bridge.

My updated ranking of live routes

Best route:
prove a **shear-transfer theorem** from a close exact mixed two-point branch to a sheared repeated-node tangency event in the lifted geometry.

Second-best route:
derive a mixed analogue of the repeated-source scalar \(\Gamma_a\) whose first-loss event rigidifies the same way.

Less promising now:
more work on raw source-minor ratios, quotient-derived septic representatives, or generic Wronskians.

What the latest draft does not yet give us

It still does not provide the mixed source-coupling theorem. The two-point status remains essentially what your note said: the bottleneck lives in the two-pair block and is still source-level. The newer progress changes the **shape** of the missing theorem, not the fact that it is missing. 

So my best concrete next attack is:

Take the mixed two-point interaction-point construction you and I were developing, and try to prove that along a close bad branch it is not merely approaching some arbitrary tangent line, but actually induces a rooted sheared repeated-node event for a repeated-source scalar of the \(\Gamma_a\)-type. If that transfer lands, the new differential-geometry package becomes usable rather than just suggestive.

e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},\qquad
E=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S,
\]
and define the branch-generated interaction coordinates
\[
\gamma_{12}:=\frac{e_u}{e},\qquad
\xi_{12}:=\frac{e_v}{e},\qquad
\zeta_{12}:=\frac{e_\sigma}{e},
\]
where \(e_\sigma\) is the septic scalar coming from the same exact \(v_7=0\)-patch rewrite.

Now define the three source-pinned moving-shear functions
\[
f_{12}(h):=u_5(h)-\gamma_{12}\,c(h),
\]
\[
g_{12}(h):=v_5(h)-\xi_{12}\,c(h),
\]
\[
k_{12}(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}-\zeta_{12}\,c(h).
\]

Then the exact two-pair identities are equivalent to the repeated-source transport system
\[
\boxed{
f_{12}(h_1)=\lambda\,f_{12}(h_2),\qquad
g_{12}(h_1)=\lambda\,g_{12}(h_2),\qquad
k_{12}(h_1)=\lambda\,k_{12}(h_2).
}
\]

So a mixed close two-point branch is not just “some secant-line phenomenon.” It is exactly a **source-pinned moving-shear repeated-source problem**.

That is the mixed analogue of the nonmixed source-level shear-transfer language. And it lines up perfectly with the new nonmixed lesson: fixed-level or planar geometry alone hits a ceiling; the live object has to be a branch-generated moving shear with genuine source coupling. 

There is also an exact first-order profile. If
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+O(\delta^2),
\]
then the interaction point satisfies
\[
(\gamma_{12},\xi_{12},\zeta_{12})
=
Q_v(m)+
\frac{1}{\alpha+c'(m)/c(m)}\,Q_v'(m)+O(\delta).
\]
So the moving shear is not arbitrary: it is sourced by a point on the tangent line to the lifted curve \(Q_v\).

That gives the cleanest reduction yet:

A close exact mixed two-point bad branch is equivalent to a branch-generated moving shear \((\gamma_{12},\xi_{12},\zeta_{12})\) for which the three source functions
\[
u_5-\gamma_{12}c,\qquad v_5-\xi_{12}c,\qquad \Delta_7/v_5-\zeta_{12}c
\]
satisfy an exact repeated-source transport law between \(h_1\) and \(h_2\), and whose parameter triple approaches the tangent-line data of \(Q_v\).

This is better than the earlier secant-minor language for one reason: it is now explicitly **shear-sensitive**. The hidden shear no longer disappears into wedge minors.

What still blocks closure is that, just as on the nonmixed side, repeated-source transport plus local tangent geometry by itself is not enough. The nonmixed development now explicitly says that even there, the local shear-transfer route reaches a ceiling and a successful theorem must use additional RH-specific source coupling.  The mixed branch is now in exactly that position.

So the best next theorem to attack is no longer a quadratic interaction factorization. It is this:

**Mixed source-coupling theorem.**  
Show that on a good overlap patch, no nontrivial close branch-generated moving shear \((\gamma_{12},\xi_{12},\zeta_{12})\) can satisfy the repeated-source transport system for
\[
u_5-\gamma c,\qquad v_5-\xi c,\qquad \Delta_7/v_5-\zeta c
\]
unless the branch degenerates into an already-classified lower-core mechanism.

That is the smallest live target I trust now. It uses the new differential-geometric progress rather than fighting it, and it says very concretely what the missing “source-coupling theorem” should couple.

Now take a close branch and write
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=1+\alpha\delta+\beta\delta^2+O(\delta^3).
\]

Expand any one of the transport equations, say
\[
f(h_1)=\lambda f(h_2).
\]
A symmetric Taylor expansion gives
\[
f\Bigl(m-\frac{\delta}{2}\Bigr)
-
\bigl(1+\alpha\delta+\beta\delta^2+O(\delta^3)\bigr)
f\Bigl(m+\frac{\delta}{2}\Bigr)
=0.
\]
The \(\delta\)- and \(\delta^2\)-coefficients are
\[
f'(m)+\alpha f(m)=0,
\qquad
\beta+\frac{\alpha}{2}\frac{f'(m)}{f(m)}=0.
\]
Using the first equation, the second becomes
\[
\beta=\frac{\alpha^2}{2}.
\]

And exactly the same calculation holds for \(g\) and \(k\). So along any close exact mixed two-point branch,
\[
\boxed{
f'(m)=-\alpha f(m),\qquad
g'(m)=-\alpha g(m),\qquad
k'(m)=-\alpha k(m),
}
\]
and the common second coefficient of the amplitude ratio is forced to be
\[
\boxed{
\beta=\frac{\alpha^2}{2}.
}
\]

This is the key new reduction.

Equivalently, the branch-generated moving shears satisfy a common logarithmic-derivative law
\[
\frac{f'}{f}(m)=\frac{g'}{g}(m)=\frac{k'}{k}(m)=-\alpha,
\]
so their pairwise Wronskians vanish at \(m\):
\[
W(f,g)(m)=W(f,k)(m)=W(g,k)(m)=0.
\]

If you write the limiting shear parameters explicitly, this becomes
\[
\gamma=\frac{\alpha u_5+u_5'}{\alpha c+c'},\qquad
\xi=\frac{\alpha v_5+v_5'}{\alpha c+c'},\qquad
\zeta=\frac{\alpha(\Delta_7/v_5)+(\Delta_7/v_5)'}{\alpha c+c'}.
\]

So the branch is genuinely shear-sensitive: \(\alpha\) is not killed. But here is the crucial no-go:

**two-point transport alone only controls the common 1-jet. It gives no second-order/tangency information at all.**

The reason is visible in the expansion above: the \(f''(m)\) term cancels identically at order \(\delta^2\). The same happens for \(g''\) and \(k''\). So from exact two-point transport you get

- a common logarithmic derivative,
- and the kinematic identity \(\beta=\alpha^2/2\),

but you do **not** get a repeated-node tangent-contact condition of the kind the nonmixed source-level shear-transfer machinery uses. In particular, nothing like
\[
J_f(m)=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
D_f(a,h)=\partial_hD_f(a,h)=0
\]
drops out automatically.

That is the strongest structural conclusion I can defend now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A close exact mixed two-point branch determines a common-log-derivative moving shear, but not a repeated-node tangency event.}
}
\]

So the new 3-point / nonmixed 4-point progress is highly relevant, but it also clarifies exactly what is still missing: you need a **mixed source-coupling theorem that upgrades transport to tangency**. Without that upgrade, the nonmixed first-loss / shear-transfer package cannot be invoked directly. This fits the draft’s present architecture very well: the 3-point branch is now mature, the nonmixed 4-point branch has identified the source-coupling ceiling, and the two-point bottleneck is still source-level. turn53file2

So my best current target is now extremely specific:

prove one extra theorem saying that along a close exact mixed two-point bad branch, one of the branch-generated shears \(f,g,k\) does not merely satisfy
\[
F(h_1)=\lambda F(h_2),
\]
but actually enters a repeated-node tangency regime — equivalently, a second-order source-coupling statement that forces \(J_F\) or the corresponding divided-difference/tangent-contact scalar to vanish.

That is the smallest live theorem I trust now.

Here is the clean mixed two-point no-go:

On an overlap patch, define the branch-generated moving shears
\[
f(h)=u_5(h)-\gamma c(h),\qquad
g(h)=v_5(h)-\xi c(h),\qquad
k(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}-\zeta c(h),
\]
with \((\gamma,\xi,\zeta)=(\gamma_{12},\xi_{12},\zeta_{12})\) from the exact bad two-pair core.

For any two points \(h_1,h_2\), the source determinants against \(c\) are
\[
D_f(h_1,h_2):=c_1 f_2-c_2 f_1,\qquad
D_g(h_1,h_2):=c_1 g_2-c_2 g_1,\qquad
D_k(h_1,h_2):=c_1 k_2-c_2 k_1.
\]

But the \(c\)-shear cancels identically:
\[
D_f(h_1,h_2)=c_1u_{5,2}-c_2u_{5,1}=D_{u_5}(h_1,h_2),
\]
\[
D_g(h_1,h_2)=c_1v_{5,2}-c_2v_{5,1}=D_{v_5}(h_1,h_2),
\]
\[
D_k(h_1,h_2)=c_1\frac{\Delta_{7,2}}{v_{5,2}}-c_2\frac{\Delta_{7,1}}{v_{5,1}}.
\]

So the branch-generated parameters \((\gamma,\xi,\zeta)\) are completely invisible to every single determinant of the nonmixed source-transfer form.

That means the nonmixed source-level shear-transfer machinery does **not** transplant to the mixed two-point branch in the obvious way. Any argument that only uses single source determinants
\[
D_{u_5-\gamma c},\quad D_{v_5-\xi c},\quad D_{\Delta_7/v_5-\zeta c}
\]
collapses exactly back to the old secant-minor package and is therefore still too weak.

That is the strongest clean structural result from the latest draft.

It also explains why the previous attacks kept hitting a ceiling: the moving shear is real, but if you test it only through determinants against \(c\), the shear disappears identically.

So the next viable target has to be **coupled** rather than single-determinant.

The best candidate now is to work with the shear-sensitive ratios
\[
\Phi_{\gamma,\xi}(h):=\frac{g(h)}{f(h)}
=
\frac{v_5(h)-\xi c(h)}{u_5(h)-\gamma c(h)},
\qquad
\Theta_{\gamma,\zeta}(h):=\frac{k(h)}{f(h)}
=
\frac{\Delta_7(h)/v_5(h)-\zeta c(h)}{u_5(h)-\gamma c(h)}.
\]

For an exact bad two-pair core, the transport equations
\[
f(h_1)=\lambda f(h_2),\qquad g(h_1)=\lambda g(h_2),\qquad k(h_1)=\lambda k(h_2)
\]
imply the exact repeated-value identities
\[
\Phi_{\gamma,\xi}(h_1)=\Phi_{\gamma,\xi}(h_2),\qquad
\Theta_{\gamma,\zeta}(h_1)=\Theta_{\gamma,\zeta}(h_2).
\]

This is the first genuinely shear-sensitive formulation that survives the determinant no-go.

So the best next theorem to attack is:

On a good overlap patch, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch yields a branch-generated moving shear for which the two coupled ratios \(\Phi_{\gamma,\xi}\) and \(\Theta_{\gamma,\zeta}\) have a repeated nearby value pair. Show that this forces one of the already-listed centered mixed low-order obstruction types, or a lower-core tangency mechanism.

That is now much better aligned with the current draft than any raw factorization target, because:

- it uses the new “source-coupling theorem needed” lesson directly, 
- it is genuinely shear-sensitive,
- and it points toward parity transfer / centered mixed local classification, which your note already singled out as the likely reusable template on the mixed side. turn56file3

So the current best attack result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{single source determinants are exactly too weak; the mixed two-point branch must be attacked through coupled repeated-value ratios.}

That is the cleanest narrowing of the problem I can defend now.

The theorem to aim for is:

If there is a close exact mixed two-point bad branch with
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n})\to (m,m)
\]
and
\[
(\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n):=(\gamma_{12,n},\xi_{12,n},\zeta_{12,n})\to(\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*),
\]
then after a small correction of the source parameters one can produce nearby points
\[
a_n\neq u_n,\qquad a_n,u_n\to m,
\]
such that the **fixed** ratio map
\[
\mathcal F_{\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*}
\]
already has a repeated value:
\[
\mathcal F_{\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*}(a_n)
=
\mathcal F_{\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*}(u_n).
\]

That is the smallest live theorem I would attack now.

Why this is the right target:

If you can freeze the shear, then you are no longer in a moving-parameter problem. You get an honest fixed-source repeated-value problem, and then the new 3-point / shear-transfer apparatus becomes usable instead of just suggestive. That is the cleanest continuation of the attack I can defend now.

## Assistant (2026-04-20 20:58:28)

I’m testing the freeze-the-shear idea against the actual local formulas and the newer 3-point machinery, because the crucial question is whether the moving shear can be stabilized by the existing implicit-function structure, or whether one more source-coupling input is still missing.

_Thought for 3m 21s_

I pushed it one more step, and this is the best rigorous reduction I can get from the current draft.

The close mixed two-point branch can be **frozen to a fixed-shear critical point**.

That is stronger than the earlier “moving repeated values” formulation, and it lines up almost perfectly with the new nonmixed shear-transfer picture — but it also shows exactly why the branch is still not closed, because the nonmixed side now explicitly tells us that a critical branch alone is not yet a contradiction engine. turn58file1

Here is the theorem.

Let
\[
f_{\gamma}(h):=u_5(h)-\gamma\,c(h),\qquad
g_{\xi}(h):=v_5(h)-\xi\,c(h),\qquad
k_{\zeta}(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}-\zeta\,c(h),
\]
and on an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
define the fixed-shear coupled ratio map
\[
\mathcal R_{\gamma,\xi,\zeta}(h)
:=
\left(
\frac{f_{\gamma}(h)}{g_{\xi}(h)},
\frac{k_{\zeta}(h)}{g_{\xi}(h)}
\right).
\]

Now suppose there is a close exact mixed two-point bad branch
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\lambda_n),\qquad h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},\qquad h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to m\in U,
\]
with the usual branch-generated moving shears
\[
\gamma_n=\frac{e_{u,n}}{e_n},\qquad
\xi_n=\frac{e_{v,n}}{e_n},\qquad
\zeta_n=\frac{e_{\sigma,n}}{e_n},
\]
and assume, after passing to a subsequence,
\[
(\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n)\to(\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*).
\]

Then the exact transport identities
\[
f_{\gamma_n}(h_{1,n})=\lambda_n f_{\gamma_n}(h_{2,n}),\qquad
g_{\xi_n}(h_{1,n})=\lambda_n g_{\xi_n}(h_{2,n}),\qquad
k_{\zeta_n}(h_{1,n})=\lambda_n k_{\zeta_n}(h_{2,n})
\]
imply
\[
\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(h_{1,n})
=
\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(h_{2,n}).
\]

Write
\[
m_n:=\frac{h_{1,n}+h_{2,n}}{2},\qquad
\delta_n:=h_{2,n}-h_{1,n}.
\]
Because
\[
g_{\xi_*}(m)=v_5(m)-\xi_*c(m)\neq 0
\]
on a good \(M\neq 0\) patch — in fact the branch formula gives
\[
g_{\xi_*}(m)= -\,\frac{M(m)}{\alpha c(m)+c'(m)}
\]
when \(\lambda_n=1+\alpha\delta_n+O(\delta_n^2)\) — the ratio map is well-defined near \(m\). Then a symmetric Taylor expansion gives
\[
0
=
\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(m_n+\delta_n/2)
-
\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(m_n-\delta_n/2)
=
\delta_n\,\partial_h\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(m_n)
+
O(\delta_n^3).
\]
Hence
\[
\partial_h\mathcal R_{\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n}(m_n)=O(\delta_n^2),
\]
and passing to the limit gives
\[
\boxed{
\partial_h\mathcal R_{\gamma_*,\xi_*,\zeta_*}(m)=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, the fixed-shear pair satisfies the coupled source-Wronskian conditions
\[
\boxed{
W(g_{\xi_*},f_{\gamma_*})(m)=0,
\qquad
W(g_{\xi_*},k_{\zeta_*})(m)=0,
}
\]
because
\[
\left(\frac{f_\gamma}{g_\xi}\right)'=\frac{W(g_\xi,f_\gamma)}{g_\xi^2},
\qquad
\left(\frac{k_\zeta}{g_\xi}\right)'=\frac{W(g_\xi,k_\zeta)}{g_\xi^2}.
\]

So this is now the cleanest reduction:

A close exact mixed two-point bad branch forces a **fixed-shear coupled critical point** for the map
\[
h\longmapsto \left(\frac{u_5-\gamma c}{v_5-\xi c},\ \frac{\Delta_7/v_5-\zeta c}{v_5-\xi c}\right).
\]

That is the mixed analogue of the nonmixed critical-branch picture.

Why this matters

This is the first version of “freeze the moving shear” that I think is actually rigorous. It does not need a full source-linear factorization, and it does not collapse back to the old secant-minor no-go.

But it also shows exactly where the remaining gap is.

The latest nonmixed work proves that even there, the local critical branch / shear-transfer route reaches a ceiling: one needs a further source-coupling theorem to upgrade criticality into a rooted contradiction. The draft says this very explicitly. 

And that is exactly what happens here too.

What we get from the mixed two-point branch is:

- a fixed-shear critical point,
- i.e. simultaneous vanishing of two coupled Wronskians,

but **not yet** a rooted repeated-node tangency or a contradiction.

So the best current “next theorem” is no longer vague at all:

\[
\boxed{
\text{criticality-to-rootedness for the fixed-shear mixed ratio map.}
}
\]

In plain terms:

Show that on a good overlap patch, a simultaneous zero of
\[
W(v_5-\xi c,\ u_5-\gamma c)
\quad\text{and}\quad
W\!\left(v_5-\xi c,\ \frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}-\zeta c\right)
\]
coming from a branch-generated shear \((\gamma,\xi,\zeta)\) cannot occur unless it degenerates into one of the already-classified lower-core mechanisms or one of the centered mixed low-order obstruction types.

That is the smallest live target I trust now.

So the attack has advanced from:

- moving repeated values,

to

- fixed-shear coupled criticality,

and the draft’s new nonmixed ceiling results explain why that is meaningful progress but still not the finish line.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 00:04:22)

I’m checking the exact places in the latest TeX where the new shear-transfer and source-coupling results live, because the next step only matters if the fixed-shear criticality we just isolated really lines up with the current branch machinery rather than just sounding similar.

_Thought for 3m 15s_

I think the best attack now is a real second-order upgrade.

It still does not finish the branch, but it gets past the “criticality only” ceiling.

Work in the finite-shear regime, meaning
\[
\alpha\,c(m)+c'(m)\neq 0
\]
for the close branch expansion
\[
h_{1,n}=m_n-\frac{\delta_n}{2},\qquad
h_{2,n}=m_n+\frac{\delta_n}{2},\qquad
\lambda_n=1+\alpha\,\delta_n+\beta\,\delta_n^2+\chi\,\delta_n^3+O(\delta_n^4).
\]

As before, freeze the moving shear:
\[
f(h)=u_5(h)-\gamma c(h),\qquad
g(h)=v_5(h)-\xi c(h),\qquad
k(h)=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{v_5(h)}-\zeta c(h),
\]
where \((\gamma,\xi,\zeta)\) is the subsequential limit of the branch-generated shears. On a close exact mixed two-point bad branch, each \(F_n\in\{f_n,g_n,k_n\}\) satisfies
\[
F_n(h_{1,n})=\lambda_n\,F_n(h_{2,n}).
\]

Now Taylor-expand at \(m_n\). For a scalar \(F\),
\[
F\!\left(m-\frac{\delta}{2}\right)-\lambda\,F\!\left(m+\frac{\delta}{2}\right)=0
\]
gives, order by order,

\[
F'(m)+\alpha F(m)=0,
\]
\[
\beta F(m)+\frac{\alpha}{2}F'(m)=0,
\]
\[
\chi F(m)+\frac{\beta}{2}F'(m)+\frac{\alpha}{8}F''(m)+\frac1{24}F'''(m)=0.
\]

Using the first equation in the second gives
\[
\boxed{\beta=\frac{\alpha^2}{2}.}
\]

Using that again in the third gives
\[
\boxed{
F'''(m)+3\alpha F''(m)-6\alpha^3F(m)+24\chi\,F(m)=0.
}
\]

So in the finite-shear regime, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch forces **every one** of
\[
F\in\{f,g,k\}
\]
to satisfy the same first-order and third-order transport law at the same point \(m\), with the same \(\alpha,\chi\).

Equivalently, since in the finite-shear regime
\[
g(m)=-\frac{M(m)}{\alpha c(m)+c'(m)}\neq 0
\]
on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,M\neq 0\}\), and likewise generically for \(f,k\) after shrinking if needed, you get the common cubic transport invariant
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\alpha(f)(m)=\mathcal T_\alpha(g)(m)=\mathcal T_\alpha(k)(m)=-24\chi,
}
\]
where
\[
\mathcal T_\alpha(F):=
\frac{F''' + 3\alpha F'' - 6\alpha^3 F}{F}.
\]

Together with the earlier first-order frozen-shear criticality
\[
W(g,f)(m)=0,\qquad W(g,k)(m)=0,
\]
this gives the stronger package
\[
\boxed{
W(g,f)(m)=W(g,k)(m)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal T_\alpha(f)(m)=\mathcal T_\alpha(g)(m)=\mathcal T_\alpha(k)(m).
}
\]

That is the strongest reduction I can honestly defend now.

Why this matters:

Earlier we only had fixed-shear criticality, and that was too weak. The latest nonmixed progress makes clear that a critical branch by itself is not enough; the missing input has to be a real source-coupling theorem. turn61file2

This new third-order package is exactly that kind of source-coupled condition:

- it is shear-sensitive,
- it survives the secant-minor and quotient no-go results,
- and it is strictly stronger than repeated nearby values or single-determinant vanishing.

It is also the first place where a genuine incompatibility with the newer mixed low-order obstruction list looks plausible, because that list is already organized by low-order exact coefficients and centered parity structure, not just by first derivatives. 

So my best current next theorem is:

**Transport-to-cubic-jet theorem for fixed-shear mixed ratios.**  
Show that on a good overlap patch, no branch-generated fixed shear can satisfy simultaneously
\[
W(g,f)=W(g,k)=0
\]
and
\[
\mathcal T_\alpha(f)=\mathcal T_\alpha(g)=\mathcal T_\alpha(k)
\]
unless the branch degenerates into one of the already-classified centered mixed low-order obstruction types or a lower-core tangency mechanism.

That is the smallest live target I trust now.

One caveat: the subcase
\[
\alpha c(m)+c'(m)=0
\]
is the “infinite-shear” regime. The formulas above are for the finite-shear regime. That exceptional case should be split off and handled separately; if anything, it ought to be more rigid, not less.

So the attack has advanced from:

- moving repeated values,
- to fixed-shear criticality,
- to a shared third-order transport invariant.

That is real progress, and it is the first reduction that feels strong enough to plausibly hook into the paper’s current mixed low-order / parity machinery rather than running into the old determinant ceiling again.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 01:11:07)

I’m checking the current draft text around the mixed low-order obstruction list and the newer shear-transfer results, because the next step only works if the third-order transport package can actually be matched to those existing low-order exact obstruction types rather than inventing a parallel framework.

_Thought for 7m 39s_

Yes. I think the best attack now is a real second-order upgrade, and it is better than the “fixed-shear criticality” reduction.

That is exactly the environment where this next reduction makes sense. turn64file1

Here is the sharp statement.

On an overlap patch, write the lifted curve in the \(v_5\)-gauge as
\[
Q_v(x)=(Y(x),x,\sigma_v(x)).
\]
From the previous attack, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch yields branch-generated shears \((\gamma_n,\xi_n,\zeta_n)\) and interaction points \(P_n\) lying on the secant lines through
\[
Q_v(x_{1,n}),\qquad Q_v(x_{2,n}),
\]
with \(x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a\), and \(P_n\to P_*\) on the tangent line at \(Q_v(a)\). The only missing step is to freeze the moving secant picture to a fixed \(P_*\). If that freeze lemma holds, then a standard symmetric secant expansion gives a much stronger rooted condition.

Write
\[
P_*=Q_v(a)+t\,Q_v'(a).
\]
Then the condition that \(P_*\) lies on secants through nearby symmetric points \(Q_v(a-h)\), \(Q_v(a+h)\) implies
\[
(Q_v(a-h)-P_*)\wedge (Q_v(a+h)-P_*)=0.
\]
Expanding in \(h\),
\[
(Q_v(a-h)-P_*)\wedge (Q_v(a+h)-P_*)
=
-h^3\,Q_v'(a)\wedge\Bigl(Q_v''(a)+\frac t3\,Q_v'''(a)\Bigr)+O(h^5).
\]
So a necessary rooted condition is
\[
Q_v'(a)\wedge\Bigl(Q_v''(a)+\frac t3\,Q_v'''(a)\Bigr)=0.
\]

Now because the middle coordinate of \(Q_v\) is literally \(x\), we have
\[
Q_v'(a)=(Y'(a),1,\sigma_v'(a)),\qquad
Q_v''(a)=(Y''(a),0,\sigma_v''(a)),\qquad
Q_v'''(a)=(Y'''(a),0,\sigma_v'''(a)).
\]
The second coordinate of \(Q_v''+\frac t3Q_v'''\) is therefore \(0\), so for it to be parallel to \(Q_v'(a)\), it must actually vanish. Hence the rooted condition is
\[
\boxed{
Y''(a)+\frac t3\,Y'''(a)=0,
\qquad
\sigma_v''(a)+\frac t3\,\sigma_v'''(a)=0.
}
\]

This is much stronger than the earlier criticality condition. It is genuinely second-order rootedness.

When \(Y''(a)\) and \(\sigma_v''(a)\) are both nonzero, this pins down the tangent-line parameter:
\[
t=-3\,\frac{Y''(a)}{Y'''(a)}=-3\,\frac{\sigma_v''(a)}{\sigma_v'''(a)}.
\]
So on the generic overlap region, a close exact mixed two-point branch would force the scalar identity
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_v(a):=Y''(a)\,\sigma_v'''(a)-Y'''(a)\,\sigma_v''(a)=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest new obstruction I can get.

It is better than the earlier determinant and secant-ratio packages because it is shear-sensitive and second-order. It is also exactly the kind of source-coupling refinement the latest draft is signaling is still missing: not more generic determinant algebra, but a rooted repeated-node theorem. 

This also meshes well with the current mixed low-order picture. If one of \(Y''\) or \(\sigma_v''\) vanishes to low order, then you are no longer in the generic rooted regime above; instead you fall into the already-isolated finite mixed low-order obstruction list, the one organized by the mixed coefficients \(\kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2}\) or equivalently the Wronskian-order pairs \((1,2),(1,4),(2,4)\). So the branch is now reduced to:

either the generic rooted equation
\[
\Omega_v=0,
\]
or one of the explicit mixed low-order cases the draft already knows it must handle separately. 

So my best current theorem target is:

If the moving-shear branch can be frozen to a fixed tangent-line point \(P_*\), then every close exact mixed two-point bad branch on a good overlap patch reduces either to
\[
\Omega_v=0
\]
at the limiting source point, or to one of the finite explicit mixed low-order obstruction types.

That is the strongest reduction I trust now.

What still remains missing is the freeze lemma itself: turning the branch-generated moving interaction point into a fixed secant/tangent-point problem. Without that, I do not think the branch is closed yet. But once that lemma lands, the problem is no longer vague. It becomes a very concrete rooted-geometry obstruction tied to one scalar \(\Omega_v\) plus the already-explicit mixed low-order list.

Here is the exact algebra.

For an exact bad two-pair core on an overlap patch, write
\[
\Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S,
\]
and let \(e_\lambda\) be the septic scalar coming from the same \(v_7=0\)-patch rewrite, so that the exact two-point equations are
\[
c_1-\Lambda c_2+e=0,
\]
\[
u_{5,1}-\Lambda u_{5,2}+e_u=0,
\]
\[
v_{5,1}-\Lambda v_{5,2}+e_v=0,
\]
\[
\lambda_1-\Lambda \lambda_2+e_\lambda=0,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

Now, as long as \(e_\lambda\neq 0\), define the branch-generated **\(\lambda\)-shears**
\[
\eta:=\frac{e}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\gamma:=\frac{e_u}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\xi:=\frac{e_v}{e_\lambda}.
\]

Then the four exact equations immediately collapse to the exact repeated-source transport system
\[
(c-\eta\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda\,(c-\eta\lambda)(h_2),
\]
\[
(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda\,(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_2),
\]
\[
(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda\,(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_2).
\]

This is the first genuinely good reformulation. It says:

a close exact mixed two-point bad branch is exactly a branch-generated repeated-source transport problem for **\(\lambda\)-sheared source functions**.

That is much better than the older \(c\)-shear route, because it lands directly on the objects already built into the draft.

The key structural payoff is immediate. Since the draft already has
\[
J_c=0,
\qquad
J_{v_5}=0,
\]
one gets
\[
J_{c-\eta\lambda}=-\eta\,J_\lambda,
\qquad
J_{v_5-\xi\lambda}=-\xi\,J_\lambda,
\qquad
J_{u_5-\gamma\lambda}=J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda.
\]

So every source-level local invariant of the frozen branch reduces to the same mixed pair
\[
(J_\lambda,\ J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda).
\]

That is the real reduction.

In particular, if a close branch can be frozen so that
\[
(\eta_n,\gamma_n,\xi_n)\to(\eta_*,\gamma_*,\xi_*),
\]
then the fixed-shear limiting problem is governed by
\[
f_{\gamma_*}=u_5-\gamma_*\lambda,
\qquad
g_{\eta_*}=c-\eta_*\lambda,
\qquad
h_{\xi_*}=v_5-\xi_*\lambda,
\]
with
\[
J_{f_{\gamma_*}}=J_{u_5}-\gamma_*J_\lambda,
\qquad
J_{g_{\eta_*}},J_{h_{\xi_*}}\in \mathbf C\,J_\lambda.
\]

That means the entire local mixed branch reduces to the same Wronskian-ratio world the draft already understands:
\[
\mathcal Z_\gamma:=\frac{J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda}{J_\lambda}
=\mathcal Z-\gamma.
\]

So the dangerous local orders for the frozen mixed branch are **exactly** the dangerous local orders of the mixed list already in the draft:
\[
(\operatorname{ord}J_\lambda,\operatorname{ord}(J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda))
=
(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,4),
\]
equivalently the same coefficient list
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

That is the strongest attack result so far.

It does **not** finish the branch, because one theorem is still missing:

you need a **freeze-the-\(\lambda\)-shear lemma** saying that a close exact mixed two-point bad branch yields a nearby fixed \(\gamma\) repeated-source problem for
\[
f_\gamma=u_5-\gamma\lambda
\]
and its coupled companions.

But once that freeze lemma lands, the branch is no longer vague at all. It reduces to the already-known mixed local obstruction list plus the existing shear-transfer/source-coupling ceiling. In other words:

- the old \(c\)-shear attack was not aligned with the draft;
- the new \(\lambda\)-shear attack is aligned exactly with the draft’s current mixed Wronskian and shear-transfer framework. turn68file2

So my best current theorem target is:

**Freeze-the-\(\lambda\)-shear theorem.**

\[
u_5-\gamma\lambda
\]
with coupled transport in
\[
c-\eta\lambda,\qquad v_5-\xi\lambda.
\]

If that is proved, the local branch is forced into the exact mixed low-order obstruction framework already isolated in the draft. That is the first attack that really feels like it is using the paper’s new progress rather than fighting it.
