## Assistant (2026-04-21 01:26:23)

I’m going straight into the latest TeX around the mixed Wronskian-order package and the newer shear-transfer/source-coupling material, because the question now is whether the \(\lambda\)-shear can actually be frozen using machinery the draft already has, rather than invented from scratch.

_Thought for 6m 34s_

I think there is a real correction to the last route, and it is useful.

The earlier “freeze-the-\(\lambda\)-shear reduces everything to \(J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda\)” was too optimistic.

What the branch actually gives is a **three-function repeated-source transport system**, and when you freeze that system the first intrinsic consequence is not a single mixed Wronskian-ratio condition, but a new **source-coupled determinant identity**.

Here is the clean derivation.

Set
\[
A:=c-\eta \lambda,\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi \lambda,\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma \lambda,
\]
where
\[
\eta=\frac{e}{e_\lambda},\qquad
\xi=\frac{e_v}{e_\lambda},\qquad
\gamma=\frac{e_u}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

For an exact bad two-pair core, the exact equations are equivalent to
\[
A(h_1)=\Lambda\,A(h_2),\qquad
B(h_1)=\Lambda\,B(h_2),\qquad
F(h_1)=\Lambda\,F(h_2),
\]
with
\[
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}.
\]

Now take a close branch and assume the frozen-shear subsequential limit exists:
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\eta_n,\xi_n,\gamma_n)\to (m,m,\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*).
\]
As in the previous transport expansions, writing
\[
\Lambda_n=1+\alpha \delta_n+O(\delta_n^2),
\qquad
\delta_n=h_{2,n}-h_{1,n},
\]
gives
\[
A'(m)+\alpha A(m)=0,\qquad
B'(m)+\alpha B(m)=0,\qquad
F'(m)+\alpha F(m)=0.
\]
So the first two rows of the source determinant for the frozen triple \((A,B,F)\) are proportional at \(m\), hence
\[
\boxed{
W(A,B,F)(m)=0,
}
\]
where
\[
W(p,q,r):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
p&q&r\\
p'&q'&r'\\
p''&q''&r''
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Now expand by multilinearity:
\[
W(c-\eta\lambda,\ v_5-\xi\lambda,\ u_5-\gamma\lambda).
\]
Because any determinant with two identical \(\lambda\)-columns vanishes, the only surviving terms are
\[
W(c,v_5,u_5)-\gamma W(c,v_5,\lambda)-\xi W(c,\lambda,u_5)-\eta W(\lambda,v_5,u_5).
\]
So the frozen branch forces
\[
\boxed{
J_{u_5}(m)-\gamma_*J_\lambda(m)-\xi_*K_1(m)-\eta_*K_2(m)=0,
}
\]
with
\[
K_1:=W(c,\lambda,u_5),
\qquad
K_2:=W(\lambda,v_5,u_5).
\]

That is the first genuinely new mixed source-coupling identity I trust.

It is better than the earlier reductions for two reasons.

First, it is **shear-sensitive**. The branch-generated \((\eta,\xi,\gamma)\) survive. Nothing collapses back to a secant-minor package.

Second, it uses exactly the kind of extra source-coupling the new draft says is still missing on the nonmixed side too: not more generic determinant algebra, but a theorem tying the live branch to a specific RH-specific source-coupled quantity. The draft’s current state is still that the 2-point burden is source-level and the nonmixed route has reached a genuine source-coupling ceiling, so this is the right kind of object to look for. turn70file0

There is also a geometric rewrite on a good \(v_5\)-patch. Write
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c},
\qquad
M=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]
Then
\[
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\qquad
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\]
and a direct calculation gives
\[
K_1
=
\frac{M^3}{c^3}\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x\bigr),
\]
while
\[
K_2
=
-\frac{M^3}{c^3}
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
Y&x&S\\
Y_x&1&S_x\\
Y_{xx}&0&S_{xx}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the frozen branch condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
Y_{xx}-\gamma_* S_{xx}-\xi_*(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x)
+\eta_*\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
Y&x&S\\
Y_x&1&S_x\\
Y_{xx}&0&S_{xx}
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest current form. It shows that the mixed 2-point branch is not governed just by the old ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\]
but by a **three-parameter source-coupled relation** involving:

- the mixed low-order Wronskian ratio piece \(J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda\),
- a first extra coupling term \(K_1\),
- and an osculating/differential-geometric term \(K_2\).

That is precisely why the newer differential-geometry and nonmixed 4-point progress matters: the osculating determinant and source-coupling themes are now showing up in the mixed 2-point branch itself, not just nearby branches. turn70file1

So the best current attack target is now very specific:

prove a theorem saying that on a good overlap patch, no branch-generated frozen shear \((\eta,\xi,\gamma)\) can satisfy
\[
J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda-\xi K_1-\eta K_2=0
\]
along a genuine close mixed 2-point branch, except by falling into one of the already-isolated mixed low-order obstruction types.

That is better than the earlier target because it is no longer just “some source-level theorem.” It is one explicit source-coupled identity, and it is the first one that genuinely uses the new shear-transfer / osculating-geometry progress rather than fighting around it.

A_n(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n A_n(h_{2,n}),\qquad

F_n(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n F_n(h_{2,n}).

As long as one denominator stays nonzero at the limit point — in the finite-shear regime this is the generic case, and if one denominator vanishes you split into the complementary chart — you can divide. For example, if \(A_*(m)\neq 0\), then
\[
\frac{B_n}{A_n}(h_{1,n})=\frac{B_n}{A_n}(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
\frac{F_n}{A_n}(h_{1,n})=\frac{F_n}{A_n}(h_{2,n}).
\]

A symmetric midpoint expansion then gives
\[
\left(\frac{B_*}{A_*}\right)'(m)=0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{F_*}{A_*}\right)'(m)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
W(A_*,B_*)(m)=0,
\qquad
W(A_*,F_*)(m)=0.
\]

So a close exact mixed two-point branch forces a **fixed-\(\lambda\)-shear coupled critical point**.

That is a better reduction than the earlier secant or \(c\)-shear formulations, because it is both shear-sensitive and already aligned with the draft’s mixed low-order Wronskian framework.

\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+a\,c+b\,v_5+\gamma\lambda,
\]
the mixed local determinant changes by

\]
because \(J_c=J_{v_5}=0\). So once the branch is frozen, the only genuinely new mixed local datum is
\[

\]
which is exactly the object whose low-order behavior is already encoded by the existing mixed obstruction list \((\kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2})\) or equivalently the Wronskian-order pairs \((1,2),(1,4),(2,4)\). That is the crucial simplification.

1. the branch falls into one of the already-listed mixed low-order obstruction types; or  
2. it degenerates into a lower-core tangency mechanism already handled by the lifted 3-point / 4-point geometry.

That is now the smallest live theorem I trust.

- the old determinant-only and quotient-only routes are dead;
- the \(\lambda\)-shear formulation is the right one;

This is the first genuinely new mixed source-coupling scalar identity I trust.

It is better than the previous reductions for two reasons.

First, it is **shear-sensitive**: the branch-generated \((\eta,\xi,\gamma)\) survive; nothing collapses back to the secant-minor or quotient-blind package.

Second, it is exactly the kind of extra source-coupling relation the current draft is telling us must exist if the remaining branches are to close. The handoff/status note still says the 2-point burden is source-level, while the mixed local side is already encoded by the Wronskian-order obstruction list and the nonmixed side now needs a genuine source-coupling theorem beyond generic determinant algebra. turn75file0

There is also a useful rewrite on a good \(v_5\)-patch. With
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c},\qquad
M=cv_5'-c'v_5,
\]
the draft already organizes the mixed local list by
\[
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\qquad
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\]
so the dangerous mixed cases are exactly the finite order pairs
\[
(\operatorname{ord}J_\lambda,\operatorname{ord}J_{u_5})=(1,2),(1,4),(2,4),
\]
equivalently the explicit \(\kappa_{1,1},\kappa_{1,3},\kappa_{2,2}\) list. 

In these coordinates,
\[
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\qquad
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\]
and a direct calculation gives
\[
K_1=\frac{M^3}{c^3}\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x\bigr),
\]
while
\[
K_2=
-\frac{M^3}{c^3}
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
Y&x&S\\
Y_x&1&S_x\\
Y_{xx}&0&S_{xx}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

So the frozen-branch condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
Y_{xx}-\gamma_*S_{xx}
-\xi_*\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x\bigr)
+\eta_*
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
Y&x&S\\
Y_x&1&S_x\\
Y_{xx}&0&S_{xx}
\end{pmatrix}
=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest form yet. It shows the mixed two-point branch is governed not just by the old ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\]
but by a **three-parameter source-coupled relation** involving:

- the mixed Wronskian-ratio piece \(J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda\),
- a first extra coupling term \(K_1\),
- and an osculating/differential-geometric term \(K_2\).

So the next attack is no longer vague. It is:

prove that on a good overlap patch, no branch-generated frozen shear \((\eta,\xi,\gamma)\) can satisfy
\[
J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda-\xi K_1-\eta K_2=0
\]
along a genuine close mixed two-point branch, except by falling into one of the already-isolated mixed low-order obstruction types or a lower-core tangency mechanism.

That is the smallest live theorem I trust now. It is the first one that really uses the paper’s new shear-transfer / source-coupling / osculating-geometry progress rather than fighting around it.

\[

\right).

\[

On any region where

S\neq 0,\qquad S'\neq 0,\qquad K_v\neq 0,

the first coordinate \(\Phi_1\) is locally injective. Therefore \(\Phi(h_1)=\Phi(h_2)\) with \(h_1\neq h_2\) is impossible there.

That is a much smaller target than anything we had earlier.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 02:23:18)

_Thought for 6m 17s_

Yes — there is a real correction and a real improvement.

The correction is that my earlier “fixed map
\[
\Phi(h)=\left(x-\frac{S}{S'},\,Y-\frac{SY'}{S'}\right)
\]
has repeated nearby values” was too strong. That used pointwise formulas for the frozen shears that only hold at the limiting point, not globally.

What survives **exactly** is better framed projectively.

For the lifted \(v\)-patch curve
\[
Q_v(h)=(Y(h),x(h),S(h)),
\qquad
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\quad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\quad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
an exact bad mixed two-point core gives the branch-generated ratios
\[
\frac{B}{A},\qquad \frac{F}{A},
\]
and those are exactly the affine coordinates of the **secant shadow** of the pair \((h_1,h_2)\) on the plane \(S=0\):
\[
\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
=
\biggl(
\frac{x_1S_2-x_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\ \frac{Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1}{S_2-S_1}
\biggr).
\]

The projective version is the cleaner invariant:
\[
\boxed{
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1].
}
\]

As \(h_2\to h_1=a\), this converges to the **projective tangent shadow**
\[
\boxed{
\mathbf\Pi(a)=
[x(a)S'(a)-S(a):\ Y(a)S'(a)-S(a)Y'(a):\ S'(a)].
}
\]

That is the first genuinely robust geometric object I trust.

Now the useful new fact:

If you differentiate \(\mathbf\Pi\), a short computation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)\wedge \mathbf\Pi'(a)
=
S(a)\,\bigl(\,S'(a)Y''(a)-S''(a)Y'(a),\ S''(a),\ *\,\bigr).
\]

So the **second component** is
\[
S(a)\,S''(a).
\]

Hence the projective tangent-shadow map is immersive whenever
\[
S(a)\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
S''(a)\neq 0.
\]

Because on a good \(v_5\)-patch the draft already identifies
\[
K_v=(x')^3S'',
\]
this means:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf\Pi\ \text{is projectively immersive away from}\ \{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
}
\]

That is a genuine improvement over my earlier reduction. It removes the spurious exceptional slice
\[
\{S'=0\}
\]
entirely. Projective compactification regularizes it.

So the mixed 2-point branch is now reduced to two explicit geometric accumulation loci:

\[
\boxed{
\{S=0\}\qquad\text{or}\qquad \{K_v=0\}.
}
\]

That lines up much better with the current draft than the older \(S'\)-based formulations. The 2-point burden is still source-level, while the \(K_v\)-branch is already one of the mature derivative-geometric parts of the paper. turn84file2

What this does **not** yet prove is exclusion. A family of secant-shadow points can still converge to a tangent shadow point without forcing a contradiction. So this is not closure.

But it is a better reduction:

- the exact invariant is the projective secant-shadow \(\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)\), not the affine \(\Phi\)-map;
- the only remaining geometric exceptional loci are \(S=0\) and \(K_v=0\);
- so the next attack should split exactly there.

The best next steps are now:

1. prove that accumulation on \(K_v=0\) is absorbed by the existing lifted 3-point branch, which the current draft already treats as the derivative-geometric locus for shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuits; 

2. analyze the septic-zero slice
\[
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=0
\]
and show that a close mixed 2-point branch cannot accumulate there without already entering the existing mixed low-order obstruction framework.

So the branch is not closed, but the geometry is cleaner now than before.

## 2) Add the two main audit/no-go remarks after `\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}`

Insert **immediately after** `\end{remark}` for `rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Audit: even-amplitude obstruction for the naive source-summed model]
\label{rem:audit-even-amplitude-obstruction-naive-source-summed-two-point}
The most obvious attempt to prove the source-level merger theorem is to insert a
weighted one-atom datum
\[
q_{a,h}=a\,q_h,
\qquad
\Phi_{a,h}=a\,\Phi_h
\]
directly into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas, whiten, and
then extract the cubic/quintic/septic outputs. This route cannot by itself
prove the required one-atom linearity
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]

Indeed the explicit corrected block formulas have the form
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s),
\qquad
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s),
\]
so after whitening the overall factor of $a$ cancels:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}\,
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)\,
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
Hence every fixed finite-order coefficient extracted from the whitened block is
an even analytic function of the source weight $a$. In particular, the naive
source-summed corrected block package cannot satisfy analytic one-atom linearity
or coincident-atom additivity unless it vanishes identically. So the remaining
two-point theorem must be proved using a different lift/transport object, not
the raw source-summed whitened coefficients themselves.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Audit: quotient and single-determinant routes are shear-blind]
\label{rem:audit-shear-blind-two-point-determinantal-routes}
On the mixed two-point branch, any route based only on cubic/quintic source
minors,
the septic quotient class,
or the pointwise patch gauges $v_7=0$ and $u_7=0$ is exactly blind to the
repeated-node shear parameter.

For an exact bad two-pair core, the cubic/quintic defect vector has the form
\[
d=\Lambda s_2-s_1,
\qquad
\Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
s_i=(c_i,u_{5,i},v_{5,i}),
\]
so
\[
s_2\wedge d=s_1\wedge s_2
\]
is independent of $\Lambda$. Likewise, any pointwise representative extracted
only from the septic quotient class and $A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}$ carries no more
information than the same determinant scalar already seen by the quotient. Thus
the remaining mixed two-point burden is genuinely source-coupled rather than
quotient-determinantal.
\end{remark}
```

## 3) Add the new mixed two-point derivative-geometry remarks after `\label{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list}`

Insert **immediately after** `\end{remark}` for `rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Work in progress: exact $\lambda$-shear transport on the mixed two-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-exact-lambda-shear-transport-mixed-two-point}
On an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
For an exact bad two-pair core write
\[
\Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S,
\]
and define \(e_\lambda\) by the exact transport identity
\[
\lambda(h_1)-\Lambda\,\lambda(h_2)+e_\lambda=0.
\]
Whenever \(e_\lambda\neq 0\), set
\[
\eta:=\frac{e}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\xi:=\frac{e_v}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\gamma:=\frac{e_u}{e_\lambda},
\]
and
\[
A:=c-\eta\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma\lambda.
\]
Then the exact mixed two-point equations are equivalent to the repeated-source
transport system
\[
A(h_1)=\Lambda\,A(h_2),
\qquad
B(h_1)=\Lambda\,B(h_2),
\qquad
F(h_1)=\Lambda\,F(h_2).
\]
So a close exact mixed two-point bad branch is naturally a branch-generated
repeated-source transport problem for \(\lambda\)-sheared source functions.
This is the shear-sensitive source-level formulation that matches the mixed
Wronskian-order bookkeeping already built into the draft.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: projective secant shadow and the remaining mixed two-point accumulation loci]
\label{rem:wip-projective-secant-shadow-mixed-two-point}
On a good \(v_5\)-patch use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate and write
\[
Q_v(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
For a pair \((h_1,h_2)\) define its projective secant shadow on the plane
\(S=0\) by
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1].
\]
As \(h_2\to h_1=a\), this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\Big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct computation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on a good \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
this means that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact
mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit exceptional
loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already forced either into the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or into the lifted \(K_v=0\) curvature geometry that
underlies the three-point branch.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Structural mixed overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
the first genuinely nontrivial mixed overlap coupling scalar can be written as
\[
\mathcal G
:=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
Hence \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch contained in
\(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish identically
there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice built into \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet close the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current attack.
\end{remark}
```

## 4) Replace `\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}`

Replace the whole remark with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant $\widehat\Psi$, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} isolates the exact
finite-order source criterion that would close the two-point branch on compact
good patches.

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic. There are now three precise conditional routes on
the two-point side.

First, the stronger finite-order source-level merger route would force the
quadratic defect estimates and hence the defect-scale closeness theorem on good
patches.

Second, the weaker quotient-diagonal route would already exclude exact close
two-point bad cores on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$ if one had a genuine
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse.

Third, on a good overlap patch in the mixed regime, the derivative-geometric
attack now naturally passes through the $\lambda$-sheared source transport
system
\[
(c-\eta\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(c-\eta\lambda)(h_2),
\qquad
(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_2),
\qquad
(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
and, after freezing a $\lambda$-shear subsequence, the associated projective
secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

So the genuinely remaining two-point work is either the verification of the
finite-order source-level merger criterion, the construction of the actual
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse,
or the source-coupling analysis of the mixed $\lambda$-shear route on those
explicit exceptional loci. Beyond that lie the genuinely multi-pair interaction
bookkeeping through orders $3,5,7$, the local lifted $3/4$-point analysis for
close-point branches on the $v_5\neq 0$ and parallel $u_5\neq 0$ patches, and
the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}
```

## 5) Replace item 1 of `\label{rem:live-attack-routes}`

Replace the current item 1 with:

```latex
\item
\textbf{Two-point branch: three live conditional routes.}
The stronger finite-order route is still
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}: prove that the actual
corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package is analytic on small two-atom
data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
The weaker exact route is
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}, which would
already remove exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of
\(\{c\neq 0\}\) from continuity and diagonal collapse of the actual corrected
two-atom quotient germ.

What is now ruled out is the naive source-summed corrected-block route: its
extracted one-atom finite-order coefficients are even in the source weight and
therefore cannot supply the required linear merger law. On the mixed side,
determinant-only and quotient-only arguments are likewise shear-blind. The
genuinely new derivative-geometric lane is the $\lambda$-shear route on a good
overlap patch, where
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
A=c-\eta\lambda,\quad
B=v_5-\xi\lambda,\quad
F=u_5-\gamma\lambda
\]
satisfy exact repeated-source transport along the branch. After freezing a
$\lambda$-shear subsequence, the associated projective secant shadow can
accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
So the remaining two-point work is either finite-order source-level merger,
quotient-diagonal continuity/diagonal collapse, or source-coupled control of
the mixed $\lambda$-shear exceptional loci.
```

_Thought for 3m 55s_

I see two stale families that are worth fixing before the compact pass.

The first is any wording that still says the finite-order source-level package has already closed the two-point branch on compact good patches. The later attack overturned that: the minimal finite-order criterion is still the right algebraic route, but the naive source-summed corrected-block model is blocked by the even-in-amplitude obstruction, so the two-point branch is not closed there yet. turn93file3turn93file5

The second is any mixed two-point wording still built around the older affine \(\Phi\)-map, the exceptional slice \(\{S=0\}\cup\{S_x=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\), or the intermediate \(K_1,K_2\) source-coupled identity as the final package. The later attack improved that: the cleaner invariant is the projective secant shadow, and the remaining mixed exceptional loci reduce to
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
That is the version I would now keep. turn92file4turn94file0

So here is the pass I would make.

First, **delete** the entire contents of these three remarks if they are currently present:

- `rem:wip-exact-lambda-shear-transport-mixed-two-point`
- `rem:wip-projective-secant-shadow-mixed-two-point`
- `rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point`

Also delete or downgrade any later text that treats
\[
J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda-\xi K_1-\eta K_2=0
\]
or
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_x=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}

as the final mixed two-point package. Those were useful intermediate reductions, but the projective-shadow formulation is cleaner and stronger. turn92file5turn94file0

Then insert the following **single compact theorem/remark package** where the first of those deleted remarks currently sits.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Conditional mixed \(\lambda\)-shear reduction on an overlap patch]
\label{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
Let
\[
U\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a good overlap patch. Set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y:=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S:=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\Lambda_n),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in U,
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to m\in U,
\]
and that along a subsequence the branch-generated \(\lambda\)-shears
\[
\eta_n:=\frac{e_n}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\xi_n:=\frac{e_{v,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\gamma_n:=\frac{e_{u,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}}
\]
converge to
\[
(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*).
\]
Set
\[
A:=c-\eta_*\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi_*\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma_*\lambda.
\]

Then the frozen branch satisfies repeated-source transport
\[
A(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nA(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
B(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nB(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
F(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nF(h_{2,n}).
\]
Moreover the branch determines the projective secant shadow
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
:=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1],
\]
and as \(h_2\to h_1=a\) this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
:=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive wherever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on the \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
any such close exact mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The exact mixed two-point equations in \(\lambda\)-sheared form are
\[
(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}).
\]
Passing to the frozen subsequence gives the transport system for \(A,B,F\).

Now
\[
A=c(1-\eta_*S),
\qquad
B=c(x-\xi_*S),
\qquad
F=c(Y-\gamma_*S),
\]
so the branch equations imply repeated nearby values of the pair of affine
coordinates
\[
\left(\frac{B}{A},\frac{F}{A}\right).
\]
Eliminating \(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*\) gives the standard secant-shadow formulas
\[
\frac{B}{A}
=
\frac{x_1S_2-x_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\qquad
\frac{F}{A}
=
\frac{Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\]
hence the projective secant shadow \(\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)\). Its limit as
\(h_2\to h_1=a\) is the projective tangent shadow \(\mathbf\Pi(a)\).

Differentiating \(\mathbf\Pi\) in the local \(x\)-coordinate gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Therefore \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever \(S\neq 0\) and
\(S_{xx}\neq 0\). On a close bad branch the secant shadows converge to tangent
shadows, so accumulation is possible only where immersion fails, i.e. on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_{xx}=0\}.
\]
Finally, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
so \(\{S_{xx}=0\}=\{K_v=0\}\) on \(U\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Useful overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On the same overlap patch, set
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u'.
\]
Then \(\mathcal G\) admits the exact factorization
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
In particular, \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch
contained in \(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice carried by \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet exclude the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
genuinely nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current
attack.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
shows that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact mixed
two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already reduced either to the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or to the lifted curvature locus \(K_v=0\). The
remaining unresolved work is to show that accumulation on \(S=0\) either falls
into the existing mixed low-order obstruction types or transfers into a
lower-core tangency mechanism, while accumulation on \(K_v=0\) is absorbed by
the existing lifted three-point branch machinery.
\end{remark}
```

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant \(\widehat\Psi\), and
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} still isolates the
exact finite-order source criterion that would close the two-point branch on
compact good patches.

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic. There are now three precise conditional routes on
the two-point side.

First, the stronger finite-order source-level merger route would force the
quadratic defect estimates and hence the defect-scale closeness theorem on good
patches.

Second, the weaker quotient-diagonal route would already exclude exact close
two-point bad cores on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\) if one had a genuine
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse.

Third, on a good overlap patch in the mixed regime, the derivative-geometric
attack passes through the \(\lambda\)-sheared transport system
\[
(c-\eta\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(c-\eta\lambda)(h_2),\qquad
(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_2),\qquad
(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_2),
\]
with

\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad

\]
and, after freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, the associated projective
secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

for close-point branches on the \(v_5\neq 0\) and parallel \(u_5\neq 0\)
patches, and the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}

## 5) Insert the compact mixed \(\lambda\)-shear package in one place

Since the current file does **not** seem to contain the three earlier remarks as separate labeled remarks, the cleanest insertion point is:

**immediately after**
```latex
\end{remark}
```
for
```latex
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
```

Insert this whole block there:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Conditional mixed \(\lambda\)-shear reduction on an overlap patch]
\label{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
Let
\[
U\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a good overlap patch. Set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y:=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S:=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\Lambda_n),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in U,
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to m\in U,
\]
and that along a subsequence the branch-generated \(\lambda\)-shears
\[
\eta_n:=\frac{e_n}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\xi_n:=\frac{e_{v,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\gamma_n:=\frac{e_{u,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}}
\]
converge to
\[
(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*).
\]
Set
\[
A:=c-\eta_*\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi_*\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma_*\lambda.
\]

Then the frozen branch satisfies repeated-source transport
\[
A(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nA(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
B(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nB(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
F(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nF(h_{2,n}).
\]
Moreover the branch determines the projective secant shadow
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
:=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1],
\]
and as \(h_2\to h_1=a\) this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
:=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive wherever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on the \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
any such close exact mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The exact mixed two-point equations in \(\lambda\)-sheared form are
\[
(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}).
\]
Passing to the frozen subsequence gives the transport system for \(A,B,F\).

Now
\[
A=c(1-\eta_*S),
\qquad
B=c(x-\xi_*S),
\qquad
F=c(Y-\gamma_*S),
\]
so the branch equations imply repeated nearby values of the pair of affine
coordinates
\[
\left(\frac{B}{A},\frac{F}{A}\right).
\]
Eliminating \(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*\) gives the standard secant-shadow formulas
\[
\frac{B}{A}
=
\frac{x_1S_2-x_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\qquad
\frac{F}{A}
=
\frac{Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\]
hence the projective secant shadow \(\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)\). Its limit as
\(h_2\to h_1=a\) is the projective tangent shadow \(\mathbf\Pi(a)\).

Differentiating \(\mathbf\Pi\) in the local \(x\)-coordinate gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Therefore \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever \(S\neq 0\) and
\(S_{xx}\neq 0\). On a close bad branch the secant shadows converge to tangent
shadows, so accumulation is possible only where immersion fails, i.e. on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_{xx}=0\}.
\]
Finally, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
so \(\{S_{xx}=0\}=\{K_v=0\}\) on \(U\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Useful overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On the same overlap patch, set
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\mathcal G:=x'\sigma_v'+Y'\tau_u'.
\]
Then \(\mathcal G\) admits the exact factorization
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
In particular, \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch
contained in \(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice carried by \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet exclude the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
genuinely nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current
attack.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
shows that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact mixed
two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already reduced either to the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or to the lifted curvature locus \(K_v=0\). The
remaining unresolved work is to show that accumulation on \(S=0\) either falls
into the existing mixed low-order obstruction types or transfers into a
lower-core tangency mechanism, while accumulation on \(K_v=0\) is absorbed by
the existing lifted three-point branch machinery.
\end{remark}
```

## 6) Tiny cleanup edits if they still appear anywhere

If you still have any phrase of the form

```latex
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_x=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}
```

replace it by

```latex
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
```

And if you still have any mainline mixed-two-point discussion centered on the affine map
\[
\Phi(h)=\left(x-\frac{S}{S_x},\,Y-\frac{SY_x}{S_x}\right),
\]
downgrade it to a remark or remove it. The projective secant-shadow package is the cleaner and stronger final formulation. turn95file2turn95file3turn95file8

Those are the specific edit points I’d make after checking the updated draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 03:12:39)

I’m pushing directly on the remaining mixed two-point slice now: \(S=0\). The goal is to see whether that slice already forces entry into the existing mixed low-order obstruction regime or a lower-core tangency mechanism, rather than leaving a genuinely new 2-point branch.

_Thought for 7m 21s_

Yes. There is a real new push on the \(S=0\) slice.

Assume the **frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence** exists, so the exact mixed two-point branch reduces to repeated nearby values of the fixed map
\[
\Phi(h):=
\left(
\frac{W(v_5,\lambda)}{W(c,\lambda)},
\frac{W(u_5,\lambda)}{W(c,\lambda)}
\right),
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
On a good \(v_5\)-patch, writing
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
this is
\[
\Phi(h)=
\left(
x-S\frac{x_h}{S_h},
\;
Y-S\frac{Y_h}{S_h}
\right),
\]
where subscripts are \(h\)-derivatives.

Now take a point \(a\) on the septic-zero slice
\[
S(a)=0.
\]
If the zero is **simple**, so
\[
S_h(a)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\Phi(a)=(x(a),Y(a)),
\qquad
\Phi'(a)=0.
\]

The next derivatives are the useful ones. A direct calculation gives
\[
\Phi''(a)
=
\frac{1}{S_h(a)}
\bigl(
K_v(a),\,K_Y(a)
\bigr),
\]
where
\[
K_v:=x_hS_{hh}-S_hx_{hh},
\qquad
K_Y:=Y_hS_{hh}-S_hY_{hh}.
\]
So if
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0,
\]
then \(\Phi''(a)\neq 0\).

One more derivative gives
\[
\det\bigl(\Phi''(a),\Phi'''(a)\bigr)
=
\frac{2}{S_h(a)^2}\,W_h(K_v,K_Y)(a).
\]
Now convert to the local \(x\)-coordinate. Since
\[
K_v=(x_h)^3 S_{xx},
\qquad
K_Y=(x_h)^3\bigl(S_{xx}Y_x-S_xY_{xx}\bigr),
\]
one gets
\[
W_h(K_v,K_Y)
=
(x_h)^7\,W_x\!\bigl(S_{xx},\,S_{xx}Y_x-S_xY_{xx}\bigr).
\]
But
\[
W_x\!\bigl(S_{xx},\,S_{xx}Y_x-S_xY_{xx}\bigr)
=
S_x\bigl(Y_{xx}S_{xxx}-Y_{xxx}S_{xx}\bigr).
\]
So finally
\[
\boxed{
\det\bigl(\Phi''(a),\Phi'''(a)\bigr)
=
\frac{2(x_h(a))^7 S_x(a)}{S_h(a)^2}\,
\Omega_v(a),
\qquad
\Omega_v:=Y_{xx}S_{xxx}-Y_{xxx}S_{xx}.
}
\]

This is the key new reduction.

Now use a standard cusp-type injectivity fact: if an analytic map
\[
\Phi:(\mathbf R,a)\to \mathbf R^2
\]
satisfies
\[
\Phi'(a)=0,\qquad \Phi''(a)\neq 0,\qquad
\det\bigl(\Phi''(a),\Phi'''(a)\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
then \(\Phi\) is locally injective near \(a\). The reason is that the Taylor difference
\[
\Phi(a+t_1)-\Phi(a+t_2)
\]
factors by \(t_1-t_2\), and the remaining bracket has leading independent
\(\Phi''(a)\)- and \(\Phi'''(a)\)-components, so it cannot vanish for distinct sufficiently small \(t_1,t_2\).

But a close exact mixed two-point bad branch gives repeated nearby values
\[
\Phi(h_{1,n})=\Phi(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to a.
\]
Therefore local injectivity must fail.

So, on the **simple septic-zero slice** \(S(a)=0\), \(S_h(a)\neq 0\), we get:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if }K_v(a)\neq 0,\ \text{then a close exact mixed two-point bad branch forces }\Omega_v(a)=0.
}
\]

That is a real improvement.

So the \(S=0\) slice now splits as follows:

- If \(S(a)=0\) and \(S_h(a)\neq 0\) and \(K_v(a)\neq 0\), then any close mixed two-point branch forces the **rooted scalar**
  \[
  \Omega_v(a)=Y_{xx}(a)S_{xxx}(a)-Y_{xxx}(a)S_{xx}(a)=0.
  \]

- If \(K_v(a)=0\), that is already the lifted 3-point curvature/osculating locus, which is exactly where the current 3-point derivative-geometry package lives. turn101file15

- If \(S_h(a)=0\), then \(a\) is a higher-order septic zero, which is a separate exceptional subcase still to analyze.

So the remaining mixed two-point accumulation on \(S=0\) is no longer broad. Under frozen \(\lambda\)-shear, it is reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
S=0,\quad S_h\neq 0,\quad K_v\neq 0
\ \Longrightarrow\ 
\Omega_v=0,
}
\]
or else to the already-known \(K_v=0\) branch or the higher-order zero subcase.

That is the strongest clean push I can defend right now.

The next best move is to see whether this new \(\Omega_v=0\) condition is already absorbed by the existing mixed low-order obstruction list or rooted-tangency geometry, instead of being a genuinely new branch. The draft’s present structure is exactly consistent with that kind of handoff: the mixed low-order list is already explicit, and the 3-point branch is already organized around \(K_v=0\) and the osculating determinant. turn101file17

_Thought for 1m 32s_

Yes. There is a cleaner push.

Assume the **frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence** exists, so the mixed two-point branch gives repeated nearby values of the fixed map
\[
\Phi(x)=\left(x-\frac{S}{S_x},\;Y-\frac{S\,Y_x}{S_x}\right),
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
in the local \(x=v_5/c\) coordinate, at least away from higher-order zeros of \(S_x\). The earlier reduction already showed that a close mixed branch can only accumulate on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\]
with \(K_v\) the lifted \(v\)-patch curvature scalar. The live case to attack is therefore the **simple septic-zero slice**
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,\qquad K_v(a)\neq 0.
\]
This is exactly the remaining mixed two-point slice outside the already-mature \(K_v=0\) three-point geometry. turn103file2

At such a point \(a\), because \(S(a)=0\),
\[
\Phi(a)=(x(a),Y(a)),
\qquad
\Phi'(a)=0.
\]
Differentiating once more gives
\[
\Phi''(a)=\frac{1}{S_x(a)}\bigl(S_{xx}(a),\;S_{xx}(a)Y_x(a)-S_x(a)Y_{xx}(a)\bigr),
\]
so if \(K_v(a)\neq 0\), equivalently \(S_{xx}(a)\neq 0\), then \(\Phi''(a)\neq 0\).

Now differentiate a third time. A direct calculation yields
\[
\det\bigl(\Phi''(a),\Phi'''(a)\bigr)
=
\frac{2}{S_x(a)^2}\,\Omega_v(a),
\]
where
\[
\Omega_v(a):=Y_{xx}(a)S_{xxx}(a)-Y_{xxx}(a)S_{xx}(a).
\]

This is the key point. If
\[
\Omega_v(a)\neq 0,
\]
then \(\Phi''(a)\) and \(\Phi'''(a)\) are linearly independent, so the Taylor expansion
\[
\Phi(a+t_1)-\Phi(a+t_2)
\]
has a nondegenerate cusp-type leading part. That makes \(\Phi\) locally injective near \(a\), so it cannot have repeated nearby values
\[
\Phi(x_1)=\Phi(x_2),\qquad x_1\neq x_2,\qquad x_1,x_2\to a.
\]
Therefore a close exact mixed two-point bad branch accumulating at a **simple** septic zero with \(K_v(a)\neq 0\) must satisfy
\[
\boxed{\Omega_v(a)=0.}
\]

That already sharpens the remaining exceptional set from “\(S=0\)” to
\[
\boxed{
S=0,\quad S_x\neq 0,\quad K_v\neq 0
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\Omega_v=0.
}
\]

There is one more goodie here. Since \(K_v\neq 0\) means \(S_{xx}\neq 0\), we can rewrite
\[
\Omega_v
=
Y_{xx}S_{xxx}-Y_{xxx}S_{xx}
=
-\,S_{xx}^2\left(\frac{Y_{xx}}{S_{xx}}\right)_x.
\]
So on the simple septic-zero slice away from \(K_v=0\),
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_v=0
\iff
\left(\frac{Y_{xx}}{S_{xx}}\right)_x=0.
}
\]

That is a very strong alignment with the newer derivative geometry: the remaining mixed two-point accumulation on \(S=0\) is forced onto the zero set of the **same scalar derivative invariant**
\[
\mathcal R:=\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)_x
\]
that the newer nonmixed four-point analysis treats as the affine-planarity / derivative-geometry scalar. So, away from \(K_v=0\), the mixed two-point branch does not create a completely new geometric obstruction; it collapses onto the \(\mathcal R=0\) geometry. 

So the remaining mixed two-point picture is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{close mixed 2-point accumulation can only occur on }
K_v=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\bigl(S=0,\ \mathcal R=0\bigr)
\quad\text{or at a higher-order septic zero }S_x=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest push I can defend right now.

The next best move is to attack the higher-order septic-zero subcase
\[
S=0,\qquad S_x=0,
\]
because the simple-zero case has now been funneled into either the existing \(K_v=0\) three-point branch or the same \(\mathcal R=0\) derivative scalar already governing the nonmixed four-point geometry. turn103file17

_Thought for 3m 50s_

Yes. This push works, and it is stronger than the last one.

Under the **frozen \(\lambda\)-shear** reduction, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch gives fixed constants \((\eta,\xi,\gamma)\) and exact repeated nearby values of the fixed map
\[
\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}(h)
:=
\left(
\frac{B(h)}{A(h)},
\frac{F(h)}{A(h)}
\right),
\]
where
\[
A=c-\eta\lambda,\qquad
B=v_5-\xi\lambda,\qquad

\]
On a good \(v_5\)-patch, writing
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad

\[
\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}(h)
=
\left(
\frac{x-\xi S}{1-\eta S},
\frac{Y-\gamma S}{1-\eta S}
\right).
\]

That exact fixed-shear map is the right object for the remaining \(S=0\) analysis.

Now take a point \(a\) on the septic-zero slice
\[
S(a)=0.
\]
Because \(c(a)\neq 0\) on the good overlap patch, we have
\[

\]
so \(\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}\) is honest and analytic near \(a\).

Differentiate the first component:
\[
\mathcal R_1(h)=\frac{x-\xi S}{1-\eta S}.
\]
At a septic zero,
\[
\mathcal R_1'(a)
=
x'(a)+(\eta x(a)-\xi)\,S'(a).

## Higher-order septic zeros are impossible

\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S'(a)=0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_1'(a)=x'(a).
}
\]
On a good patch,
\[
x'(a)=\frac{M(a)}{c(a)^2}\neq 0.
\]
So \(\mathcal R_1\) is locally injective near \(a\), hence the pair map
\[
\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}
\]
is locally injective near \(a\) as well.

But a close exact mixed two-point bad branch gives repeated nearby values
\[
\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}(h_{1,n})
=
\mathcal R_{\eta,\xi,\gamma}(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to a,
\]
which is impossible under local injectivity.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A close exact mixed two-point bad branch cannot accumulate at a higher-order septic zero }S=0,\ S'=0.
}
\]

That is a real new theorem-level reduction.

## What remains on the \(S=0\) slice

So the only possible \(S=0\) accumulation is at a **simple septic zero**
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S'(a)\neq 0.
\]

And from the previous push, at such a simple septic zero, if also

\]
then the branch forces
\[

\]
equivalently
\[

\[
\boxed{
\text{accumulation can occur only on }K_v=0
\quad\text{or on}\quad
\bigl(S=0,\ S'\neq 0,\ \Omega_v=0\bigr).
}
\]

Since
\[

=

=
-\,S_{xx}^2\left(\frac{Y_{xx}}{S_{xx}}\right)_x,

this is the same as saying:

\[
\boxed{

\quad\text{or on}\quad
\bigl(S=0,\ S'\neq 0,\ \mathcal R=0\bigr),
}
\]
with
\[
\mathcal R:=\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)_x.
\]

That is much cleaner.

It means the higher-order septic-zero subcase is gone entirely, and the simple-zero subcase collapses onto the same derivative scalar \(\mathcal R\) that already governs the nonmixed four-point derivative geometry. Meanwhile \(K_v=0\) is already the lifted curvature/osculating locus underlying the three-point branch. So the mixed two-point branch is no longer creating a broad new exceptional set; it is being funneled into two already-recognizable derivative-geometric loci. This is exactly the kind of source-coupled sharpening the current draft structure was asking for. turn104file17turn104file15

_Thought for 3m 58s_

Yes. There is a real push, and it changes the interpretation of the remaining slice.

At this point the **simple septic-zero slice**
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,\qquad K_v(a)\neq 0
\]
does **not** feed into the existing mixed low-order obstruction list. It feeds into the **nonmixed derivative-geometry scalar** instead.

Here is the clean argument.

Under the frozen \(\lambda\)-shear reduction, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch gives repeated nearby values of a fixed map on the \(v_5\)-patch, and the previous step already forced
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,\qquad K_v(a)\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Omega_v(a)=0,
\]
equivalently
\[
\mathcal R(a):=\left(\frac{Y_{xx}}{S_{xx}}\right)_x(a)=0.
\]

Now recall what the draft’s mixed low-order package is actually organized by: the pair
\[
(J_\lambda,\ J_{u_5}),
\]
or equivalently the Wronskian-order types
\[
(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,4).
\]
In particular, every one of those low-order obstruction types requires that \(J_\lambda\) vanish to positive order. That is exactly how the draft packages the mixed local obstruction list. turn106file1

But on the good \(v_5\)-patch,
\[
J_\lambda \asymp S_{xx},
\qquad
K_v \asymp S_{xx},
\]
so
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0 \quad\Longrightarrow\quad J_\lambda(a)\neq 0.
\]
Therefore at a simple septic zero with \(K_v(a)\neq 0\), none of the mixed low-order obstruction types can occur.

So the remaining slice is **not**
\[
\text{“simple }S=0\text{ plus one of }(1,2),(1,4),(2,4)\text{.”}
\]

Instead it is:

\[
\boxed{
S(a)=0,\quad S_x(a)\neq 0,\quad K_v(a)\neq 0
\ \Longrightarrow\ 
\mathcal R(a)=0,
\text{ with }J_\lambda(a)\neq 0.
}
\]

That is the useful new conclusion.

So the mixed two-point branch has now split cleanly into two derivative-geometric lanes:

- \(K_v=0\), which is already the lifted 3-point curvature/osculating branch; the draft’s 3-point package is explicitly built around shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuits forcing \(K_v=0\), plus local classification and global continuation/nonrecurrence there. 

- \(S=0\) with \(K_v\neq 0\), which cannot be mixed low-order and instead forces
  \[
  \mathcal R=0,
  \qquad
  \mathcal R=\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)_x.
  \]
  But \(\mathcal R\) is already the nonmixed four-point derivative scalar: interval-persistent nonmixed four-point degeneracy is controlled by \(\mathcal R=0\), not by raw coplanarity alone. turn105file17

So the strongest honest reduction is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A close mixed two-point branch can only accumulate either on }K_v=0
\text{ or on the codimension-two derivative-geometric set }
\{S=0,\ \mathcal R=0,\ K_v\neq 0\}.
}
\]

And that codimension-two set is **not** part of the mixed low-order list.

That is important, because it tells us the next attack should **not** be “push harder on the mixed low-order obstruction types.” The simple septic-zero remainder has already escaped that package.

The right next move is instead:

- treat \(K_v=0\) as a handoff to the lifted 3-point branch;
- treat
  \[
  S=0,\ \mathcal R=0,\ K_v\neq 0
  \]
  as a handoff to the nonmixed derivative-geometry / first-loss rigidification side, since \(\mathcal R\) is exactly that branch’s scalar. turn105file5turn106file13

So this push does **not** close the two-point branch, but it does sharpen it substantially:

the only remaining non-\(K_v\) accumulation is not generic mixed local obstruction at all — it is a codimension-two derivative-geometric slice governed by the same \(\mathcal R\)-scalar that already appears on the nonmixed four-point side.

_Thought for 4m 59s_

I pushed it one more step, and the cleanest new reduction is this:

On the remaining **simple septic-zero slice**
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
use \(s:=S\) itself as the local parameter. Then the projective secant-shadow construction becomes an exact planar **tangent-shadow** map. If
\[
C(s):=(x(s),Y(s)),
\]
where \(x=v_5/c\) and \(Y=u_5/c\), then the shadow point is
\[
P(s)=C(s)-s\,C'(s).
\]
So the leftover mixed two-point problem is no longer a vague source-level interaction problem there; it is exactly a nearby double-value problem for the planar tangent-shadow map \(P\). This is the right local normal form for the remaining \(S=0\) branch. It fits the draft’s current derivative-geometric picture: \(K_v=0\) is already the lifted 3-point curvature/osculating locus, while \(\mathcal R=\frac{d}{dx}\!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\) is already the nonmixed four-point derivative scalar. turn107file18turn107file9

In this \(s\)-coordinate,
\[
P'(s)=-s\,C''(s),
\]
so
\[
P'(0)=0,\qquad P''(0)=-C''(0),\qquad P'''(0)=-2C'''(0).
\]
Hence the first obstruction to nearby double values is the cusp determinant
\[
\det(P''(0),P'''(0))=2\det(C''(0),C'''(0)).
\]
Translated back to the \(x\)-coordinate, this is exactly the scalar we already found:
\[
\det(C'',C''')\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\Omega_v\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathcal R\neq 0
\]
on the simple septic-zero slice with \(K_v\neq 0\). So the earlier reduction becomes conceptually cleaner: away from \(K_v=0\), a close mixed two-point branch on \(S=0\) can survive only at a **higher tangent-shadow singularity** of \(P\), not at an ordinary cusp. turn107file18turn107file9

This means the mixed two-point branch is now funneled into exactly two derivative-geometric lanes:

\[
K_v=0,
\]
which is already the mature lifted 3-point lane, or
\[
S=0,\quad \det(C'',C''')=0,
\]
equivalently
\[
S=0,\quad \mathcal R=0,\quad K_v\neq 0,
\]
which is a **higher tangent-shadow singularity** lane. The higher-order septic-zero subcase \(S=0,\ S_x=0\) is already gone from the picture. So the next real theorem is no longer about generic mixed low-order obstructions; it is a local singularity-classification theorem for the tangent-shadow map \(P(s)=C(s)-sC'(s)\) on the simple septic-zero slice. turn107file18turn107file3

My honest status is: this still does not close the branch, but it is a real reduction. The remaining non-\(K_v\) mixed two-point geometry is now a standard-looking planar tangent-shadow singularity problem, and that is much narrower than the earlier source-level formulations.

_Thought for 2m 3s_

Yes. I checked the updated TeX itself, and there **are** meaningful new differential-geometry additions on the 2-point side.

The main new block is the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow package around lines **19790–20245**. The most important additions are:

- **`prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction`** at about line **19790**. This is the core new 2-point derivative-geometry proposition. It reformulates a close exact mixed 2-point bad branch as a moving \(\lambda\)-shear transport problem on an overlap patch and then shows that the associated **projective secant shadow**
  \[
  \mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
  \]
  converges to a **projective tangent shadow**
  \[
  \mathbf\Pi(a)=[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x].
  \]
  The payoff is the reduction
  \[
  \text{mixed 2-point accumulation} \subset \{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
  \]
  which is a real improvement over the older broader exceptional set.

- The proof explicitly computes
  \[
  \mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
  =
  S(x)\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}\bigr),
  \]
  so the tangent-shadow map is projectively immersive away from
  \[
  S=0,\qquad S_{xx}=0.
  \]
  Using \(K_v=(x')^3S_{xx}\), the paper correctly collapses this to
  \[
  \{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
  \]

- **`rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point`** just below it records the overlap scalar
  \[
  \mathcal G
  =
  -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
  \qquad
  \lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
  \]
  equivalently
  \[
  \mathcal G
  =
  \frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
  \left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
  \]
  That is a genuinely useful “goodie”: it is the first clean \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the mixed 2-point attack.

- **`prop:exact fixed-shear overlap branches off \(K_v=0\) force a fold at \(S=0\)`** around line **20059** is also genuinely new and important. This is the next derivative-geometric sharpening of the \(S=0\) slice, beyond the projective-shadow reduction.

- The later summary remarks now consistently refer to the mixed 2-point route as a **conditional \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow lane** rather than as a closed theorem, which is the right status. In particular, the updated summaries around the “what remains,” “live attack routes,” and “current state” remarks now correctly present the two-point side as splitting into:
  1. finite-order source-level merger,
  2. quotient-diagonal exact exclusion,
  3. mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow control on \(\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\).

So, in substance, the new 2-point differential geometry in the updated draft is:

\[
\text{mixed 2-point branch}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{\(\lambda\)-shear transport}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{projective secant-shadow geometry}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]

That is a real structural advance, and it is now aligned with the mature 3-point \(K_v\)-geometry and the nonmixed \(\mathcal R\)-geometry rather than sitting as an isolated ad hoc argument. The conversation transcript is also consistent with that interpretation. turn108file15turn108file17

My only caution is that this is still a **reduction**, not a closure. The new material cleanly narrows the remaining mixed 2-point geometry, but it does not yet prove that accumulation on the remaining loci is impossible. The next math push should still be exactly what we were doing: analyze the \(S=0\) slice and hand off the \(K_v=0\) slice into the lifted 3-point machinery.

Here is the next clean push.

On the remaining **simple septic-zero slice**
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
use
\[
s:=S
\]
as the local parameter, and write
\[
C(s):=(x(s),Y(s)).
\]
Then the mixed two-point tangent-shadow map is
\[
P(s):=C(s)-s\,C'(s).
\]
A close mixed two-point branch on this slice gives nearby double values of \(P\). From the previous push, if also
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0,
\]
then \(C''(0)\neq 0\), and nearby double values already forced
\[
\det(C''(0),C'''(0))=0,
\]
which is the same as
\[
\mathcal R(a)=0.
\]

Now expand:
\[
C(s)=C_0+C_1 s+\frac12 C_2 s^2+\frac16 C_3 s^3+\frac1{24} C_4 s^4+O(s^5),
\]
so
\[
P(s)=P_0-\frac12 C_2 s^2-\frac13 C_3 s^3-\frac18 C_4 s^4+O(s^5).
\]

Assume we are on the remaining slice
\[
\det(C_2,C_3)=0
\]
but still
\[
\det(C_2,C_4)\neq 0.
\]
Choose affine coordinates so that
\[
C_2=(1,0),\qquad C_3=(\mu,0),\qquad C_4=(a,b),
\qquad b\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
P_1(s)=u_0-\frac12 s^2-\frac{\mu}{3}s^3-\frac{a}{8}s^4+O(s^5),
\]
\[
P_2(s)=v_0-\frac{b}{8}s^4+O(s^5).
\]

If \(P(s_1)=P(s_2)\) for distinct small \(s_1,s_2\), then equality of the second coordinate forces
\[
s_2=-s_1+o(s_1),
\]
since the first nonzero term of \(P_2\) is even quartic with nonzero coefficient \(b\). Plugging that into the first coordinate gives
\[
P_1(s_1)-P_1(s_2)
=
-\frac{2\mu}{3}s_1^3+o(s_1^3).
\]
So double values are impossible unless
\[
\mu=0.
\]

In invariant form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }S=0,\ S_x\neq 0,\ K_v\neq 0,\ \mathcal R=0,\ \det(C'',C'''')\neq 0,
\text{ then a close mixed 2-point branch forces }C'''=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, on the simple septic-zero slice, a close mixed two-point branch must satisfy **one more degeneracy beyond** \(\mathcal R=0\), namely

\[
\boxed{
C'''(0)=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Theta_v(a):=\det(C''(0),C''''(0))=0.
}
\]

So the remaining non-\(K_v\) lane is now narrower than before:

\[
\boxed{
S=0,\ S_x\neq 0,\ K_v\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal R=0
\Longrightarrow
\bigl(C'''=0\bigr)\ \text{or}\ \bigl(\Theta_v=0\bigr).
}
\]

That is a real extra codimension hit.

Conceptually, this is good news. The worker note said the mixed side would need genuine \(Y\)-\(S\) coupling and likely a repeated-node/tangency style rigidification, not just \((x,S)\)-only planar geometry. This new condition is exactly that: it lives in the planar **\(C=(x,Y)\)** tangent-shadow geometry, not in \((x,S)\)-only geometry, and it says the remaining simple septic-zero branch is already forced into a **higher tangent-shadow singularity** beyond the cusp-level \(\mathcal R=0\) condition. turn112file14

So the remaining mixed 2-point picture is now:

- \(K_v=0\), which is the lifted 3-point curvature/osculating lane already present in the draft. 
- or
  \[
  S=0,\quad S_x\neq 0,\quad K_v\neq 0,\quad \mathcal R=0,
  \]
  and then in fact one more degeneracy:
  \[
  C'''=0 \quad\text{or}\quad \Theta_v=0.
  \]

\[

\quad\text{or}\quad

\]
is already equivalent to, or absorbed by, one of the derivative-geometry packages elsewhere in the draft.

_Thought for 2m 30s_

Yes. The worker note lets the next push land more cleanly.

The strong affine freeze lemma is false, but the exact projective secant-shadow reduction is enough to keep pushing. In the **conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane** off \(K_v=0\), the remaining local problem can be put into a standard **fold normal form**, and then the mixed two-point branch becomes an **odd-zero problem** with leading coefficient proportional to the same scalar \(\mathcal R\) already governing the nonmixed derivative geometry. turn108file15turn108file17

Here is the clean reduction.

Work at an accumulation point \(a\) on a good overlap patch, in the conditional exact fixed-shear lane, and assume
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0.
\]
From the worker note and the current draft package, the fixed-shear map is
\[
\Phi(x)=\left(\frac{x-\xi_*S}{1-\eta_*S},\frac{Y-\gamma_*S}{1-\eta_*S}\right),
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
and repeated nearby values
\[
\Phi(x_{1,n})=\Phi(x_{2,n}),\qquad x_{1,n}\neq x_{2,n},\qquad x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a
\]
force
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
while \(K_v(a)\neq 0\) implies
\[
S_{xx}(a)\neq 0.
\]
If we set
\[
U(x):=\Phi_1(x)-\Phi_1(a),\qquad V(x):=\Phi_2(x)-\Phi_2(a),
\]
then
\[
U(a)=U_x(a)=0,\qquad U_{xx}(a)\neq 0,
\]
so \(U\) has a fold at \(a\). This is exactly the fold-type regime the worker note identified off \(K_v=0\). 

Now apply the one-dimensional analytic Morse lemma: there is a local real-analytic coordinate \(t\) with \(t(a)=0\) such that
\[
U=t^2.
\]
Equivalently, after reparametrizing the curve by \(t\),
\[
\widetilde V(t):=V(x(t))
\]
is an analytic scalar function, and repeated nearby values of \(\Phi\) are equivalent to
\[
\widetilde V(t)=\widetilde V(-t).
\]
So the whole remaining fixed-shear mixed two-point problem has become an **odd-part vanishing problem**
\[
\widetilde V_{\mathrm{odd}}(t):=\frac{\widetilde V(t)-\widetilde V(-t)}{2}=0.
\]

That is already a big conceptual simplification.

Now compute the leading odd coefficient. Write derivatives at \(a\). A standard normal-form expansion gives
\[
\widetilde V_{\mathrm{odd}}(t)
=
\kappa_3\,t^3+O(t^5),
\]
with
\[
\kappa_3
\propto
U_{xx}(a)V_{xxx}(a)-U_{xxx}(a)V_{xx}(a).
\]
In other words, the cubic odd coefficient is the determinant of the \(2\)-jets and \(3\)-jets of \((U,V)\).

But in the present fixed-shear overlap lane, that determinant is exactly the same cusp/tangent-shadow scalar we already isolated before, namely
\[
\Omega_v(a)=Y_{xx}(a)S_{xxx}(a)-Y_{xxx}(a)S_{xx}(a).
\]
And since \(K_v(a)\neq 0\) means \(S_{xx}(a)\neq 0\),
\[
\Omega_v
=
-\,S_{xx}^2\left(\frac{Y_{xx}}{S_{xx}}\right)_x
=
-\,S_{xx}^2\,\mathcal R.
\]
So the leading odd coefficient satisfies
\[
\kappa_3\propto \Omega_v(a)\propto \mathcal R(a).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In the exact fixed-shear overlap lane off }K_v=0,\ 
\text{the remaining mixed two-point branch is an odd-zero problem whose leading coefficient is }\mathcal R.
}
\]

That is the strongest useful push from the worker note.

It means the remaining off-\(K_v\) fixed-shear branch is no longer some separate mixed vector-valued obstruction. After fold normalization, it has the **same shape** as the nonmixed odd-zero route: a one-variable odd scalar whose first nontrivial coefficient is controlled by \(\mathcal R\). turn108file15turn108file17

What this does **not** yet prove is full absorption into the existing nonmixed package. To prove that rigorously, one still needs to identify the higher odd coefficients of \(\widetilde V_{\mathrm{odd}}(t)\) with the same scalar package already used on the nonmixed side, or at least prove that their sign/parity/first-loss behavior is governed by the same \(\mathcal R\)-theory. The worker note was exactly right about this missing step. 

So the current picture is now very sharp:

- The automatic compactness theorem is **projective compactness**, not affine freezing. 
- The exact projective secant-shadow theorem reduces the mixed two-point branch to
  \[
  \{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
  \]
- On the conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane off \(K_v=0\), the branch is forced into a **fold normal form**.
- In that fold normal form, the remaining branch is an **odd-zero problem with leading coefficient \(\mathcal R\)**.

So the next best attack is now very specific: show that this fold-normalized odd scalar is actually governed by the existing nonmixed odd-zero \(\mathcal R\)-package, not by a genuinely new mixed branch.

_Thought for 1m 2s_

Yes. In the **conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane**, there is a stronger conclusion than just “the leading odd coefficient is proportional to \(\mathcal R\).”

Assume we are in the worker’s fixed-shear regime off \(K_v=0\): there is a fixed triple \((\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*)\) and a local map
\[
\Phi(x)=\left(\frac{x-\xi_*S}{1-\eta_*S},\frac{Y-\gamma_*S}{1-\eta_*S}\right),
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
with repeated nearby values
\[
\Phi(x_{1,n})=\Phi(x_{2,n}),\qquad x_{1,n}\neq x_{2,n},\qquad x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a,
\]
and \(K_v(a)\neq 0\). The note already tells us that this forces
\[
S(a)=0,\qquad S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
and that the first coordinate is in a fold regime:
\[
U(x):=\Phi_1(x)-\Phi_1(a),\qquad U(a)=U_x(a)=0,\qquad U_{xx}(a)\neq 0.
\]
That part is already solid. turn108file17

Now apply the analytic Morse lemma in one variable. There is a local analytic coordinate \(t\) with \(t(a)=0\) such that
\[
U=t^2.
\]
Write
\[
V(t):=\Phi_2(x(t)).
\]
Then repeated nearby values of \(\Phi\) become repeated nearby values of
\[
(t^2,V(t)).
\]
Since \(t^2\) is the first coordinate, any two nearby distinct points with the same first coordinate are \(t\) and \(-t\). Therefore the branch gives a sequence \(t_n\to 0\), \(t_n\neq 0\), such that
\[
V(t_n)=V(-t_n).
\]

But then the odd part
\[
V_{\mathrm{odd}}(t):=\frac{V(t)-V(-t)}{2}
\]
is an analytic odd function with infinitely many zeros accumulating at \(0\). Hence
\[
\boxed{V_{\mathrm{odd}}\equiv 0.}
\]

So in the exact fixed-shear overlap lane off \(K_v=0\), the map is not merely “cusp-like with leading odd coefficient proportional to \(\mathcal R\).” It actually factors **exactly** through the square:
\[
\boxed{
\Phi(x(t))=\bigl(t^2,\ \mathcal V(t^2)\bigr)
}
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal V\). Equivalently, there is a local analytic involution
\[
\iota:t\mapsto -t
\]
such that
\[
\Phi\circ \iota=\Phi.
\]

That is a much stronger structural statement.

So the consequences are:

1. Every odd coefficient in the fold-normalized second coordinate vanishes, not just the first one.  
   In particular, the cubic odd coefficient vanishes, which recovers
   \[
   \mathcal R(a)=0
   \]
   as a necessary condition, but now as just the **first** member of an infinite tower of odd-jet constraints. turn108file15turn108file17

2. The remaining off-\(K_v\) fixed-shear branch is a genuine **local reflection-symmetry branch**, not just a generic repeated-value branch.

3. This means the next attack is no longer “compute the next odd coefficient.” The right next question is whether the draft’s existing nonmixed odd-zero / first-loss machinery can rule out this exact local evenization, or show it transfers into an already-known branch. The worker note was pointing exactly in that direction: the missing step is not the leading coefficient, but identifying the whole off-\(K_v\) fixed-shear lane with the existing nonmixed \(\mathcal R\)-package. 

So the current sharp picture is:

- The **projective** mixed two-point reduction is unconditional and lands on
  \[
  \{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
  \]
- In the **conditional exact fixed-shear** overlap lane with \(K_v\neq 0\), the branch is forced into an exact local factorization
  \[
  \Phi(x(t))=(t^2,\mathcal V(t^2)).
  \]
- Thus the only clearly genuinely mixed locus left is still
  \[
  K_v=0,
  \]
  while the off-\(K_v\) fixed-shear lane has become a local reflection-symmetry problem rather than a free mixed obstruction. turn108file17

The next push I’d make is: try to show that this exact local evenization of \(\Phi\) is incompatible with the existing nonmixed odd-zero / first-loss rigidification package unless it is already absorbed by it.
